# 004-001  BRAND FOUNDATION          SME: Morgan (Strategic Brand Architect)
#   RCP-004-001-001  Brand Context Initializer    [Beginner]      Gathers business context, activates the cookbook persona, emits the shared context block all later recipes read.
#   RCP-004-001-002  Target Audience Analyzer     [Intermediate]  Defines audience segments and sharpening anti-personas.
#   RCP-004-001-003  Pain Point Identifier        [Intermediate]  Scores and prioritizes customer pain points by frequency and severity.
#   RCP-004-001-004  Value Proposition Crafter    [Intermediate]  Builds the unique value proposition across multiple frameworks and lengths.
#   RCP-004-001-005  Competitive Edge Definer     [Advanced]      Maps differentiation, defensibility, and positioning against the competitive set.
#   RCP-004-001-006  Elevator Pitch Builder       [Intermediate]  Produces a multi-context pitch portfolio (15 / 30 / 60 / 120-second).
#   RCP-004-001-007  Brand Profile Synthesizer    [Advanced]      Synthesizes the full brand profile and the messaging pillars the Campaign section consumes.

# 004-002  CAMPAIGN PLANNING         SME: Maggie (Strategic Campaign Architect)
#   RCP-004-002-001  Campaign Architecture Designer [Intermediate] Section entry point — activates Maggie; defines campaign phase structure and escalation model.
#   RCP-004-002-002  Messaging Matrix Builder       [Advanced]     Maps messaging pillars to phases, personas, and platforms; emits the message library.
#   RCP-004-002-003  Content Pillar Planner         [Advanced]     Defines content categories and phase-by-phase content ratios.
#   RCP-004-002-004  Channel Strategy Developer     [Advanced]     Prioritizes platforms (Tier 1-4) and builds per-channel playbooks.
#   RCP-004-002-005  Campaign Timeline Architect    [Advanced]     Lays out the week-by-week schedule with intensity mapping and milestones.

# 004-003  CONTENT EXECUTION         SME: Quinn (Multi-Channel Content Strategist)
#   RCP-004-003-001  Content Calendar Generator   [Advanced]      Section entry point — activates Quinn; builds the slot-by-slot publishing calendar.
#   RCP-004-003-002  Social Post Creator          [Intermediate]  Composes platform-native posts from the messaging matrix's message library.
#   RCP-004-003-003  Blog Content Planner         [Intermediate]  Plans blog briefs with an SEO framework and a cross-channel amplification plan.
#   RCP-004-003-004  Content Performance Analyzer [Intermediate]  Analyzes content metrics and closes the optimization loop back to planning.

# ===== BEGIN RECIPES =====
# =========================================================
# WPRM CONTENT - RCP-004-001-001-BRAND-CONTEXT-INIT
# Created: December 25, 2025
# Revised: June 23, 2026 (v3.00a - format upgrade to current
#          CRAFTFramework.ai recipe form)
#          Revised June 26, 2026 (P062-SP11): made tier-less
#          (SP09) and flavor-less (SP10)
# Creator: Auguste (Content Creator)
# Upgraded by: P062-Cat (SP08 Branding & Identity cookbook)
# Status: Ready for Validation
# =========================================================


# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-001-001-BRAND-CONTEXT-INIT

Description: Gathers essential business context to inform
all brand development work. Creates foundational
understanding of business stage, goals, constraints, and
existing assets. Establishes the BRAND_PERSONA object and
activates the default persona ({PERSONA_NAME}) to guide
the brand development process. Produces reusable context
block for subsequent recipes.


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 001

Recipe ID Numbers: 001

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Foundation

Recipe Tags:
    brand-strategy, context-gathering, initialization,
    persona-activation, business-context, brand-development,
    discovery, strategic-planning, persona-configuration

Recipe Recommended Personas: Morgan (Strategic Brand
    Architect)

Recipe Difficulty: Beginner


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 1: Persona Configuration and Activation

    This recipe establishes the BRAND_PERSONA object that
    all Brand ID recipes reference. The default persona is
    Morgan (Strategic Brand Architect) - the persona
    bundled with this cookbook. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default. The persona
    object is stored in PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence
    across recipes. After configuration, the persona
    activates and guides the user through comprehensive
    brand discovery using structured frameworks and priority
    matrices.


STEP 2: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories including platform
    capabilities, competitive intelligence gathering, and
    proprietary business information. If potential conflict
    detected, note that brand context may involve sensitive
    business information and keep it confidential.


STEP 3: Initial Context Gathering

    Collect the core required parameters: business name,
    business age, and industry sector. If current stage is
    not provided, infer it from business age:
        - pre-launch suggests concept or MVP
        - 0-3 months suggests beta or launched
        - 3-12 months suggests launched
        - 1+ years suggests growth
    Confirm the inference with the user. Review team size
    and existing brand assets if provided. Ask clarifying
    questions for any missing required information.


STEP 4: Goals and Constraints Assessment

    Gather immediate goals for the next 1-3 months. Parse
    goals for urgency indicators, identify timeline
    pressure, and assess complexity. Categorize the
    priority as:
        - foundation-building
        - market-entry
        - growth-scaling
    Collect known constraints including time, budget, and
    resource limitations. For each constraint, identify
    strategic adaptations and workarounds.


STEP 5: Adaptive Follow-Up Questions

    Based on business age and current stage, ask 2-3
    targeted questions:
        - For concept/MVP: ask about value proposition
          validation and target launch date
        - For beta: ask about user targets and primary
          beta goals
        - For launched: ask about current brand
          performance and refresh needs
        - For growth: ask about growth metrics and brand
          evolution needs


STEP 6: Context Validation

    Review all gathered information for:
        - Logical consistency (stage matches age/goals)
        - Completeness (all critical info captured)
        - Clarity (no ambiguous statements)
        - Strategic alignment (goals match constraints)
    If inconsistencies detected, challenge constructively
    and ask for clarification. Provide a confidence
    assessment with percentage for context completeness.


STEP 7: Generate Session Context Block

    Generate structured context block containing:
        - Business identity (name, industry, age, stage)
        - Team and resources (team size, existing assets)
        - Goals and constraints (immediate goals, known
          constraints)
        - Strategic context (primary focus, key
          priorities, timeline pressure, confidence level)
        - Active persona ({PERSONA_NAME})
    This block will be used as the starting point for all
    subsequent brand recipes.


STEP 8: Brand Development Roadmap

    Create prioritized recipe roadmap based on the gathered
    context. Standard sequence is:
        1. Target Audience Analyzer
        2. Pain Point Identifier
        3. Value Prop Crafter
        4. Competitive Edge Definer
        5. Elevator Pitch Builder
        6. Brand Profile Synthesizer
    Adjust sequence based on context (pre-launch focuses
    on foundation, fundraising focuses on pitch,
    substantial assets start with competitive edge).
    Present priority matrix with rationale.


STEP 9: Quick Reference Card and Readiness Assessment

    Generate concise one-page reference card with stage,
    goal, team, focus area, active persona, and next steps.
    Provide readiness diagnostic with three categories:
        - Ready to address now (with confidence percentage)
        - Needs more information (with specific gaps)
        - Can be deferred (with rationale)
    List 2-3 priority actions for the next 48 hours.


STEP 10: Initialization Complete

    Provide summary of deliverables:
        - Session Context Block
        - Brand Development Roadmap
        - Quick Reference Card
        - Readiness Assessment
        - {PERSONA_NAME} activated as guide
    Confirm what has been established including context,
    strategy, framework, and confidence level. Provide
    final strategic guidance and ask if user is ready to
    proceed with the next recipe or wants to refine any
    aspects of the foundation first.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: What if I do not have all the required information?

A: The recipe is designed to handle incomplete information.
   It will ask clarifying questions for missing required
   fields and can proceed with reasonable defaults or
   inferences for optional fields. The context validation
   step will flag any critical gaps.

Q: Can I skip this recipe and go directly to other brand
   recipes?

A: While possible, it is not recommended. This recipe
   creates the context block that all subsequent recipes
   reference. Without it, other recipes will ask many of
   the same questions, reducing efficiency. Consider this
   recipe as creating your brand configuration file.

Q: How long does this recipe typically take?

A: For a straightforward business with clear goals, expect
   15-25 minutes of interactive conversation. Complex
   situations with multiple stakeholders or unclear
   direction may take longer. The recipe adapts to your
   pace and complexity.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Morgan as the default brand
   strategist. Morgan assumes brand literacy and works
   peer-to-peer, moving efficiently from context to
   recommendations. To override it, attach your own custom
   persona file; if you prefer step-by-step educational
   guidance, attach a more explanatory custom persona of
   your own.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe initializes the brand development workflow by
establishing the BRAND_PERSONA object, gathering essential
business context, and activating the selected persona. The
AI should execute the steps in sequence, adapting the
depth of questioning based on user responses.

Key processing logic:
    - Step 1 defines BRAND_PERSONA object and activates
      the persona (default Morgan; custom attach allowed)
    - Step 3 requires inference if current_stage is not
      provided
    - Step 5 branches based on the determined business
      stage
    - Step 6 validates consistency across all gathered
      data
    - Step 7 generates the context block output including
      active persona reference
    - Step 8 adjusts recipe sequence based on context

The persona activation in Step 1 sets the AI communication
style to the (peer-level, efficient execution)
Morgan persona bundled with this cookbook. Users may attach
a custom persona to override it.

The recipe produces four key outputs:
    - Context block (for use in all subsequent recipes)
    - Development roadmap (prioritized sequence)
    - Quick reference card (one-page summary)
    - Readiness assessment (diagnostic with next steps)

Parameter handling:
    - business_name, business_age, industry_sector are
      required
    - current_stage can be inferred from business_age
    - Optional parameters have sensible defaults or are
      gathered through interactive questioning


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Establishes the BRAND_PERSONA object and gathers essential
business context. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} to guide brand
development. Creates a reusable context block that informs
all subsequent brand recipes. The starting point for any
brand development workflow.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe when starting any brand development
project, whether for a new business, rebrand, or brand
refresh. It should be the first recipe executed in the
Brand Identity Cookbook workflow. The context block and
persona it establishes are required by all subsequent
brand recipes:
    - Target Audience Analyzer
    - Pain Point Identifier
    - Value Prop Crafter
    - Competitive Edge Definer
    - Elevator Pitch Builder
    - Brand Profile Synthesizer

Also use this recipe when resuming brand work after a
significant gap, when business circumstances have changed
substantially, or when working with a new AI session that
lacks the previous context.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: Fine Dining Restaurant (Pre-Launch)

    Parameters:
        - business_name: Terra and Olive
        - business_age: pre-launch
        - industry_sector: Fine Dining / Hospitality
        - current_stage: concept
        - team_size: 2-5
        - existing_brand_assets: Restaurant name, Location
          secured, Menu concept
        - immediate_goals: Open in 3 months, build local
          reputation before launch
        - known_constraints: Limited marketing budget,
          Competitive fine dining market

    Output: Context block emphasizing foundation-building,
    roadmap prioritizing Target Audience, Pain Point
    Identifier (understanding diner frustrations), and
    Value Prop Crafter. Assessment flags need to define
    unique positioning in competitive restaurant market.
    {PERSONA_NAME} activated to guide the work.

    Strategic Analysis: Pre-launch with moderate timeline.
    Foundation and positioning critical for restaurant
    success. Confidence 85% this approach will establish
    strong brand identity before opening.


Example 2: Environmental Consulting (Beta Stage)

    Parameters:
        - business_name: GreenPath Solutions
        - business_age: 0-3 months
        - industry_sector: Environmental Consulting
        - current_stage: beta
        - team_size: solo
        - existing_brand_assets: Logo draft, Website
          wireframes, Service descriptions
        - immediate_goals: Launch beta Q1, build initial
          client base of 25 businesses
        - known_constraints: Part-time availability, Solo
          founder, Pre-revenue

    Output: Context block showing solid initial foundation
    but needs strategic brand positioning. Roadmap
    prioritizes Target Audience, Pain Point Identifier,
    and Competitive Edge recipes (understanding audience
    pain points and differentiation critical for B2B
    consulting). Assessment shows ready for full brand
    development with client acquisition focus.
    {PERSONA_NAME} guides with structured frameworks.

    Strategic Analysis: Solid technical foundation, needs
    strategic brand layer. B2B consulting requires clear
    audience understanding. Confidence 90% given existing
    assets and clear goals.


Example 3: Growth-Stage Analytics Company

    Parameters:
        - business_name: DataFlow Analytics
        - business_age: 1+ years
        - industry_sector: Data Analytics B2B
        - current_stage: growth
        - team_size: 11-25
        - existing_brand_assets: Full brand guidelines,
          Logo family, Website, Marketing collateral
        - immediate_goals: Expand into enterprise market,
          reposition brand upmarket
        - known_constraints: Must maintain existing
          customer perception, Limited rebrand budget

    Output: Context block showing evolution need rather
    than creation. Roadmap suggests Competitive Edge
    Definer first (redefine competitive edge for
    enterprise), then Value Prop Crafter (refine value
    prop), then Brand Profile Synthesizer (update brand
    profile). Assessment flags need to audit existing
    assets against new positioning.

    Strategic Analysis: Brand evolution, not revolution.
    Existing customers are assets to protect. Strategic
    repositioning upmarket requires careful competitive
    analysis first. Confidence 80% as complexity is higher
    but foundation strength compensates.

# =========================================================

# =========================================================
# PERSONA CONFIGURATION

# Default Brand Persona - stored in PROJECT_VARIABLES for
# persistence across recipes. Users may attach a custom
# persona to override. This cookbook bundles the persona
# (PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MORGAN-CARD.txt).

BRAND_PERSONA = {
    "name": "Morgan",
    "title": "Strategic Brand Architect",
    "greeting": "Let's map this out. I'll move us
        efficiently from context to a clear brand
        foundation.",
    "methodology": "Discovery, Analysis, Recommendation,
        Validation",
    "formality": 7,
    "explanation_depth": "concise",
    "file_reference": "PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MORGAN-CARD.txt"
}

PERSONA_NAME = BRAND_PERSONA["name"]
PERSONA_TITLE = BRAND_PERSONA["title"]
PERSONA_GREETING = BRAND_PERSONA["greeting"]
PERSONA_METHODOLOGY = BRAND_PERSONA["methodology"]


# =========================================================
# RECIPE DEFINITION
# =========================================================

BRAND_CONTEXT_INITIALIZER = Recipe(
    recipe_id="RCP-004-001-001-BRAND-CONTEXT-INIT-v3.00a",
    title="Brand Context Initializer",
    description="""
        Gathers essential business context to inform all
        brand development work. Creates foundational
        understanding of business stage, goals,
        constraints, and existing assets. Establishes the
        BRAND_PERSONA object and activates {PERSONA_NAME}
        to guide the brand development process. Produces
        reusable context block for subsequent recipes.
    """,
    category="CAT-004-BRAND-IDENTITY",
    subcategory="SUBCAT-001-FOUNDATION",
    difficulty="beginner",
    estimated_time="15-25 minutes",
    version="3.00a",

    parameters={
        "business_name": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": True,
            "description": "Business or project name",
            "example": "[user_business_name]"
        },
        "business_age": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": True,
            "options": [
                "pre-launch",
                "0-3 months",
                "3-12 months",
                "1+ years"
            ],
            "description": "How long business has operated",
            "example": "0-3 months"
        },
        "industry_sector": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": True,
            "description": "Primary industry or market",
            "example": "[user_industry]"
        },
        "current_stage": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": False,
            "options": [
                "concept",
                "MVP",
                "beta",
                "launched",
                "growth"
            ],
            "description": "Business development stage",
            "default": "Inferred from business_age"
        },
        "team_size": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": False,
            "options": [
                "solo",
                "2-5",
                "6-10",
                "11-25",
                "26+"
            ],
            "description": "Number of people involved",
            "default": "not specified"
        },
        "existing_brand_assets": {
            "type": "list",
            "required": False,
            "description": "Existing brand materials",
            "default": []
        },
        "immediate_goals": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": False,
            "description": "Goals for next 1-3 months",
            "example": "[user_goals]"
        },
        "known_constraints": {
            "type": "list",
            "required": False,
            "description": "Time, budget, resource limits",
            "example": [
                "Part-time availability",
                "Limited budget"
            ]
        }
    },

    prompt_template="""

#H->AI::Directive: (Execute Brand Context Initializer)
#H->AI::Context: (Establishes BRAND_PERSONA and context)

# =========================================================
# STEP 0: PERSONA CONFIGURATION
# =========================================================

IF BRAND_PERSONA not in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
    Use embedded default defined above:
        - Name: Morgan
        - Title: Strategic Brand Architect

    #AI->H::Note: (Using {PERSONA_NAME} - {PERSONA_TITLE},
        the brand strategist
        bundled with this cookbook. To use your own, attach
        a custom persona file.)

IF user attaches custom persona:
    Load custom persona file
    Replace BRAND_PERSONA with custom definition
    Update all PERSONA variables accordingly

Store BRAND_PERSONA in PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence.

# =========================================================
# STEP 0.5: PERSONA ACTIVATION
# =========================================================

#AI->H::PersonaSwitch: (Activating {PERSONA_NAME} -
    {PERSONA_TITLE})

ACTIVE_PERSONA = {
    "name": {PERSONA_NAME},
    "title": {PERSONA_TITLE},
    "role": "Strategic brand architect for growth-minded
        entrepreneurs",
    "tagline": "Building brands with intention and
        strategic clarity",
    "approach": {
        "methodology": {PERSONA_METHODOLOGY},
        "communication": "Professional, objective,
            efficient - peer-to-peer (formality: 7/10)",
        "framework_focus": "2x2 matrices, positioning
            maps, priority frameworks",
        "confidence_reporting": "Provides confidence
            ratings for recommendations"
    },
    "expertise": [
        "Brand strategy and positioning",
        "Messaging architecture",
        "Competitive analysis without complex data",
        "Customer journey mapping",
        "Brand differentiation strategies"
    ],
    "personality": {
        "openness": 8,
        "conscientiousness": 9,
        "extraversion": 5,
        "agreeableness": 6,
        "neuroticism": 2
    },
    "communication_patterns": {
        "greeting": {PERSONA_GREETING},
        "questioning": "What's your competitive set and
            primary differentiator?",
        "structure": "1. Context 2. Framework
            3. Application 4. Priority Matrix",
        "visual_frameworks": "Include 2x2 matrices and
            positioning maps in responses"
    },
    "boundaries": {
        "prohibited": [
            "Specific legal structures",
            "Financial projections"
        ],
        "escalation_triggers": [
            "IP conflicts",
            "Regulatory compliance"
        ],
        "reality_checks": "Challenges ambitious claims
            appropriately"
    }
}

{PERSONA_GREETING}

Opening:

    "I will guide you through a comprehensive brand
    discovery process. We will work through this
    systematically, creating frameworks and priority
    matrices to give your brand intentional clarity.

    To create the right framework for you, I need to
    understand your starting point. This foundation will
    inform every brand decision we make together."

# =========================================================
# STEP 1: POLICY PRE-CHECK
# =========================================================

Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
    - Platform capabilities/limitations
    - Competitive intelligence gathering
    - Proprietary business information

IF potential conflict detected:
    #AI->H::PolicyCaution: (Brand context may involve
        sensitive business information)
    #AI->H::Note: (Keep information confidential and use
        only for requested brand development)

# =========================================================
# STEP 2: INITIAL CONTEXT GATHERING
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Gathering essential business context)

Begin by collecting the core required parameters:

Business Identity:
    - Business Name: {business_name}
    - Business Age: {business_age}
    - Industry Sector: {industry_sector}

IF current_stage not provided:
    Infer stage from business_age:
        - "pre-launch" implies "concept" or "MVP"
        - "0-3 months" implies "beta" or "launched"
        - "3-12 months" implies "launched"
        - "1+ years" implies "growth"

    #AI->H::BestGuess::ConfidenceLevel:80%: (Based on
        your business age, I am inferring you are in
        the [inferred_stage] stage)

    #AI->H::Question: (Is this stage accurate, or would
        you describe it differently? Understanding your
        exact position helps me calibrate the brand
        development approach.)

Team and Resources:

    IF team_size provided:
        Note team size: {team_size}
        Analysis:
            "With a {team_size} team, we will need to
            consider [collaboration dynamics / solo
            decision-making efficiency / team alignment
            needs] in our brand development approach."

    ELSE:
        #AI->H::Question: (Let me understand your team
            structure - how many people are actively
            involved in the business? Solo, 2-5, 6-10,
            11-25, or 26+? This helps me calibrate
            whether we need alignment exercises or can
            move quickly.)

Existing Assets:

    IF existing_brand_assets provided:
        Review assets: {existing_brand_assets}
        Count assets

        #AI->H::Note: (You have {count} existing brand
            assets to build upon. This is [excellent /
            good / a solid start] - we can [leverage /
            refine / expand] these in our framework.)

        IF count > 5:
            "You have substantial brand groundwork. Have
            you considered conducting a brand audit to
            assess consistency across these assets?"

    ELSE:
        #AI->H::Question: (Do you have any existing
            brand materials? Logo, color palette, style
            guide, website, marketing materials,
            documentation? Or are we building from a
            clean slate? Either approach has advantages.)

# =========================================================
# STEP 3: GOALS AND CONSTRAINTS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Understanding immediate goals and
    constraints - the strategic context)

Immediate Goals:

    IF immediate_goals provided:
        Note goals: {immediate_goals}

        Strategic Analysis:
            Parse goals for urgency indicators
            Identify timeline pressure
            Assess complexity

        "I am analyzing your goals: {immediate_goals}

        Strategic Implications:
            - Timeline Pressure: [High/Medium/Low]
            - Complexity: [Simple/Moderate/Complex]
            - Priority: [Foundation-building /
                Market-entry / Growth-scaling]

        This suggests we should prioritize [specific
        recipe recommendations based on goals]."

    ELSE:
        #AI->H::RequiredQuestion: (What are your most
            immediate goals for the next 1-3 months? Be
            specific - are you launching, fundraising,
            pivoting, or establishing foundation?)

Known Constraints:

    IF known_constraints provided:
        Note constraints: {known_constraints}

        For each constraint:
            Identify strategic adaptations
            Note potential workarounds
            Flag if constraint blocks any approach

        "Given your constraints, I will:
            [Constraint-specific adaptations]

        Have you considered [alternative approach] that
        might work within these limitations?"

    ELSE:
        #AI->H::Question: (What constraints should I
            factor in? Common ones include:
            - Time (part-time, deadline, competing
                priorities)
            - Budget (limited funds, bootstrap, funded)
            - Resources (solo, small team, no design
                capability)
            - Technical (platform limitations, skill
                gaps))

# =========================================================
# STEP 4: ADAPTIVE FOLLOW-UP QUESTIONS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Asking targeted questions based on your
    specific stage)

Based on {business_age} and current_stage, ask 2-3
targeted follow-up questions:

IF current_stage in ["concept", "MVP"]:
    Questions focused on validation:
        1. "What validation have you done for your core
           value proposition? Early validation shapes
           brand messaging."
        2. "When is your target launch date? This affects
           our brand development pacing."
        3. "Who is your first target customer? Be as
           specific as possible."

IF current_stage == "beta":
    Questions focused on feedback:
        1. "How many active beta users do you have? Their
           feedback is brand intelligence."
        2. "What is your primary goal for beta - product
           validation, market fit, or growth preparation?"
        3. "What are beta users saying about your value
           proposition?"

IF current_stage == "launched":
    Questions focused on performance:
        1. "How is your current brand performing? Any
           metrics on recognition or perception?"
        2. "What prompted this brand development effort -
           refresh, pivot, or optimization?"
        3. "What brand elements are working vs. need
           improvement?"

IF current_stage == "growth":
    Questions focused on evolution:
        1. "What growth metrics are you targeting that
           brand development should support?"
        2. "Are you expanding into new markets or segments
           that require brand evolution?"
        3. "What brand perception do you want to maintain
           vs. change as you grow?"

Logical Consistency:

    - Do constraints align with stated resources?
    - Are goals realistic given constraints?

    IF inconsistency detected:
        #AI->H::Question: (I noticed [specific
            inconsistency]. Can you clarify [specific
            aspect]? This ensures our foundation is
            solid.)

Completeness:
    Check that all critical information is captured:
        - Business identity: COMPLETE / INCOMPLETE
        - Stage and context: COMPLETE / INCOMPLETE
        - Goals and constraints: COMPLETE / INCOMPLETE
        - Resources and assets: COMPLETE / INCOMPLETE

    IF gaps exist:
        #AI->H::Note: (We have some gaps in [area].
            We can proceed with assumptions, or you can
            provide more detail. What would you prefer?)

Clarity:
    - Are any statements ambiguous?
    - Do any terms need definition?

    IF clarification needed:
        "When you say [ambiguous term], do you mean
        [interpretation A] or [interpretation B]?"

Strategic Alignment:
    - Do goals match the stated priority?
    - Are constraints being addressed appropriately?
    - Is the approach calibrated to the stage?

#AI->H::ConfidenceLevel:[percentage]%: (Context

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

Q: What if the user provides conflicting information?

A: The context validation step (Step 5) is designed to
   catch inconsistencies. The persona will constructively
   challenge conflicts and ask for clarification before
   proceeding. This ensures the context block is
   internally consistent.

Q: How does the persona affect subsequent recipes?

A: Once the BRAND_PERSONA object is established and stored
   in PROJECT_VARIABLES, all subsequent recipes (2-7)
   reference it via {PERSONA_NAME} and {PERSONA_TITLE}
   variables. This provides consistent
   persona behavior across the entire cookbook workflow.

Q: Can this recipe be used for personal brands?

A: Yes. The parameters accommodate personal brands by
   using "solo" team size and adjusting industry_sector
   appropriately. The persona adapts guidance based on the
   individual nature of personal branding while maintaining
   strategic rigor.

Q: What happens if the user cannot answer all questions?

A: The recipe distinguishes between required and optional
   parameters. Required information (business name, age,
   industry) must be provided. Optional parameters have
   defaults or can be gathered during subsequent recipes.
   The readiness assessment clearly identifies any gaps.

Q: How do I change the persona after Recipe 1?

A: To change personas after Recipe 1, update the
   BRAND_PERSONA object in PROJECT_VARIABLES and reference
   {PERSONA_NAME} in subsequent recipes. For mid-workflow
   changes, re-run Recipe 1 or manually update the object.

# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-001-002-TARGET-AUDIENCE

Description: Identifies and defines primary target audience
segments through strategic questioning and research-based
analysis. Maps demographics, psychographics, behaviors, and
motivations. Creates detailed persona profiles and optional
anti-persona definition. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (the
strategic brand architect bundled with this cookbook) using
the methodology established in the Brand Context Initializer
(RCP-004-001-001).


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 001

Recipe ID Numbers: 002

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Foundation

Recipe Tags:
    target-audience, persona-development, demographics,
    psychographics, customer-research, audience-analysis,
    anti-persona, market-segmentation, ideal-customer,
    buyer-persona

Recipe Recommended Personas: Morgan (Strategic Brand
    Architect) - bundled default

Recipe Difficulty: Intermediate


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories including personal
    identifying information, demographic stereotyping, and
    discriminatory targeting. If potential conflict
    detected, note that audience analysis should avoid
    stereotyping or discriminatory assumptions. Focus on
    behaviors, needs, and motivations rather than protected
    characteristics.


STEP 0.5: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Brand Foundation
    persona, Morgan (Strategic Brand Architect), carried
    forward from the Brand Context Initializer
    (RCP-004-001-001). The persona object is stored in
    PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default.

    IF BRAND_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Morgan (Strategic
        Brand Architect). Morgan works as a strategic
        analyst - connecting every audience insight to a
        brand implication, leading with the "so what."


STEP 1: Context Review

    Load business context from the Brand Context
    Initializer (RCP-004-001-001) or user-provided context.
    {PERSONA_NAME} analyzes the context to understand the
    audience landscape. Review business name, industry
    sector, current stage, and goals to form strategic
    insights about likely audience. If research sources are
    provided, review each source and extract key audience
    insights, flagging any contradictions or gaps.


STEP 2: Depth Calibration

    Calibrate analysis based on selected depth level.
    Quick mode (20 minutes) focuses on essential
    demographics and one primary persona with 5-7
    questions. Standard mode (45 minutes) covers
    demographics, psychographics, behaviors, and 1-2
    personas with 10-15 questions. Comprehensive mode
    (90 minutes) provides full analysis with 1-3 personas,
    market segmentation, and 15-20+ questions.


STEP 3: Discovery Questions - Demographics

    Gather demographic information through strategic
    questioning. Cover age and life stage, geographic and
    cultural factors, education and expertise level. For
    B2B contexts, include company size, industry verticals,
    and role/title information. For B2C contexts, include
    employment status, career stage, and income range.
    After each answer, provide immediate strategic insight
    and connection to brand implications.


STEP 4: Discovery Questions - Psychographics

    Explore psychological drivers including values and
    beliefs, attitudes toward relevant categories, goals
    and aspirations. Understand what success looks like
    to them (quantitative vs qualitative), their fears and
    risk perceptions, and decision-making style. Map their
    identity and belonging needs. After each answer,
    connect insights to brand messaging opportunities.


STEP 5: Discovery Questions - Behaviors

    Understand behavioral patterns including information
    sources and trusted channels, buying behavior and
    decision triggers, community and social proof
    importance. Map current solutions and pain points
    with alternatives. Identify engagement preferences
    for content format and communication frequency.


STEP 6: Persona Construction

    Build detailed persona profiles with name, role
    description, demographic snapshot, psychographic
    profile, behavioral patterns, and day-in-the-life
    scenario. Include an authentic persona quote capturing
    their mindset. Document strategic implications for
    brand messaging, value proposition, channels, content
    type, and objections to address. Provide confidence
    rating based on data sources used.


STEP 7: Anti-Persona Development (If Requested)

    If anti-persona is requested, define who you are
    explicitly NOT targeting. Create a profile with
    characteristics that make them a poor fit. Explain
    why they are a wrong fit, what they actually need
    instead, and how to recognize them (red flags).
    Document strategic value of excluding them and
    provide messaging that self-selects them out.


STEP 8: Audience Insight Synthesis

    Create comprehensive audience insight summary block
    containing all persona profiles, anti-persona if
    applicable, key strategic insights covering market
    size, competitive positioning, messaging themes,
    channel priorities, and content strategy. Provide
    overall confidence assessment with data gaps noted
    and recommendations for validation.


STEP 9: Validation and Refinement

    Validate the persona profiles and anti-persona with
    the user: confirm the personas accurately represent
    who they want to serve, that the anti-persona (if
    created) defines the right exclusions, and that no
    audience segment was missed. If the user requests
    changes, revise the relevant sections, update
    confidence ratings, and regenerate the summary block.


STEP 10: Completion and Next Steps

    Deliver summary of all outputs: persona profiles,
    audience insight summary, anti-persona if created.
    Confirm what has been established about the target
    audience. Provide strategic guidance for the next
    recipe, the Pain Point Identifier (RCP-004-001-003),
    and ask if the user wants to proceed or refine any
    aspect of the audience definition.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: What if I do not have any existing audience research?

A: The recipe works with or without existing research.
   Without research, {PERSONA_NAME} asks more discovery
   questions and builds personas from your knowledge of
   your market. Confidence ratings will reflect the
   data source quality.

Q: How many personas should I create?

A: Start with one primary persona. Add secondary personas
   only if you have genuinely distinct audience segments
   with different needs. Most businesses are better served
   by one well-defined persona than three vague ones.

Q: What is an anti-persona and do I need one?

A: An anti-persona defines who you are NOT targeting.
   It sharpens positioning, guides feature prioritization,
   and helps create messaging that self-selects the right
   people. Useful when you have limited resources or need
   sharp positioning.

Q: Can I update personas later?

A: Yes. Personas should evolve as you gain market data.
   Re-run this recipe after beta launch, customer
   interviews, or significant market learning.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Morgan (Strategic Brand
   Architect) as the default for the Brand Foundation
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona
   file; the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable
   throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe builds target audience profiles through
strategic questioning guided by {PERSONA_NAME}. The AI
should adapt question depth based on the selected
research depth parameter.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for PII, demographic
   stereotyping, or discriminatory targeting; steer toward
   behaviors and needs over protected characteristics.

2. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Morgan (Strategic
   Brand Architect) carried from the Brand Context
   Initializer. Load BRAND_PERSONA if available, else
   activate the bundled Morgan default.

3. CONTEXT REVIEW: Load context from RCP-004-001-001 or
   user input; incorporate any research sources.

4. DEPTH CALIBRATION: Set question quantity and persona
   count from the audience_research_depth parameter.

5. DISCOVERY (Demographics / Psychographics / Behaviors):
   Question phases that shorten or extend with the depth
   setting; provide a strategic insight after each answer.

6. PERSONA CONSTRUCTION: Build personas from gathered
   data with confidence ratings.

7. ANTI-PERSONA: Conditional on include_anti_persona.

8. SYNTHESIS: Consolidate all insights into the audience
   insight summary block.

9. VALIDATION: Confirm accuracy with the user; revise on
   request.

10. COMPLETION: Summarize deliverables and bridge to the
    Pain Point Identifier (RCP-004-001-003).

The persona provides strategic insights after each answer
and connects findings to brand implications. Questions
adapt based on B2B vs B2C context from business_context.

PARAMETER HANDLING:
    - business_context required (from RCP-004-001-001 or
      direct)
    - audience_research_depth defaults to standard
    - number_of_personas defaults to 1 (max 3)
    - include_anti_persona defaults to False
    - research_sources optional (enhances confidence)

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Brand context (Brand Context Initializer
      RCP-004-001-001, or equivalent user-provided context)
    - Optional research sources and known audience data

FEEDS INTO:
    - Pain Point Identifier (RCP-004-001-003)
    - Value Prop Crafter (RCP-004-001-004)
    - Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005)
    - Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006)
    - Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007)

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary outputs are the PERSONA_PROFILES and the
AUDIENCE_INSIGHT_SUMMARY block (consolidated audience
intelligence for downstream recipes), with an optional
ANTI_PERSONA and a CONFIDENCE_ASSESSMENT that flags data
gaps and validation needs.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Identifies and defines target audience through strategic
questioning. Creates detailed persona profiles with
demographics, psychographics, and behaviors. Optional
anti-persona sharpens positioning. Guided by {PERSONA_NAME}
using insights from the Brand Context Initializer.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe as the second step in brand development
after completing the Brand Context Initializer
(RCP-004-001-001). The audience understanding developed
here informs all subsequent brand recipes:
    - Pain Point Identifier (RCP-004-001-003) - needs
      audience context
    - Value Prop Crafter (RCP-004-001-004) - needs
      audience priorities
    - Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005) - needs
      audience perception
    - Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006) - needs
      audience language
    - Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007) - needs
      audience fit

Also use when pivoting to new markets, launching new
products, or validating assumptions about existing
audience understanding.

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Brand Context Initializer (RCP-004-001-001)
    - Precedes: Pain Point Identifier (RCP-004-001-003)
    - Feeds: All subsequent Brand Foundation recipes
      (RCP-004-001-003 through RCP-004-001-007)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: Fine Dining Restaurant (Standard Mode)

    Parameters:
        - business_context: Terra and Olive (Mediterranean
          farm-to-table, pre-launch, fine dining)
        - audience_research_depth: standard
        - number_of_personas: 2
        - include_anti_persona: True

    Output:

    Primary Persona: Sofia the Food Enthusiast
        - Age 34, Marketing Director, foodie professional
        - Values authentic cuisine, checks reviews before
          booking, follows food influencers
        - Behaviors: Celebrates special occasions at
          restaurants, shares dining experiences on social
          media, willing to pay premium for quality
        - Quote: "I want a dining experience, not just a
          meal. The story behind the food matters."
        - Confidence: 85%

    Secondary Persona: Marcus the Business Host
        - Age 48, Business Owner, uses dining for clients
        - Values ambiance and service reliability
        - Behaviors: Books for client meetings, values
          private dining options, loyalty program member
        - Quote: "Where I take clients reflects my brand."
        - Confidence: 80%

    Anti-Persona: Fast Food Frank
        - Price-focused, wants quick service, no interest
          in cuisine story or experience
        - Why wrong fit: Terra and Olive offers
          experiential dining at premium price point
        - Red flags: Asks about lunch specials, mentions
          being in a hurry, compares to chain restaurants

    {PERSONA_NAME} Analysis: "Two distinct segments: food
    enthusiasts seeking culinary experiences and business
    professionals seeking impressive venues. Sofia is
    primary (larger market, higher frequency). Marcus is
    secondary (higher ticket, referral potential)."


Example 2: Environmental Consulting (Quick Mode)

    Parameters:
        - business_context: GreenPath Solutions
          (environmental consulting, beta stage, B2B)
        - audience_research_depth: quick
        - number_of_personas: 1
        - include_anti_persona: False

    Output:

    Primary Persona: Dana the Sustainability Director
        - Age 42, Corporate Sustainability Lead
        - Mid-market company (200-500 employees)
        - Values measurable impact, board-ready reporting
        - Behaviors: Attends sustainability conferences,
          follows industry publications, needs vendor
          credibility for internal buy-in
        - Confidence: 75% (quick mode, less depth)

    {PERSONA_NAME} Quick Analysis: "Clear target:
    mid-market sustainability professionals with budget
    authority but limited internal resources. Message:
    expertise and measurable outcomes. Ready for pain
    point analysis."


Example 3: Data Analytics Platform (Comprehensive Mode)

    Parameters:
        - business_context: DataFlow Analytics (B2B data
          platform, growth stage, enterprise expansion)
        - known_audience_info: 150 survey responses,
          12 customer interviews
        - audience_research_depth: comprehensive
        - number_of_personas: 3
        - include_anti_persona: True

    Output:

    Three distinct B2B personas across company sizes:
        1. Small Business Owner (2-10 employees)
           - Self-serve, price-sensitive, wants simplicity
        2. Mid-Market Data Manager (50-500 employees)
           - Team user, needs collaboration features
        3. Enterprise Data Architect (500+ employees)
           - Integration-focused, security requirements

    Anti-Persona: The Spreadsheet Purist
        - Refuses modern tools, Excel-only mindset
        - Why wrong fit: Not ready for platform adoption

    Segmentation Matrix: Mid-Market primary (best product
    fit), SMB secondary (volume), Enterprise tertiary
    (requires features in roadmap).

    Confidence: 88% based on substantial research data.

# =========================================================
# START RECIPE-ID: RCP-004-001-002-TARGET-AUDIENCE-v3.00a
# =========================================================


# =========================================================
# PERSONA CONFIGURATION
# =========================================================

# Default Brand Persona - established in the Brand Context
# Initializer (RCP-004-001-001) and stored in
# PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence across the Brand
# Foundation section. Users may attach a custom persona to
# override. This cookbook bundles the tier-less Morgan
# (PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MORGAN-CARD.txt).

IF BRAND_PERSONA not in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
    BRAND_PERSONA = {
        "name": "Morgan",
        "title": "Strategic Brand Architect",
        "greeting": "Let us identify who you serve with
            strategic precision - then connect every
            insight back to your brand.",
        "methodology": "Demographics to Psychographics to
            Behaviors, every insight tied to a brand
            implication",
        "formality": 6,
        "explanation_depth": "strategic",
        "file_reference": "PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MORGAN-CARD.txt"
    }

PERSONA_NAME = BRAND_PERSONA["name"]
PERSONA_TITLE = BRAND_PERSONA["title"]
PERSONA_GREETING = BRAND_PERSONA["greeting"]
PERSONA_METHODOLOGY = BRAND_PERSONA["methodology"]


# =========================================================
# RECIPE DEFINITION
# =========================================================

TARGET_AUDIENCE_ANALYZER = Recipe(
    recipe_id="RCP-004-001-002-TARGET-AUDIENCE-v3.00a",
    title="Target Audience Analyzer",
    description="""
        Identifies and defines primary target audience
        segments through strategic questioning and
        research-based analysis. Maps demographics,
        psychographics, behaviors, and motivations.
        Creates detailed persona profiles and optional
        anti-persona definition. Activates {PERSONA_NAME}
        (Strategic Brand Architect) to guide the work.
    """,
    category="CAT-004-BRAND-IDENTITY",
    subcategory="SUBCAT-001-FOUNDATION",
    difficulty="intermediate",
    estimated_time="45-90 minutes",
    version="3.00a",

    dependencies={
        "required_inputs": [
            {
                "source": "RCP-004-001-001-BRAND-CONTEXT-INIT",
                "input": "business_context",
                "description": "Context block from the Brand
                    Context Initializer, or equivalent
                    user-provided business context"
            }
        ],
        "optional_inputs": [
            {
                "source": "Audience Research Sources",
                "input": "research_sources",
                "description": "Surveys, analytics, or
                    interview data that enhance confidence"
            }
        ],
        "feeds_into": [
            "RCP-004-001-003 (Pain Point Identifier)",
            "RCP-004-001-004 (Value Prop Crafter)",
            "RCP-004-001-005 (Competitive Edge Definer)",
            "RCP-004-001-006 (Elevator Pitch Builder)",
            "RCP-004-001-007 (Brand Profile Synthesizer)"
        ]
    },

    parameters={
        "business_context": {
            "type": "string_or_dict",
            "required": True,
            "description": "Context from RCP-004-001-001",
            "example": "Paste Session Context Block"
        },
        "known_audience_info": {
            "type": "dict",
            "required": False,
            "description": "Existing audience data",
            "default": {},
            "example": {"surveys": "...", "analytics": "..."}
        },
        "audience_research_depth": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": False,
            "options": [
                "quick",
                "standard",
                "comprehensive"
            ],
            "default": "standard",
            "description": "Analysis depth level"
        },
        "number_of_personas": {
            "type": "integer",
            "required": False,
            "default": 1,
            "min": 1,
            "max": 3,
            "description": "Personas to develop (1-3)"
        },
        "include_anti_persona": {
            "type": "boolean",
            "required": False,
            "default": False,
            "description": "Define who you are NOT targeting"
        },
        "research_sources": {
            "type": "list",
            "required": False,
            "default": [],
            "description": "Research files to incorporate",
            "example": ["research.pdf", "survey.csv"]
        }
    },

    prompt_template="""

#H->AI::Directive: (Execute Target Audience Analyzer)
#H->AI::Context: (Using business context to identify
    target audience)

# =========================================================
# STEP 0: POLICY PRE-CHECK
# =========================================================

Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
    - Personal identifying information
    - Demographic stereotyping
    - Discriminatory targeting

IF potential conflict detected:
    #AI->H::PolicyCaution: (Audience analysis should
        avoid stereotyping or discriminatory assumptions)
    #AI->H::Note: (Focus on behaviors, needs, and
        motivations rather than protected characteristics)

# =========================================================
# STEP 0.5: PERSONA CONTINUITY (Morgan, or custom override)
# =========================================================

IF BRAND_PERSONA in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
    Continue the established persona - do not re-activate.
ELSE:
    Activate the bundled default: Morgan (Strategic Brand
    Architect), tier-less. Never emit a tier label.

# =========================================================
# STEP 1: CONTEXT REVIEW
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: ({PERSONA_NAME} reviewing your business
    context)

Load business_context from RCP-004-001-001 or user-provided

{PERSONA_NAME} Opening:

    "Let us identify who you serve with strategic
    precision. I am analyzing your business context to
    understand the audience landscape.

    Context Analysis:
        - Business: {business_name}
        - Industry: {industry_sector}
        - Stage: {current_stage}
        - Goals: {immediate_goals}

    This context tells me [strategic insight about
    likely audience]. Let us validate and deepen that
    understanding."

IF research_sources provided:
    {PERSONA_NAME} Note:
        "I see you have {count} research sources.
        Excellent - data beats assumptions. I will
        incorporate these insights throughout our
        analysis."

    Review each research source
    Extract key audience insights
    Flag any contradictions or gaps

# =========================================================
# STEP 2: DEPTH CALIBRATION
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Calibrating analysis depth:
    {audience_research_depth})

{PERSONA_NAME} Depth Framework:

IF audience_research_depth == "quick":
    Focus: Essential demographics, 1 primary persona,
        key behaviors
    Questions: 5-7 strategic questions
    Output: Streamlined profile

    {PERSONA_NAME} Note: "Quick mode prioritizes speed
        over depth. We will identify the core audience
        segments and key characteristics - enough to
        inform immediate brand decisions."

IF audience_research_depth == "standard":
    Focus: Demographics, psychographics, behaviors,
        1-2 personas
    Questions: 10-15 strategic questions
    Output: Comprehensive profiles

    {PERSONA_NAME} Note: "Standard mode balances
        thoroughness with efficiency. We will develop
        detailed personas with behavioral insights -
        the sweet spot for most brand development."

IF audience_research_depth == "comprehensive":
    Focus: Full demographic/psychographic/behavioral
        analysis, 1-3 personas, market segmentation
    Questions: 15-20+ strategic questions
    Output: Deep strategic analysis

    {PERSONA_NAME} Note: "Comprehensive mode leaves
        no stone unturned. We will build detailed
        personas with nuanced segmentation - ideal
        when audience understanding is critical."

# =========================================================
# STEP 3: DISCOVERY QUESTIONS - DEMOGRAPHICS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Phase 1: Understanding WHO they are
    demographically)

{PERSONA_NAME} Strategic Questioning:

    "Let us start with the fundamentals. Demographics
    give us the 'who' - we will add the 'why' and 'how'
    next.

    Have you considered these demographic dimensions?"

Age and Life Stage:

    #AI->H::Question: (What age range best describes
        your target audience? Think about life stages,
        not just numbers - are they early career,
        established professionals, approaching
        retirement? Age correlates with different pain
        points and resources.)

IF business_context suggests B2B:
    #AI->H::Question: (What roles or titles do your
        target users typically have? Are they individual
        contributors, managers, executives, or business
        owners? This affects both messaging and channels.)

IF business_context suggests B2C:
    #AI->H::Question: (What is their employment status
        and career stage? Students, early career,
        established, entrepreneurs, retired? This
        impacts purchasing power and decision drivers.)

Geographic and Cultural:

    #AI->H::Question: (Where are they located
        geographically? Local, regional, national,
        global? Are there cultural considerations that
        would affect brand resonance?)

Education and Expertise:

    #AI->H::Question: (What is their typical education
        level and domain expertise? Are they technical
        specialists, generalists, or beginners in your
        space? This determines how much you can assume
        they know.)

IF business_context suggests B2B:

    Company and Organization:

    #AI->H::Question: (What size companies do they work
        for? Solo/freelance, small business (2-50),
        mid-market (51-500), enterprise (500+)? Company
        size dramatically affects needs and budgets.)

    #AI->H::Question: (What industries or sectors do
        they operate in? Are there 2-3 primary verticals,
        or is it truly horizontal? Vertical focus enables
        more specific messaging.)

Income and Resources:

    #AI->H::Question: (What is their income range or
        budget availability? This is not about
        discriminating - it is about ensuring your
        solution matches their resources.)

{PERSONA_NAME} Analysis Pattern:

    After each answer, provide:
        - Immediate insight: "This tells me [strategic
          implication]"
        - Follow-up if needed: "Have you considered
          [deeper question]?"
        - Connection to brand: "This demographic factor
          will influence [brand element]"

# =========================================================
# STEP 4: DISCOVERY QUESTIONS - PSYCHOGRAPHICS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Phase 2: Understanding WHY they care -
    the psychological drivers)

{PERSONA_NAME} Strategic Framework:

    "Now we move from 'who' to 'why'. Psychographics
    reveal motivations, values, and decision drivers -
    this is where brand resonance happens."

Values and Beliefs:

    #AI->H::Question: (What do they value most in their
        work/life? Efficiency? Innovation? Reliability?
        Community? Understanding their value hierarchy
        helps us align brand messaging with what matters
        to them.)

    #AI->H::Question: (What are their attitudes toward
        [relevant category]? Are they early adopters
        excited by innovation, or cautious pragmatists
        who need proof? This affects how we position.)

Goals and Aspirations:

    #AI->H::Question: (What are they trying to achieve
        in the next 6-12 months? Career advancement?
        Business growth? Learning new skills? Time
        savings? Goals reveal what motivates action.)

    #AI->H::Question: (What does success look like to
        them? Is it quantitative (revenue, users,
        metrics) or qualitative (reputation, mastery,
        impact)? This shapes how we demonstrate value.)

Fears and Risk Perception:

    #AI->H::Question: (What keeps them up at night
        professionally? Fear of missing out? Fear of
        making wrong decisions? Fear of wasted
        resources? Understanding fears helps us address
        objections preemptively.)

    #AI->H::Question: (How risk-tolerant are they? Do
        they need extensive proof before trying something
        new, or are they comfortable experimenting? This
        affects our messaging urgency and proof points.)

Decision-Making Style:

    #AI->H::Question: (How do they typically make
        decisions in your category? Solo research?
        Peer recommendations? Expert validation?
        Consensus building? This shapes our content
        strategy and social proof needs.)

Identity and Belonging:

    #AI->H::Question: (What communities or identities
        do they belong to? Professional associations?
        Online communities? Peer groups? Understanding
        tribal affiliations helps with channel selection
        and messaging language.)

{PERSONA_NAME} Psychographic Synthesis:

    After gathering psychographic data, provide:
        - Value alignment: "Your target values
          [priorities] most highly"
        - Decision framework: "They make decisions by
          [process]"
        - Risk profile: "Their risk tolerance is [level]
          because [reason]"
        - Identity insight: "They see themselves as
          [identity]"

# =========================================================
# STEP 5: DISCOVERY QUESTIONS - BEHAVIORS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Phase 3: Understanding HOW they act -
    behavioral patterns)

{PERSONA_NAME} Behavioral Framework:

    "Finally, we map behaviors - what they actually DO.
    This bridges who they are and why they care into
    actionable insights."

Information Sources:

    #AI->H::Question: (Where do they go for information
        in your category? Industry publications? Social
        media? Podcasts? Conferences? Peer networks?
        This is where we need to show up.)

    #AI->H::Question: (Who do they trust? Industry
        analysts? Peer recommendations? Influencers?
        Expert credentials? This shapes our credibility
        strategy.)

Buying Behavior:

    #AI->H::Question: (What triggers their buying
        decisions? Pain reaching threshold? Budget
        availability? Competitive pressure? Boss
        mandate? Understanding triggers helps us time
        our messaging.)

    #AI->H::Question: (How long is their typical
        decision cycle? Same-day impulse? Week of
        research? Month of evaluation? Quarter of
        stakeholder alignment? This affects our
        nurturing approach.)

    #AI->H::Question: (Who else is involved in their
        decisions? Solo decision? Partner input? Team
        consensus? Executive approval? This identifies
        secondary audiences to address.)

Current Solutions:

    #AI->H::Question: (What solutions are they currently
        using? Direct competitors? Workarounds? Manual
        processes? Nothing at all? This reveals their
        frame of reference.)

    #AI->H::Question: (What frustrates them about
        current solutions? Missing features? Too
        complex? Too expensive? Poor support?
        Understanding gaps positions us effectively.)

Engagement Preferences:

    #AI->H::Question: (How do they prefer to consume
        content? Long-form articles? Quick videos?
        Detailed documentation? Interactive tools?
        This shapes our content strategy.)

    #AI->H::Question: (What is their tolerance for
        communication frequency? Daily updates?
        Weekly digest? Only when essential? This
        informs our engagement cadence.)

{PERSONA_NAME} Behavioral Synthesis:

    After gathering behavioral data, provide:
        - Channel priorities: "Reach them through
          [channels] because [reason]"
        - Content strategy: "They prefer [format]
          content at [frequency]"
        - Competitive context: "Currently using
          [solutions] with [frustrations]"
        - Decision path: "Buy decision takes [time]
          involving [stakeholders]"

# =========================================================
# STEP 6: PERSONA CONSTRUCTION
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Building detailed persona profiles from
    gathered insights)

{PERSONA_NAME} Persona Framework:

    For each persona (1 to {number_of_personas}):

    Generate persona profile structure:

=============================================================
PERSONA {N}: {PERSONA_NAME_N}
{Descriptive tagline}
=============================================================

    Demographics:
        - Name: [Realistic name for reference]
        - Age: [Age or range]
        - Role: [Job title or life role]
        - Location: [Geographic context]
        - Education: [Level and relevance]
        - Income/Budget: [Range or description]

    IF B2B:
        - Company Size: [Employee range]
        - Industry: [Sector]
        - Decision Authority: [Level]

    Psychographics:
        - Core Values: [2-3 primary values]
        - Goals: [Immediate and aspirational]
        - Fears: [What keeps them up at night]
        - Risk Tolerance: [Low/Medium/High + context]
        - Decision Style: [How they decide]
        - Identity: [How they see themselves]

    Behaviors:
        - Information Sources: [Where they learn]
        - Trusted Voices: [Who they believe]
        - Buying Triggers: [What prompts action]
        - Decision Timeline: [How long]
        - Current Solutions: [What they use now]
        - Key Frustrations: [Pain points]

    Pain Points:
        - Primary Challenge: [Main problem]
        - Secondary Challenges: [2-3 additional]
        - Current Solution Gaps: [What is not working]
        - Friction Points: [Specific frustrations]

    Day-in-the-Life Scenario:
        [Narrative paragraph showing typical workflow
        or day, highlighting where pain points emerge
        and where your solution fits]

    Persona Quote:
        "[Authentic quote capturing their mindset,
        frustration, or aspiration - in their voice]"

    Strategic Implications:
        - Brand Messaging: [How to speak to them]
        - Value Proposition: [What resonates most]
        - Channels: [Where to reach them]
        - Content Type: [What format works]
        - Objections to Address: [Likely concerns]

=============================================================

{PERSONA_NAME} Confidence Rating for Each Persona:

    "Persona Accuracy: [percentage]% confidence this
    accurately represents your target

    Based on: [data sources used - research, interview
    insights, market knowledge, assumptions]

    Gaps: [any areas where more data would strengthen
    profile]"

# =========================================================
# STEP 7: ANTI-PERSONA (IF REQUESTED)
# =========================================================

IF include_anti_persona == True:

    #AI->H::Status: (Defining anti-persona - who you are
        explicitly NOT targeting)

    {PERSONA_NAME} Anti-Persona Framework:

        "An anti-persona sharpens positioning by defining
        who is a poor fit. This is not about discrimination
        - it is about focus and resource allocation. Let
        us identify who would struggle to succeed with
        your solution."

    #AI->H::Question: (Think about users who might seem
        like prospects but would actually be poor fits.
        What characteristics make someone wrong for your
        solution? Too large/small? Wrong use case?
        Misaligned expectations?)

    Generate anti-persona structure:

=============================================================

        - Red flag 3: [Identifiable characteristic]

        - Positioning sharpened: [Clarity gained]

        [Specific copy that self-selects them out]

        Example: "Built for small teams who value
        simplicity, not enterprises requiring custom
        integrations"

=============================================================

    {PERSONA_NAME} Anti-Persona Strategic Value:

        "This anti-persona helps you:
            - Say NO to feature requests that do not
              serve your core audience
            - Avoid marketing channels where they
              congregate
            - Create messaging that self-selects the
              right people
            - Protect resources from support-intensive
              mismatches

        attract our anti-persona? If yes, reconsider.'"

ELSE:

        later feel messaging is too broad or attracting

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe uses the context block from the
   Brand Context Initializer (RCP-004-001-001), or
   equivalent user-provided business context. It can run
   standalone when the user supplies comprehensive context
   directly.

2. PERSONA FLEXIBILITY: The recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME}
   variable pattern. Default is Morgan (Strategic Brand
   Architect); it adapts to any BRAND_PERSONA object
   provided.

3. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: The Persona Profiles and Audience
   Insight Summary feed the Pain Point Identifier
   (RCP-004-001-003), Value Prop Crafter (RCP-004-001-004),
   Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005), Elevator
   Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006), and Brand Profile
   Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007).

4. STEREOTYPE GUARD: The recipe emphasizes behaviors and
   motivations over demographics. Use demographic data as
   context, not constraints. The persona quote and day-in-
   the-life scenario humanize beyond statistics.

5. MULTIPLE PERSONAS: Create multiple personas only if
   segments have genuinely different needs, behaviors, or
   decision processes. If they differ only slightly, one
   persona with noted variations is cleaner (max 3).

6. CONFIDENCE TARGETS: 70%+ is actionable for early-stage
   businesses; 80%+ is ideal for significant investment
   decisions; 90%+ requires substantial research data.
   Lower confidence is fine if you plan to validate.

7. LIVING PERSONAS: Personas should evolve with market
   data. Re-run after beta launch, customer interviews, or
   significant market learning.
