# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-001-003-PAIN-POINT-ID

Description: Identifies specific problems, frustrations,
and unmet needs of the target audience through strategic
questioning. Analyzes severity and impact, maps the current
solution landscape, and connects pain points to your
offering. Produces a prioritized pain point summary for
value proposition development. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (the
brand strategist bundled with this cookbook) to guide the
discovery and analysis.


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 001

Recipe ID Numbers: 003

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Foundation

Recipe Tags:
    pain-points, customer-problems, frustrations,
    unmet-needs, problem-discovery, solution-mapping,
    competitive-analysis, value-proposition-input,
    emotional-analysis, prioritization

Recipe Recommended Personas: Morgan (Strategic Brand
    Architect) - bundled default; carried forward from
    Target Audience Analyzer (RCP-004-001-002)

Recipe Difficulty: Intermediate


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories including user
    research data with personal information, competitive
    intelligence, health or medical pain points, and
    financial stress topics. If sensitive content detected,
    note that pain point research may involve sensitive
    user data and maintain confidentiality while focusing
    on strategic brand insights. For health or medical
    contexts, focus on practical challenges rather than
    clinical advice.


STEP 0.5: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Brand Foundation
    persona, Morgan (Strategic Brand Architect), carried
    forward from the Target Audience Analyzer recipe
    (RCP-004-001-002). The persona object is stored in
    PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default.

    IF BRAND_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Morgan (Strategic
        Brand Architect). Morgan works through strategic
        questioning, framework thinking, and empathy
        balanced with analysis - digging beneath surface
        symptoms to root frustrations and rating confidence
        transparently.


STEP 1: Context Loading and Validation

    Load and verify required inputs from previous recipes.
    Parse the context block from Brand Context Initializer
    (RCP-004-001-001) for business name, stage, goals, and
    constraints. Parse the audience profile from Target
    Audience Analyzer (RCP-004-001-002) for persona details
    including demographics, psychographics, and behaviors.
    If either input is missing, request it before
    proceeding. Note any research sources provided for
    validation. Assess stage-specific pain-point focus
    (pre-launch validates assumed pain; beta surfaces actual
    friction; launched targets conversion/retention
    barriers; growth targets scaling pressures).


STEP 2: Depth Calibration

    Calibrate analysis based on the selected depth mode.
    Quick mode (25 minutes) focuses on the top 3 pain points
    with 5-7 questions. Standard mode (45 minutes) provides
    comprehensive exploration of 5-7 pain points with
    10-15 questions across categories. Comprehensive mode
    (60 minutes) delivers a deep dive into 7-10 pain points
    with competitive analysis and 20+ questions.


STEP 3: Pain Point Discovery Questions

    Conduct strategic questioning across pain point
    categories, scaled to the depth mode. Workflow and
    process pain points cover where users get stuck,
    repetitive tasks, and coordination challenges. Tool and
    technology pain points cover current tools, limitations,
    tool sprawl, and complexity barriers. Knowledge and
    capability pain points cover skill gaps, inconsistent
    results, and blank-page syndrome. Emotional pain points
    (if enabled) cover stress, overwhelm, imposter syndrome,
    and confidence issues. Business impact pain points cover
    outcomes and missed opportunities. Comprehensive mode
    adds extended competitive analysis (solutions already
    tried and why they failed), deep emotional exploration
    (worst-case scenarios, reputation impact), market-trend
    questions (is the pain worsening; emerging unaddressed
    pain), and quantitative assessment (time/money cost).


STEP 4: Pain Point Categorization and Scoring

    Organize discovered pain points into a structured
    framework. For each pain point, document: name with
    descriptive label, category (workflow, tool, knowledge,
    emotional, business), 2-3 sentence description,
    frequency rating (daily=10, weekly=7, monthly=4,
    occasional=2), severity rating (critical=10,
    significant=7, moderate=4, minor=2), emotional impact
    (if analysis enabled), current solution, and solution
    gap. Calculate PRIORITY_SCORE = frequency + severity
    (+ emotional if applicable); maximum 30 with emotional,
    20 without. Rank pain points, then bin into a priority
    matrix: CRITICAL (24-30 / 17-20) for hero messaging,
    HIGH (18-23 / 13-16) for strong supporting messages,
    MEDIUM (12-17 / 8-12) for mention-if-relevant, LOW
    (below 12 / 8) which may not warrant messaging focus.
    Present the ranked Pain Point Priority Matrix table.


STEP 5: Current Solution Landscape Analysis

    Map existing solutions for each CRITICAL and HIGH pain
    point. Document what solutions currently exist
    (competitors, workarounds, manual processes, nothing)
    with strengths and weaknesses. Identify why current
    solutions fail and classify the market gap as
    underserved (no good solutions), over-complicated
    (exist but too complex/expensive), fragmented (multiple
    tools, no integrated approach), or wrong-tradeoffs
    (solve A but create B). Surface the biggest strategic
    opportunity with a rationale and confidence rating
    (70-90%).


STEP 6: Solution Alignment Mapping

    Connect prioritized pain points to your offering. For
    each CRITICAL and HIGH pain point, map how your solution
    addresses it, the unique advantage you provide, the
    evidence or proof that exists, and coverage (directly
    addressed, partially addressed, or not addressed). Then
    generate a messaging priority recommendation by
    combining pain-point severity (scoring), solution
    strength (alignment), and competitive gap size
    (landscape): PRIMARY (lead - critical + strong solution
    + large gap), SECONDARY (support), and TERTIARY (mention
    if relevant). Be transparent about partial solutions and
    flag unaddressed pain points as scope or development
    decisions.


STEP 7: Pain Point Summary Block Creation

    Generate a copy-paste ready summary block for use in
    Value Proposition Crafter (RCP-004-001-004). Include
    target audience reference, critical pain points with
    full details (problem, impact, current solution, your
    solution, confidence), high-priority pain points with
    brief details, solution gaps as competitive advantages,
    messaging priorities ranked, and emotional hooks for
    copywriting (before and after states).


STEP 8: Validation and Confidence Assessment

    Provide an honest confidence assessment for all pain
    point identifications. Rate research-backed pain points
    higher (85-95%) than persona-inferred pain points
    (70-80%) and assumed pain points (60-70%). Note any
    assumptions made and areas needing validation. Recommend
    specific validation actions such as user interviews,
    customer surveys, support-ticket analysis, or competitor
    review monitoring.


STEP 9: Completion and Next Steps

    Deliver a summary of all outputs including the pain
    point summary block, priority matrix, solution alignment
    map, and confidence assessment. Confirm what has been
    established about audience pain points (what frustrates
    them, how much it hurts, what they use now, where you
    fit, what to say). Provide strategic guidance for the
    next recipe, Value Proposition Crafter
    (RCP-004-001-004), and ask whether the user wants to
    proceed or refine any aspect of the pain point analysis.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: What if I do not have research data on pain points?

A: The recipe works with or without research. Without
   research, {PERSONA_NAME} relies on persona insights
   from Target Audience Analyzer (RCP-004-001-002) and
   strategic questioning. Confidence ratings will be lower
   (70-80%) and validation is strongly recommended before
   finalizing messaging.

Q: How many pain points should I identify?

A: Focus on 3-5 critical and high-priority pain points.
   More than 7 dilutes messaging focus. Quick mode
   identifies 3, standard mode 5-7, comprehensive mode
   7-10 with deeper analysis on top priorities.

Q: Should I include emotional pain points?

A: Yes for B2C and relationship-driven B2B. Emotional
   hooks are powerful in marketing copy. For technical
   B2B, balance emotional with practical. The parameter
   allows you to disable if purely rational positioning.

Q: What if my solution does not address the top pain
   points?

A: This is valuable strategic insight. Either adjust
   your offering to address critical pain points, or
   reposition to lead with pain points you DO address
   well. Honest assessment prevents messaging that
   overpromises.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Morgan (Strategic Brand
   Architect) as the default for the Brand Foundation
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona
   file; the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable
   throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe discovers and prioritizes target audience
pain points through strategic questioning guided by
{PERSONA_NAME}. The AI should adapt question depth based
on the selected depth mode parameter.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for sensitive user data,
   competitive intelligence, or health/financial topics.

2. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Morgan (Strategic
   Brand Architect) carried from the Target Audience
   Analyzer recipe. Load BRAND_PERSONA if available, else
   activate the bundled Morgan default.

3. CONTEXT LOADING: Load the context block (RCP-004-001-001)
   and audience profile (RCP-004-001-002); halt and request
   either if missing.

4. DEPTH CALIBRATION: Set question quantity and category
   coverage from the depth_mode parameter.

5. PAIN POINT DISCOVERY: Question across workflow, tool,
   knowledge, emotional, and business categories; B2B vs
   B2C context shapes emphasis.

6. SCORING: Calculate priority scores (frequency + severity
   + optional emotional) and rank into the priority matrix.

7. SOLUTION LANDSCAPE: Map competitive solutions and
   classify the market gap type.

8. SOLUTION ALIGNMENT: Connect pain points to the offering
   and derive the messaging hierarchy.

9. SUMMARY BLOCK: Emit the PAIN_POINT_SUMMARY_BLOCK for the
   downstream value-proposition recipe.

10. VALIDATION + NEXT STEPS: Rate confidence honestly and
    bridge to Value Proposition Crafter (RCP-004-001-004).

Pain point discovery follows a hierarchy:
    - Level 1: Surface symptoms (what users say)
    - Level 2: Functional problems (practical challenges)
    - Level 3: Emotional impact (how it makes them feel)
    - Level 4: Root causes (why the problem exists)

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Context block (Brand Context Initializer,
      RCP-004-001-001)
    - Audience profile (Target Audience Analyzer,
      RCP-004-001-002)
    - Research sources (optional - enhances confidence)

FEEDS INTO:
    - Value Proposition Crafter (RCP-004-001-004) -
      CRITICAL INPUT
    - Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005)
    - Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006)
    - Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007)

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is the PAIN_POINT_SUMMARY_BLOCK containing
target audience reference, critical and high-priority pain
points, solution gaps, ranked messaging priorities, and
emotional hooks. Secondary outputs include the Priority
Matrix, Solution Alignment Map, and Confidence Assessment.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Identifies and prioritizes target audience pain points
through strategic questioning. Maps current solutions,
analyzes competitive gaps, and connects pain points to
your offering. Produces a summary block for value
proposition development. Guided by {PERSONA_NAME}.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe as the third step in brand development
after completing Brand Context Initializer
(RCP-004-001-001) and Target Audience Analyzer
(RCP-004-001-002). The pain point understanding developed
here is critical input for:
    - Value Proposition Crafter (RCP-004-001-004) -
      direct input
    - Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005) -
      gap analysis
    - Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006) -
      problem framing
    - Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007) -
      messaging foundation

Also use when validating assumptions about customer
problems, refining positioning after market feedback,
or preparing for messaging updates.

PREREQUISITES:
    - Context Block (RCP-004-001-001)
    - Audience Profile (RCP-004-001-002)
    - Research sources (optional)

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Target Audience Analyzer (RCP-004-001-002)
    - Precedes: Value Proposition Crafter (RCP-004-001-004)
    - Feeds: Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005),
      Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006), Brand
      Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: Fine Dining Restaurant (Standard Mode)

    Parameters:
        - context_block: Terra and Olive (Mediterranean
          farm-to-table, pre-launch, fine dining)
        - audience_profile: Sofia the Food Enthusiast,
          Marcus the Business Host (from RCP-004-001-002)
        - depth_mode: standard
        - focus_area: all
        - include_emotional_analysis: True

    Output:

    Critical Pain Points (Score 24-30):
        1. "Finding Authentic Experiences" (26/30)
           Problem: Diners frustrated by restaurants
           that promise authenticity but deliver generic
           food. Chain restaurants feel soulless.
           Impact: Daily decision, high frustration
           Current: Read reviews obsessively, often
           disappointed
           Your Solution: True farm-to-table sourcing,
           chef story, ingredient provenance
           Confidence: 85%

        2. "Special Occasion Anxiety" (25/30)
           Problem: Fear of choosing wrong restaurant
           for important celebrations or client dinners.
           Impact: Monthly, high stakes
           Current: Ask friends, check multiple review
           sites, still uncertain
           Your Solution: Consistent quality, private
           dining, reliable service
           Confidence: 80%

    High Priority Pain Points (Score 20-23):
        3. "Reservation Frustration" (22/30)
        4. "Menu Uncertainty" (21/30)

    Competitive Gap: No local fine dining emphasizes
    ingredient story and chef connection at mid-premium
    price point.

    Messaging Priority:
        - Lead with: Authentic Mediterranean experience
        - Support with: Perfect for special occasions
        - Mention: Easy online reservations

    {PERSONA_NAME} Analysis: "Food enthusiasts crave
    authenticity they cannot find. Business hosts need
    reliability they can trust. Position Terra and Olive
    as the answer to both."


Example 2: Environmental Consulting (Standard Mode)

    Parameters:
        - context_block: GreenPath Solutions
          (environmental consulting, beta stage, B2B)
        - audience_profile: Dana the Sustainability
          Director (from RCP-004-001-002)
        - depth_mode: standard
        - focus_area: all
        - include_emotional_analysis: True

    Output:

    Critical Pain Points:
        1. "Board-Ready Reporting Gap" (27/30)
           Problem: Sustainability directors struggle to
           translate environmental data into business
           metrics executives understand.
           Impact: Quarterly, career-affecting
           Current: Manual report creation, often
           challenged by CFO
           Your Solution: Automated executive dashboards,
           ROI frameworks
           Confidence: 90%

        2. "Regulatory Uncertainty" (25/30)
           Problem: Constantly changing environmental
           regulations create compliance anxiety.
           Your Solution: Regulatory monitoring and
           guidance

    Competitive Gap: Existing consultants focus on
    compliance, not business case translation.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Analysis: "Dana needs to look
    competent to leadership. Position GreenPath as
    making sustainability directors look like heroes."


Example 3: Meeting Assistant SaaS (Quick Mode)

    Parameters:
        - context_block: MeetingFlow (AI meeting
          assistant, growth stage, B2B SaaS)
        - audience_profile: Brandon the Remote Manager
        - depth_mode: quick
        - research_sources: User feedback survey (n=150)
        - focus_area: primary_only
        - include_emotional_analysis: False

    Output:

    Top 3 Pain Points (Quick Analysis):
        1. "Meeting Note Overload" - HIGH severity
           Validated by survey (78% cited this)
           Your Solution: Automated summaries

        2. "Action Item Tracking Failure" - HIGH severity
           Validated by survey (65% cited this)
           Your Solution: AI action extraction

        3. "Meeting Prep Time Waste" - MEDIUM severity
           New insight from survey
           Your Solution: Pre-meeting briefs (partial)

    Quick Prioritization:
        - Lead with: Pain #1 (most frequent + highest
          impact)
        - Support with: Pain #2 (strong solution fit)
        - Mention: Pain #3 (developing feature)

    Confidence: 75% (survey data, limited sample)

    {PERSONA_NAME} Quick Note: "Survey validates top
    two pain points. Update website hero to emphasize
    pain #1. Ready for quick Value Proposition Crafter
    execution."

# =========================================================
# START RECIPE-ID: RCP-004-001-003-PAIN-POINT-ID-v3.00a
# =========================================================


# =========================================================
# PERSONA CONFIGURATION
# =========================================================

# Default Brand Persona - stored in PROJECT_VARIABLES for
# persistence across the Brand Foundation section. Carried
# forward from Brand Context Initializer / Target Audience
# Analyzer. Users may attach a custom persona to override.
# This cookbook bundles the tier-less Morgan
# (PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MORGAN-CARD.txt).

IF BRAND_PERSONA not in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
    Load the bundled default:
        BRAND_PERSONA = {
            "name": "Morgan",
            "title": "Strategic Brand Architect",
            "greeting": "Let us dig into what truly
                frustrates your audience - that is where
                authentic brand messaging begins.",
            "methodology": "Strategic questioning ->
                Categorize -> Prioritize -> Map Solutions",
            "file_reference":
                "PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MORGAN-CARD.txt"
        }
ELSE:
    Load from PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        BRAND_PERSONA = PROJECT_VARIABLES["BRAND_PERSONA"]

PERSONA_NAME = BRAND_PERSONA["name"]
PERSONA_TITLE = BRAND_PERSONA["title"]
PERSONA_GREETING = BRAND_PERSONA["greeting"]
PERSONA_METHODOLOGY = BRAND_PERSONA["methodology"]


# =========================================================
# RECIPE DEFINITION
# =========================================================

PAIN_POINT_IDENTIFIER = Recipe(
    recipe_id="RCP-004-001-003-PAIN-POINT-ID-v3.00a",
    title="Pain Point Identifier",
    description="""
        Identifies specific problems, frustrations, and
        unmet needs of the target audience through
        strategic questioning. Analyzes severity and
        impact, maps the current solution landscape, and
        connects pain points to your offering. Produces a
        prioritized pain point summary for value
        proposition development. Activates {PERSONA_NAME}
        (Strategic Brand Architect) to guide the work.
    """,
    category="CAT-004-BRAND-IDENTITY",
    subcategory="SUBCAT-001-FOUNDATION",
    difficulty="intermediate",
    estimated_time="25-60 minutes (varies by depth)",
    version="3.00a",

    dependencies={
        "required_inputs": [
            {
                "source": "RCP-004-001-001-BRAND-CONTEXT-INIT",
                "input": "context_block",
                "description": "Business name, stage, goals,
                    and constraints from Brand Context
                    Initializer"
            },
            {
                "source": "RCP-004-001-002-TARGET-AUDIENCE",
                "input": "audience_profile",
                "description": "Target personas with
                    demographics, psychographics, and
                    behaviors from Target Audience Analyzer"
            }
        ],
        "optional_inputs": [
            {
                "source": "Research Sources",
                "input": "research_sources",
                "description": "Survey/interview/analytics
                    files that raise confidence"
            }
        ],
        "feeds_into": [
            "RCP-004-001-004 (Value Proposition Crafter) - CRITICAL INPUT",
            "RCP-004-001-005 (Competitive Edge Definer)",
            "RCP-004-001-006 (Elevator Pitch Builder)",
            "RCP-004-001-007 (Brand Profile Synthesizer)"
        ]
    },

    parameters={
        "context_block": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": True,
            "description": "Context from RCP-004-001-001",
            "example": "Business context block"
        },
        "audience_profile": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": True,
            "description": "Personas from RCP-004-001-002",
            "example": "Detailed persona profiles"
        },
        "depth_mode": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": False,
            "default": "standard",
            "options": [
                "quick",
                "standard",
                "comprehensive"
            ],
            "description": "Analysis depth level"
        },
        "research_sources": {
            "type": "list",
            "required": False,
            "default": [],
            "description": "Research files to incorporate"
        },
        "focus_area": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": False,
            "default": "all",
            "options": [
                "all",
                "primary_only",
                "specific_category"
            ],
            "description": "Pain point scope"
        },
        "include_emotional_analysis": {
            "type": "boolean",
            "required": False,
            "default": True,
            "description": "Include emotional dimension"
        }
    },

    prompt_template="""

#H->AI::Directive: (Execute Pain Point Identifier)
#H->AI::Context: (Building on audience understanding to
    identify specific problems)

# =========================================================
# STEP 0: POLICY PRE-CHECK
# =========================================================

Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
    - User research data (personal information)
    - Competitive intelligence
    - Health/medical pain points
    - Financial stress/struggles

IF sensitive content detected:
    #AI->H::PolicyCaution: (Pain point research may
        involve sensitive user data)
    #AI->H::Note: (Will maintain confidentiality and
        focus on strategic brand insights)

IF health/medical context:
    #AI->H::PolicyNote: (Medical context detected -
        will focus on practical challenges, not
        clinical advice)

# =========================================================
# STEP 0.5: PERSONA CONTINUATION
# =========================================================

#AI->H::PersonaSwitch: ({PERSONA_NAME} continuing from
    Target Audience Analyzer)

{PERSONA_NAME} approach for pain point discovery:
    - Strategic questioning: "What is the real
      frustration beneath the surface symptom?"
    - Framework thinking: Categorize, Prioritize,
      Map Solutions
    - Empathy balanced with analysis: Understand
      emotion, but focus on actionable insights
    - Confidence transparency: Rate certainty of
      pain point severity assessments

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} here. Let us dig into
    what truly frustrates your audience. Understanding
    pain points is where authentic brand messaging
    begins. I will help you prioritize which problems
    matter most and how your offering addresses them.)

# =========================================================
# STEP 1: CONTEXT LOADING AND VALIDATION
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Loading context from previous recipes)

Verify Required Inputs:

1. Context Block from Brand Context Initializer
   (RCP-004-001-001):

    IF context_block provided:
        Parse business_name, stage, goals, constraints
        #AI->H::Note: (Context loaded: {business_name}
            at {stage} stage)

    ELSE:
        #AI->H::RequiredQuestion: (I need the context
            block from Brand Context Initializer
            (RCP-004-001-001). Please provide business
            name, stage, immediate goals, and constraints,
            or execute that recipe first.)
        HALT until provided

2. Audience Profile from Target Audience Analyzer
   (RCP-004-001-002):

    IF audience_profile provided:
        Parse persona(s): demographics, psychographics,
            behaviors, goals
        #AI->H::Note: (Audience profile loaded:
            {persona_count} persona(s) identified)

    ELSE:
        #AI->H::RequiredQuestion: (I need the audience
            profile from Target Audience Analyzer
            (RCP-004-001-002). Please provide target
            persona details or execute that recipe first.)
        HALT until provided

3. Research Sources:

    IF research_sources provided:
        #AI->H::Note: ({count} research source(s)
            available for validation)
    ELSE:
        #AI->H::Note: (No additional research provided -
            will rely on persona insights and strategic
            questioning)

Strategic Context Assessment:

    Based on loaded context, identify focus areas:

    #AI->H::StrategyNote: (
        Business Stage: {stage}
        Key Consideration: {stage_specific_focus}

        Stage-specific pain point focus:
        - Pre-launch/Concept: Validate assumed pain
          points
        - Beta: Focus on actual user feedback and
          friction points
        - Launched: Focus on conversion barriers and
          retention challenges
        - Growth: Focus on scaling pain points and
          competitive pressures
    )

# =========================================================
# STEP 2: DEPTH CALIBRATION
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Calibrating analysis depth:
    {depth_mode})

{PERSONA_NAME} Depth Framework:

IF depth_mode == "quick":
    Focus: Top 3 most critical pain points
    Questions: 5-7 essential questions
    Time: 25 minutes
    Output: Streamlined pain point summary

    #AI->H::Note: (Quick mode: Focusing on top 3 most
        critical pain points for rapid validation.)

IF depth_mode == "standard":
    Focus: 5-7 pain points across categories
    Questions: 10-15 strategic questions
    Time: 45 minutes
    Output: Comprehensive pain point analysis

    #AI->H::Note: (Standard mode: Comprehensive
        exploration across pain point categories.)

IF depth_mode == "comprehensive":
    Focus: 7-10 pain points with competitive analysis
    Questions: 20+ strategic questions
    Time: 60 minutes
    Output: Deep strategic analysis with gaps

    #AI->H::Note: (Comprehensive mode: Deep dive with
        competitive landscape analysis.)

# =========================================================
# STEP 3: PAIN POINT DISCOVERY - QUICK MODE
# =========================================================

IF depth_mode == "quick":

    {PERSONA_NAME} Essential Questions:

    1. Primary Frustration:
        #AI->H::Question: (When your target audience
            ({persona_name}) tries to {primary_goal},
            what is the biggest obstacle or frustration
            they encounter?)

    2. Current Workarounds:
        #AI->H::Question: (How are they currently
            attempting to solve this problem? What
            solution are they using, and why is it not
            working well?)

    3. Impact Assessment:
        #AI->H::Question: (On a scale of minor annoyance
            to critical blocker, how severe is this
            problem for them? What happens if they do
            not solve it?)

    4. Secondary Pain Point:
        #AI->H::Question: (What is the second most
            significant challenge they face in this
            area?)

    5. Emotional Response:
        IF include_emotional_analysis == True:
            #AI->H::Question: (How does this problem
                make them feel? Stressed, overwhelmed,
                frustrated, confused, anxious?)

    6. Validation Check:
        #AI->H::Question: (Based on your research or
            user interactions, how confident are you
            that this is a genuine, widespread pain
            point? Rate 1-10.)

    7. Connection to Your Offering:
        #AI->H::Question: (How does your product or
            service address this specific pain point?)

# =========================================================
# STEP 4: PAIN POINT DISCOVERY - STANDARD MODE
# =========================================================

IF depth_mode == "standard":

    {PERSONA_NAME} conducts systematic discovery:

    Category 1: Workflow and Process Pain Points

        #AI->H::Question: (Walk me through your
            audience typical workflow when dealing with
            {relevant_task}. Where do they get stuck
            or slow down?)

        #AI->H::Question: (What repetitive tasks or
            inefficiencies frustrate them most?)

        #AI->H::Question: (Are there handoffs,
            dependencies, or coordination challenges
            that create friction?)

    Category 2: Tool and Technology Pain Points

        #AI->H::Question: (What tools or platforms are
            they currently using? What limitations or
            problems do these create?)

        #AI->H::Question: (Do they experience tool
            sprawl - too many disconnected tools? How
            does this impact their work?)

        #AI->H::Question: (Are there technical barriers
            such as learning curves, complexity, or
            unreliability?)

    Category 3: Knowledge and Capability Pain Points

        #AI->H::Question: (What knowledge gaps or skill
            deficiencies hold them back?)

        #AI->H::Question: (Do they struggle with
            inconsistent results or lack of
            reproducibility?)

        #AI->H::Question: (Is there a blank page
            syndrome - not knowing where to start?)

    Category 4: Emotional Pain Points

        IF include_emotional_analysis == True:

            #AI->H::Question: (What causes them stress,
                anxiety, or overwhelm in this domain?)

            #AI->H::Question: (Do they experience
                imposter syndrome, fear of mistakes,
                or lack of confidence?)

    Category 5: Business Impact Pain Points

        #AI->H::Question: (How do these problems impact
            their business outcomes, career, or goals?)

        #AI->H::Question: (What opportunities are they
            missing because of these challenges?)

    Validation and Prioritization:

        #AI->H::Question: (Of all the pain points we
            have discussed, which 3-5 are most severe
            and most common?)

        #AI->H::Question: (For each top pain point,
            rate: How frequent - daily, weekly, monthly?
            How impactful - minor, moderate, severe?)

# =========================================================
# STEP 5: PAIN POINT DISCOVERY - COMPREHENSIVE MODE
# =========================================================

IF depth_mode == "comprehensive":

    Include ALL standard mode questions PLUS:

    Extended Competitive Analysis:

        #AI->H::Question: (For each major pain point,
            what solutions have they already tried?
            Why did those solutions fail or fall short?)

        #AI->H::Question: (What competitors or
            alternatives are they aware of? What do they
            think of them?)

        #AI->H::Question: (Are there solutions they
            have rejected? Why?)

    Deep Emotional Exploration:

        #AI->H::Question: (What is the worst case
            scenario if this pain point is not resolved?
            What keeps them up at night?)

        #AI->H::Question: (How does this problem affect
            their professional identity or reputation?)

    Market Trend Questions:

        #AI->H::Question: (Is this pain point getting
            worse over time? What trends are making it
            more acute?)

        #AI->H::Question: (Are there emerging pain
            points that competitors are not yet
            addressing?)

    Quantitative Assessment:

        #AI->H::Question: (Can you estimate the time or
            money cost of this pain point? Hours wasted
            per week? Revenue lost?)

# =========================================================
# STEP 6: PAIN POINT CATEGORIZATION AND SCORING
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Categorizing and scoring discovered
    pain points)

{PERSONA_NAME} Scoring Framework:

For each pain point identified:

    PAIN_POINT_PROFILE = {
        "name": "[Descriptive label]",
        "category": "[workflow/tool/knowledge/emotional/
            business]",
        "description": "[2-3 sentence problem statement]",
        "frequency": {
            "rating": "[daily/weekly/monthly/occasional]",
            "score": "[10/7/4/2]"
        },
        "severity": {
            "rating": "[critical/significant/moderate/
                minor]",
            "score": "[10/7/4/2]"
        },
        "emotional_impact": "[If analysis enabled]",
        "current_solution": "[What exists now]",
        "solution_gap": "[Why current solution fails]"
    }

    PRIORITY_SCORE = frequency_score + severity_score
        + (emotional_score if applicable)

    Maximum Score: 30 (with emotional) or 20 (without)

Priority Ranking Matrix:

    CRITICAL (Score 24-30 or 17-20):
        - Must address in core messaging
        - Hero value proposition material

    HIGH (Score 18-23 or 13-16):
        - Strong supporting messages
        - Feature highlight material

    MEDIUM (Score 12-17 or 8-12):
        - Mention if relevant
        - Secondary content material

    LOW (Score below 12 or 8):
        - May not warrant messaging focus
        - Consider for future development

#AI->H::Deliverable: (Pain Point Priority Matrix)

Present ranked pain points:

    +---------------------------------------------------+
    |           PAIN POINT PRIORITY MATRIX              |
    +---------------------------------------------------+
    | Rank | Pain Point          | Score | Priority    |
    +------+---------------------+-------+-------------+
    | 1    | [Name]              | XX/30 | CRITICAL    |
    | 2    | [Name]              | XX/30 | CRITICAL    |
    | 3    | [Name]              | XX/30 | HIGH        |
    | 4    | [Name]              | XX/30 | HIGH        |
    | 5    | [Name]              | XX/30 | MEDIUM      |
    +---------------------------------------------------+

# =========================================================
# STEP 7: CURRENT SOLUTION LANDSCAPE ANALYSIS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Mapping competitive landscape for each
    pain point)

{PERSONA_NAME} Competitive Analysis:

For each CRITICAL and HIGH pain point:

    SOLUTION_LANDSCAPE = {
        "pain_point": "[Name]",
        "current_solutions": [
            {
                "solution": "[Competitor/Workaround]",
                "strengths": "[What it does well]",
                "weaknesses": "[Why it fails]"
            }
        ],
        "market_gap_type": "[underserved/overcomplicated/
            fragmented/wrong_tradeoffs]"
    }

Market Gap Identification:

    {PERSONA_NAME} identifies patterns:

    Gap Type 1 - Underserved Pain Points:
        Problems with no good solutions

    Gap Type 2 - Over-Complicated Solutions:
        Solutions exist but too complex or expensive

    Gap Type 3 - Fragmented Solutions:
        Need multiple tools, no integrated approach

    Gap Type 4 - Wrong Trade-offs:
        Solutions that solve A but create problem B

#AI->H::StrategyNote: (
    Your biggest opportunity: [Type of gap]
    Rationale: [Why this represents strategic advantage]
    Confidence: [70-90%]
)

# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Connecting pain points to your offering)

    SOLUTION_ALIGNMENT = {
        "pain_point": "[Name]",
        "severity": "[CRITICAL/HIGH]",
        "your_solution": "[How you address this]",
        "unique_advantage": "[Why you are better]",
        "evidence_proof": "[Validation this works]",
        "coverage": "[direct/partial/none]"
    }

Coverage Analysis:

    Directly Addressed:
        [List pain points you fully solve]

    Partially Addressed:
        [List pain points you partly solve]

    Not Addressed:
        [List pain points outside your scope]

#AI->H::StrategyNote: (Focus messaging on pain points
    you directly address. For partial solutions, be
    transparent about limitations. For unaddressed
    pain points, consider: Are they outside your scope
    intentionally, or opportunities for development?)

Messaging Priority Recommendation:

    Based on:
        1. Pain point severity (from scoring)
        2. Your solution strength (from alignment)
        3. Competitive gap size (from landscape)

    PRIMARY MESSAGING (Lead with these):
        [Pain Point X]: Critical + Strong Solution +
            Large Gap = Hero Message

    SECONDARY MESSAGING (Support with these):
        [Pain Point Y]: High Priority + Good Solution +
            Moderate Gap

    TERTIARY MESSAGING (Mention if relevant):
        [Pain Point Z]: Medium Priority + Partial
            Solution

#AI->H::BestGuess::ConfidenceLevel:85%: (Messaging
    hierarchy based on strategic fit analysis)

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires the context block from
   Brand Context Initializer (RCP-004-001-001) and the
   audience profile from Target Audience Analyzer
   (RCP-004-001-002). Request either if missing before
   proceeding.

2. MULTIPLE PERSONAS: If pain points differ significantly
   between personas, run a separate pain point analysis for
   each distinct persona. The summary block supports
   multiple personas; document which pain points apply to
   which persona for targeted messaging.

3. CONFLICTING RESEARCH AND ASSUMPTIONS: Research takes
   precedence. Note the conflict in the confidence
   assessment and recommend validation to resolve.
   {PERSONA_NAME} flags when persona-inferred pain points
   conflict with research data.

4. SOLUTIONS THAT CREATE NEW PAIN: Honest assessment is
   valuable. Document trade-offs in the solution alignment
   map. Some solutions solve A but create B - position
   messaging to acknowledge trade-offs when appropriate.

5. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: The Pain Point Summary Block is
   critical input for Value Proposition Crafter
   (RCP-004-001-004) and also feeds Competitive Edge
   Definer (RCP-004-001-005), Elevator Pitch Builder
   (RCP-004-001-006), and Brand Profile Synthesizer
   (RCP-004-001-007).

6. VALIDATION: Rate research-backed pain points higher than
   persona-inferred ones and recommend specific validation
   actions for lower-confidence identifications.

# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-001-004-VALUE-PROP

Description: Creates compelling unique value propositions
that differentiate your offering and resonate with the
target audience. Synthesizes insights from context,
audience, and pain points to generate multiple UVP
variations across different styles. Provides feature-benefit
mapping, component breakdowns, and resonance assessment.
Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (the brand strategist bundled with
this cookbook) to guide the work.


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 001

Recipe ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Brand Foundation

Recipe Tags:
    value-proposition, uvp, unique-value, differentiation,
    messaging, positioning, benefit-mapping, brand-message,
    feature-benefits, copywriting

Recipe Recommended Personas: Morgan (Strategic Brand
    Architect) - bundled default; hands off to the
    Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005) for
    positioning depth

Recipe Difficulty: Intermediate


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories: competitive
    claims that must be substantiated, superlative claims
    (best, only, number one), health or medical benefit
    promises, financial outcome guarantees, and regulatory
    compliance issues. If sensitive content is detected,
    flag unsubstantiated claims and recommend evidence
    gathering. For superlatives, recommend qualifying
    language or proof points.


STEP 0.5: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Brand Foundation
    persona, Morgan (Strategic Brand Architect), carried
    forward from the prior foundation recipes. The persona
    object is stored in PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence.
    Users may attach a custom persona to override the
    default.

    IF BRAND_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Morgan (Strategic
        Brand Architect). Morgan presses for the value you
        ACTUALLY deliver versus what you THINK you deliver,
        translates features into emotional outcomes, and
        rates the believability and resonance of every UVP.


STEP 1: Context Loading and Validation

    Load and verify required inputs from previous recipes.
    Parse the context block from Brand Context Initializer
    (RCP-004-001-001) for business name, stage, goals,
    industry, and constraints. Parse the audience profile
    from Target Audience Profiler (RCP-004-001-002) for
    persona details and primary persona focus. Parse the
    pain point summary from Pain Point Identifier
    (RCP-004-001-003) for critical pain points and solution
    alignment. If any required input is missing, request it
    before proceeding. Note competitive context if provided
    (optional; full competitive analysis lives in
    RCP-004-001-005). Summarize the integration: name the
    primary persona and its top 3 pain points the UVP must
    address.


STEP 2: Value Proposition Framework Selection

    Present four UVP style frameworks and recommend the
    best fit. Benefit-focused leads with a clear outcome
    for the target audience ("[Action] [Benefit] [for
    Audience] [without Pain Point]"). Transformation-focused
    emphasizes a before-to-after state change. Problem-
    solution leads with the pain point and its resolution.
    Hybrid combines elements for complex or multi-segment
    propositions. Select per the uvp_style parameter or
    recommend based on context, giving a confidence read
    for each framework against the loaded inputs.


STEP 3: Feature to Benefit Mapping

    If include_feature_benefits is enabled, map features
    through three levels: Level 1 functional (what the user
    can DO), Level 2 outcome (the result they ACHIEVE),
    Level 3 emotional (how they FEEL). Build a feature-
    benefit table for the top 5-7 features. Then prioritize
    benefits by pain point severity (from RCP-004-001-003),
    differentiation strength, believability, and emotional
    resonance, and recommend which benefit the UVP should
    lead with. If disabled, skip to UVP generation.


STEP 4: UVP Variation Generation

    Generate value-proposition variations scaled to
    depth_mode:
        - Quick (2 variations, primary style): each with
          style, focus, pain point addressed, and a
          confidence read.
        - Standard (3 variations across 2 styles): each
          with a component breakdown (target audience, core
          benefit, differentiation, pain-point link),
          strengths, considerations, confidence; plus a
          comparison matrix rating clarity, differentiation,
          emotional resonance, and believability, and a
          recommended primary UVP.
        - Comprehensive (variation_count, all styles): all
          standard content PLUS extended formats per UVP
          (long, short, tweet-length under 280 chars,
          tagline 5-7 words), a per-style trade-off analysis
          (advantage / trade-off / best-for / risk), a
          competitive differentiation overlay when
          competitive_context is provided, and an A/B
          testing framework (hypotheses, metric, predicted
          winner, sample size, duration, confidence
          threshold).


STEP 5: UVP Component Breakdown

    For the primary recommended UVP, deconstruct each
    segment: its purpose, the pain point or benefit it
    connects to, why the language choice works (emotional
    hooks, concrete imagery, transformation signals), and a
    confidence read. Close with the strategic rationale for
    the overall structure - the pattern it follows, the
    frustration it addresses, and the alternative approach
    it differentiates from.


STEP 6: Value Proposition Summary Block Creation

    Generate a copy-paste-ready summary block for downstream
    recipes. Include: target audience reference, core
    offering description, the primary UVP with style /
    confidence / rationale, a short version and a tagline,
    alternative UVPs with use cases, key benefits in
    priority order (each with the pain point addressed, the
    emotional outcome, and the proof type needed), the
    feature-benefit table when included, messaging
    applications for hero and support sections, proof points
    needed, and differentiation notes.


STEP 7: Validation and Resonance Check

    Evaluate the primary UVP against six quality criteria,
    rating each and giving analysis plus an improvement
    note: clarity (immediately understandable), specificity
    (concrete vs vague), differentiation (unique vs
    generic), relevance (connects to pain points),
    credibility (believable claims), and emotional resonance
    (connects to feelings). Produce an overall quality
    score, name strengths and areas for refinement, and
    state whether the UVP is ready or needs another pass.
    Ask the user whether the primary recommendation captures
    what makes the offering unique.


STEP 8: Completion and Next Steps

    Deliver a summary of all outputs (value proposition
    summary block, UVP variations, component breakdown,
    quality assessment, feature-benefit map if included) and
    confirm the primary UVP recommendation. Restate what was
    established (what you offer, who it is for, why it
    matters, how you differ, how to use it). Provide the
    strategic bridge to the Competitive Edge Definer
    (RCP-004-001-005) - the summary block hands it the core
    value, differentiation angles, and proof points it needs
    - and ask whether the user wants to proceed or refine
    any aspect first.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: How many UVP variations should I create?

A: Start with 3 (default). Two variations may not provide
   enough contrast, while five can be overwhelming. Use
   quick mode (2) for time constraints, comprehensive (5)
   when exploring multiple positioning options.

Q: Which UVP style should I choose?

A: Benefit-focused works for clear, singular benefits.
   Transformation-focused works for dramatic improvement
   stories. Problem-solution works for pain-driven markets.
   Hybrid works for complex offerings or multiple segments.
   When uncertain, use hybrid (default).

Q: What if my UVP sounds generic?

A: Generic UVPs usually lack specificity or differentiation.
   {PERSONA_NAME} will flag this in the quality assessment.
   Solutions include adding concrete outcomes, naming
   specific pain points, or highlighting a unique approach.

Q: Should I include all features in the value proposition?

A: No. Focus on 1-3 core benefits that address top pain
   points. Feature lists dilute messaging. Save detailed
   features for product pages, not value propositions.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Morgan (Strategic Brand
   Architect) as the default for the Brand Foundation
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona
   file; the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable
   throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe synthesizes outputs from the three prior
foundation recipes to create compelling value propositions
guided by {PERSONA_NAME}. The AI scales variation quantity
and depth to the selected depth_mode parameter.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for competitive/superlative claims
   that need substantiation or qualifying language.

2. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Morgan (Strategic Brand
   Architect) carried from the prior foundation recipes.
   Load BRAND_PERSONA if available, else activate the
   bundled Morgan default.

3. CONTEXT LOADING: Load and validate the context block
   (RCP-004-001-001), audience profile (RCP-004-001-002),
   and pain point summary (RCP-004-001-003). HALT for any
   missing required input.

4. FRAMEWORK SELECTION: Choose among benefit-focused,
   transformation-focused, problem-solution, or hybrid per
   uvp_style or by recommendation.

5. FEATURE-BENEFIT MAPPING: Conditional on
   include_feature_benefits; map features through functional,
   outcome, and emotional levels, then prioritize.

6. VARIATION GENERATION: Produce variations scaled to
   depth_mode (quick / standard / comprehensive).

7. COMPONENT BREAKDOWN: Deconstruct the primary UVP segment
   by segment with strategic rationale.

8. SUMMARY BLOCK: Generate the copy-paste-ready value
   proposition summary block for downstream recipes.

9. VALIDATION: Rate the primary UVP against the six quality
   criteria and recommend ready-or-refine.

UVP QUALITY CRITERIA:
    - Clarity: Immediately understandable
    - Specificity: Concrete, not vague
    - Differentiation: Unique, not generic
    - Relevance: Connects to pain points
    - Credibility: Believable claims
    - Emotional Resonance: Connects to feelings

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Context block (RCP-004-001-001)
    - Audience profile (RCP-004-001-002)
    - Pain point summary (RCP-004-001-003)

FEEDS INTO:
    - Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005)
    - Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006)
    - Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007)

PARAMETER HANDLING:
    - context_block required (RCP-004-001-001)
    - audience_profile required (RCP-004-001-002)
    - pain_point_summary required (RCP-004-001-003)
    - uvp_style defaults to hybrid
    - depth_mode defaults to standard
    - variation_count defaults to 3 (min 2, max 5)
    - include_feature_benefits defaults to True
    - competitive_context optional

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is the VALUE_PROPOSITION_SUMMARY_BLOCK
containing the target audience, core offering, primary UVP
with rationale, short version and tagline, alternative UVPs,
prioritized benefits, messaging applications, proof points,
and differentiation notes. Secondary outputs include the UVP
variations, component breakdown, quality assessment, and the
feature-benefit map (when enabled).


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Creates compelling unique value propositions that
differentiate your offering. Synthesizes context, audience,
and pain points to generate multiple UVP variations with
component breakdowns and quality assessment. Guided by
{PERSONA_NAME}.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe as the fourth step in brand development,
after Brand Context Initializer (RCP-004-001-001), Target
Audience Profiler (RCP-004-001-002), and Pain Point
Identifier (RCP-004-001-003). The value proposition
developed here is critical input for:
    - Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005) -
      positioning context
    - Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006) - core of
      the pitch
    - Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007) -
      messaging foundation

Also use when repositioning for new markets, launching new
products, or refreshing messaging after market feedback.

PREREQUISITES:
    - Context block (RCP-004-001-001)
    - Audience profile (RCP-004-001-002)
    - Pain point summary (RCP-004-001-003)

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Pain Point Identifier (RCP-004-001-003)
    - Precedes: Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005)
    - Feeds: Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006) and
      Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: Fine Dining Restaurant (Standard Mode)

    Parameters:
        - context_block: Terra and Olive (Mediterranean
          farm-to-table, pre-launch, fine dining)
        - audience_profile: Sofia the Food Enthusiast,
          Marcus the Business Host (from RCP-004-001-002)
        - pain_point_summary: Finding authentic
          experiences, special occasion anxiety
          (from RCP-004-001-003)
        - uvp_style: transformation-focused
        - depth_mode: standard
        - variation_count: 3
        - include_feature_benefits: True
        - competitive_context: Local fine dining lacks
          authentic farm-to-table story

    Output:

    VARIATION 1 (Transformation - Recommended):
        "Transform special occasions into unforgettable
        Mediterranean journeys. Terra and Olive brings
        farm-to-table authenticity to every celebration."

        Component Breakdown:
        - "Transform special occasions" - elevates dining
          beyond transaction
        - "unforgettable Mediterranean journeys" - concrete
          sensory promise
        - "farm-to-table authenticity" - differentiator
          from generic fine dining

        Confidence: 85%

    VARIATION 2 (Benefit-Focused):
        "Experience authentic Mediterranean cuisine with
        ingredients sourced directly from local farms -
        no compromises, no pretense."

        Confidence: 80%

    VARIATION 3 (Problem-Solution):
        "Tired of restaurants that promise authenticity
        but deliver generic? Terra and Olive sources
        every ingredient with a story worth sharing."

        Confidence: 78%

    Short Version: "Farm-to-table Mediterranean dining
    that delivers on authenticity."

    Tagline: "Where Every Ingredient Has a Story"

    Feature-Benefit Mapping:
        - Local sourcing -> Fresh ingredients -> Trust
          in quality
        - Chef transparency -> Know your food origin ->
          Confidence in choices
        - Private dining -> Exclusive experience ->
          Special occasion assurance

    {PERSONA_NAME} Analysis: "Lead with transformation
    for emotional resonance with Sofia. Authenticity
    differentiator addresses core frustration. Recommend
    testing tagline on social media before launch."


Example 2: Environmental Consulting (Standard Mode)

    Parameters:
        - context_block: GreenPath Solutions
          (environmental consulting, beta stage, B2B)
        - audience_profile: Dana the Sustainability
          Director (from RCP-004-001-002)
        - pain_point_summary: Board-ready reporting gap,
          regulatory uncertainty (from RCP-004-001-003)
        - uvp_style: problem-solution
        - depth_mode: standard
        - variation_count: 3
        - include_feature_benefits: True
        - competitive_context: Existing consultants
          focus on compliance, not business case

    Output:

    VARIATION 1 (Problem-Solution - Recommended):
        "Sustainability directors struggle to translate
        environmental impact into boardroom language.
        GreenPath delivers executive-ready insights that
        make you the strategic voice, not just the
        compliance checkbox."

        Confidence: 88%

    VARIATION 2 (Transformation-Focused):
        "Transform sustainability reporting from
        compliance burden to strategic advantage.
        GreenPath helps you lead the conversation,
        not chase it."

        Confidence: 82%

    VARIATION 3 (Benefit-Focused):
        "Deliver board-ready sustainability metrics with
        business impact language executives understand -
        without becoming a full-time report writer."

        Confidence: 80%

    Short Version: "Sustainability insights in
    boardroom language."

    Tagline: "Make Sustainability Strategic"

    {PERSONA_NAME} Analysis: "Dana needs to look
    competent to leadership. Problem-solution framework
    resonates because it names her exact frustration.
    Differentiation: business case focus vs compliance
    focus sets GreenPath apart."


Example 3: Task Management SaaS (Quick Mode)

    Parameters:
        - context_block: TaskFlow (AI task management,
          growth stage, B2B SaaS)
        - audience_profile: Emma the Overwhelmed Manager
        - pain_point_summary: Tool sprawl, priority
          confusion, context switching
        - uvp_style: benefit-focused
        - depth_mode: quick
        - variation_count: 2
        - include_feature_benefits: False
        - competitive_context: Asana too complex,
          Notion too flexible

    Output:

    VARIATION 1 (Benefit - Recommended):
        "Manage all your tasks in one intelligent
        workspace - without the overwhelm of enterprise
        project management tools."

        Focus: Simplicity + consolidation
        Confidence: 80%

    VARIATION 2 (Benefit - Alternative):
        "Stop losing track of priorities. TaskFlow
        keeps your most important work front and center,
        automatically."

        Focus: Priority management + automation
        Confidence: 75%

    {PERSONA_NAME} Quick Analysis: "Variation 1
    addresses tool sprawl and complexity pain points
    directly. Test both on a landing page with 500+
    visitors to validate. Ready for the Competitive Edge
    Definer (RCP-004-001-005)."

                        (RCP-004-001-001), audience_profile
                        (RCP-004-001-002), pain_point_summary
                        (RCP-004-001-003). If any is absent,
                        request it and HALT; the UVP only
                        differentiates if it is anchored to
                        real audience pain."},
                    {"key": "GENERIC UVP",
                     "body": "If a variation reads generic, it
                        lacks specificity or differentiation.
                        Flag it in the quality assessment and
                        sharpen with a concrete outcome, a
                        named pain point, or the unique
                        approach - never ship a vague UVP."},
                    {"key": "UNSUBSTANTIATED CLAIMS",
                     "body": "Superlatives (best/only/#1) and
                        health/financial/competitive claims
                        must carry qualifying language or a
                        proof point. Surface the proof needed;
                        do not assert claims the inputs cannot
                        support."}
                ]
            },
            {
                "type": "prose",
                "body": "QUALITY BAR - the recipe succeeds when
                    it emits a self-contained
                    VALUE_PROPOSITION_SUMMARY_BLOCK a
                    downstream recipe could consume with zero
                    prior context, the primary UVP is 1-2
                    sentences (under ~30 words) and traces
                    directly to a named pain point and
                    audience, every claim is either believable
                    on its face or paired with the proof type
                    needed, and confidence reads tie to stated
                    inputs rather than being fabricated."
            }
        ],
        "lessons_learned": [
            {"key": "SUMMARY-BLOCK-IS-SHARED-BRAND-STATE",
             "body": "The real output is the
                VALUE_PROPOSITION_SUMMARY_BLOCK - the Brand
                Foundation section's shared messaging memory.
                Emit it copy-paste ready with stable field
                names; the competitive-edge, elevator-pitch,
                and brand-profile recipes all key off it."},
            {"key": "LEAD-WITH-OUTCOME-NOT-FEATURE",
             "body": "UVPs fail when they list features.
                Translate every feature through functional ->
                outcome -> emotional and lead with the benefit
                that maps to the audience's top pain point;
                that is what makes a UVP resonate rather than
                describe."},
            {"key": "VARIATIONS-EXIST-TO-BE-TESTED",
             "body": "Generating multiple UVPs is not
                indecision - it is positioning exploration.
                Always recommend a primary, but preserve the
                alternates with their use cases and confidence
                so the downstream pitch and A/B work have real
                options to test."}
        ]
    }
)

# =========================================================
# END RECIPE-ID: RCP-004-001-004-VALUE-PROP-v3.00a
# =========================================================


# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires the context block
   (RCP-004-001-001), audience profile (RCP-004-001-002),
   and pain point summary (RCP-004-001-003). The UVP only
   differentiates when anchored to real audience pain.

2. UVP LENGTH: The primary UVP should be 1-2 sentences
   (under 30 words). If longer, it is likely trying to say
   too much; use the tagline (5-7 words) for the shortest
   format and save detail for supporting content.

3. BRAND NAME: Including the brand name in the UVP is
   optional - it builds awareness; excluding it focuses on
   the benefit. Problem-solution style often includes the
   brand name naturally. Test both.

4. PERSONA FLEXIBILITY: The recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME}
   variable pattern. Default is Morgan (Strategic Brand
   Architect); it adapts to any BRAND_PERSONA object
   provided.

5. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: The Value Proposition Summary Block
   feeds the Competitive Edge Definer (RCP-004-001-005),
   Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006), and Brand
   Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007).

6. WHEN NOTHING FITS: If no variation feels right, this
   usually indicates unclear positioning or too many pain
   points. Return to the Pain Point Identifier
   (RCP-004-001-003) and narrow to the top 1-2 pain points;
   simpler input yields a clearer UVP.

7. VALIDATION: Test the primary UVP with 5-10 target
   audience members and A/B test variations where traffic
   allows; gather feedback on clarity and resonance.
