# =========================================================
# RECIPE DEFINITION
# =========================================================

ELEVATOR_PITCH_BUILDER = Recipe(
    recipe_id="RCP-004-001-006-ELEVATOR-PITCH-BUILDER-v3.00a",
    title="Elevator Pitch Builder - Multi-Context Pitch
        Creation",
    description="""
        Creates compelling elevator pitches across multiple
        lengths, styles, and contexts. Synthesizes
        competitive advantages, value propositions, and
        audience insights into persuasive narratives.
        Includes pitch variations for investors, customers,
        networking, and press with delivery guidance and a
        quality assessment framework. Activates
        {PERSONA_NAME} (Strategic Brand Architect) to guide
        the work.
    """,
    category="CAT-004-BRAND-IDENTITY",
    subcategory="SUBCAT-001-FOUNDATION",
    difficulty="intermediate",
    estimated_time="45-60 minutes",
    version="3.00a",

    dependencies={
        "required_inputs": [
            {
                "source": "RCP-004-001-002-TARGET-AUDIENCE",
                "input": "audience_profile",
                "description": "Audience segments and
                    characteristics from Target Audience
                    Analyzer"
            },
            {
                "source": "RCP-004-001-004-VALUE-PROP",
                "input": "value_prop_summary",
                "description": "Value proposition summary
                    from Value Prop Crafter"
            },
            {
                "source": "RCP-004-001-005-COMPETITIVE-EDGE",
                "input": "competitive_advantages",
                "description": "Competitive advantages from
                    Competitive Edge Definer"
            }
        ],
        "optional_inputs": [
            {
                "source": "RCP-004-001-003-PAIN-POINT-ID",
                "input": "pain_points",
                "description": "Pain points to strengthen
                    problem framing"
            },
            {
                "source": "Traction Data",
                "input": "traction_data",
                "description": "Metrics or validation that
                    strengthen proof"
            }
        ],
        "feeds_into": [
            "RCP-004-001-007 (Brand Profile Synthesizer)"
        ]
    },

    parameters={
        "pitch_contexts": {
            "type": "list",
            "required": True,
            "options": [
                "investor",
                "customer",
                "networking",
                "press",
                "partnership",
                "hiring"
            ],
            "description": "Contexts for pitch creation"
        },
        "pitch_lengths": {
            "type": "list",
            "required": True,
            "options": [
                "15-second",
                "30-second",
                "60-second",
                "2-minute"
            ],
            "description": "Pitch durations to create",
            "default": ["30-second", "60-second"]
        },
        "pitch_style": {
            "type": "string",
            "required": False,
            "options": [
                "problem-solution",
                "transformation",
                "value-first",
                "story-based",
                "all"
            ],
            "description": "Pitch narrative structure",
            "default": "all"
        },
        "audience_profile": {
            "type": "text_block",
            "required": True,
            "description": "Output from Target Audience
                Analyzer (RCP-004-001-002)"
        },
        "value_prop_summary": {
            "type": "text_block",
            "required": True,
            "description": "Output from Value Prop Crafter
                (RCP-004-001-004)"
        },
        "competitive_advantages": {
            "type": "text_block",
            "required": True,
            "description": "Output from Competitive Edge
                Definer (RCP-004-001-005)"
        },
        "include_delivery_tips": {
            "type": "boolean",
            "required": False,
            "default": True,
            "description": "Include delivery guidance"
        },
        "traction_data": {
            "type": "text",
            "required": False,
            "description": "Metrics or validation data"
        }
    },

    prompt_template="""

#H->AI::Directive: (Execute ELEVATOR-PITCH-BUILDER)
#H->AI::Parameters: (
    pitch_contexts: {pitch_contexts}
    pitch_lengths: {pitch_lengths}
    pitch_style: {pitch_style}
    audience_profile: [provided]
    value_prop_summary: [provided]
    competitive_advantages: [provided]
    include_delivery_tips: {include_delivery_tips}
    traction_data: {traction_data}
)

# =========================================================
# STEP 1: PERSONA ACTIVATION AND CONTEXT SYNTHESIS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::PersonaSwitch: (Activating {PERSONA_NAME} -
    {PERSONA_TITLE})

#AI->H::Context: ({PERSONA_NAME} brings decades of pitch
    refinement experience from boardrooms to trade shows)

#AI->H::Status: (Loading all previous recipe outputs for
    pitch synthesis)

CONTEXT_INTEGRATION = {
    "from_target_audience": audience_profile,
    "from_value_prop": value_prop_summary,
    "from_competitive_edge": competitive_advantages,
    "traction": traction_data,
    "contexts": pitch_contexts,
    "lengths": pitch_lengths,
    "styles": pitch_style
}

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} says: "Alright, let us craft
    your pitches. Remember: a pitch is not about cramming in
    every feature. It is about creating curiosity,
    demonstrating value, and earning the right to continue
    the conversation. Different contexts need different
    emphasis.")

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} philosophy: "The best pitches
    follow a simple rule: make them care before you make them
    understand. Hook emotion first, justify with logic
    second. We will structure every pitch accordingly.")

# =========================================================
# STEP 2: CORE NARRATIVE COMPONENTS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Extracting core narrative components)

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} says: "Every great pitch has
    the same building blocks. Let us identify yours, then we
    will assemble them differently for each context and
    style.")

NARRATIVE_COMPONENTS = {
    "hook": {
        "purpose": "Grab attention in first 5 seconds",
        "approaches": [
            "Provocative question related to pain point",
            "Surprising statistic about the problem",
            "Bold statement about the future or change",
            "Relatable scenario that resonates"
        ],
        "sources": "Pain points (RCP-004-001-003), audience
            insights (RCP-004-001-002)"
    },
    "problem": {
        "purpose": "Establish pain point with emotion",
        "elements": [
            "Who experiences this problem",
            "What the problem is specifically",
            "Why it matters (business or emotional)",
            "Why existing solutions fail"
        ],
        "sources": "RCP-004-001-003, RCP-004-001-005
            competitive gaps"
    },
    "solution": {
        "purpose": "Introduce offering as natural answer",
        "elements": [
            "What you built (category)",
            "How it works (methodology)",
            "What it enables (outcomes)",
            "Why now (market timing)"
        ],
        "sources": "RCP-004-001-004, RCP-004-001-005
            positioning"
    },
    "differentiation": {
        "purpose": "Why you vs alternatives",
        "elements": [
            "Primary competitive advantage",
            "Unique approach or methodology",
            "Defensible positioning (moat)",
            "Proof point or validation"
        ],
        "sources": "RCP-004-001-005 competitive advantages"
    },
    "transformation": {
        "purpose": "Paint the after picture",
        "elements": [
            "What changes for the user",
            "Quantifiable outcome if possible",
            "Emotional payoff (how they feel)",
            "Vision of better future"
        ],
        "sources": "RCP-004-001-004 benefit translations"
    },
    "proof": {
        "purpose": "Build credibility and reduce risk",
        "elements": [
            "Traction metrics (users, revenue, growth)",
            "Social proof (testimonials, logos)",
            "Credentials (team, advisors, backers)",
            "Validation (awards, press, partnerships)"
        ],
        "sources": "traction_data parameter"
    },
    "call_to_action": {
        "purpose": "Clear next step for context",
        "variations": {
            "investor": "Let us discuss the opportunity",
            "customer": "Try it or see a demo",
            "networking": "Can we connect",
            "press": "Available for interview",
            "partnership": "Let us explore collaboration",
            "hiring": "Join us"
        }
    }
}

FOR EACH COMPONENT:
    1. Pull relevant content from RCP-004-001-002/003/004/005
    2. Craft 2-3 variations of each component
    3. Keep each element to 1-2 sentences max
    4. Test for emotional resonance and clarity

CREATE COMPONENT_LIBRARY:

    PITCH NARRATIVE COMPONENTS
    ==========================

    HOOKS (Choose based on context):
        1. [Question-based hook]
        2. [Statistic-based hook]
        3. [Statement-based hook]

    PROBLEM STATEMENTS:
        1. [Problem emphasizing pain]
        2. [Problem emphasizing opportunity cost]

    SOLUTION INTRODUCTIONS:
        1. [Solution as methodology]
        2. [Solution as transformation]

    DIFFERENTIATION POINTS:
        1. [Primary competitive advantage]
        2. [Secondary unique approach]
        3. [Defensible positioning]

    TRANSFORMATION OUTCOMES:
        1. [Quantifiable outcome]
        2. [Emotional outcome]

    PROOF POINTS:
        1. [Traction metric if available]
        2. [Social proof if available]
        3. [Team or validation if available]

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} says: "These components are
    your pitch toolkit. We will mix and match them based on
    context, length, and style. Not every pitch uses every
    component - shorter pitches are ruthlessly selective.")

# =========================================================
# STEP 3: PITCH STYLE FRAMEWORKS
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Defining pitch narrative structures)

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} says: "There are four proven
    pitch structures. Each works better for different
    audiences and contexts. Let me show you the frameworks,
    then we will build your variations.")

PITCH_STYLE_FRAMEWORKS = {
    "problem_solution": {
        "structure": [
            "Hook: Establish problem dramatically",
            "Problem: Quantify impact and frustration",
            "Solution: Introduce your offering",
            "How: Explain approach at high level",
            "Proof: Validate it works",
            "CTA: Invite next step"
        ],
        "best_for": "Technical audiences, B2B, investors who
            want logic",
        "example_flow": "Problem is real, existing solutions
            fail, our approach works, proof",
        "emotional_arc": "Frustration, Relief, Hope,
            Confidence"
    },
    "transformation": {
        "structure": [
            "Hook: Paint before scenario vividly",
            "Current State: This is painful or limiting",
            "Vision: Imagine this better future",
            "Bridge: We make transformation possible",
            "How: High-level methodology",
            "Proof: Others have transformed",
            "CTA: You can too"
        ],
        "best_for": "Aspirational buyers, lifestyle or
            productivity tools, change agents",
        "example_flow": "Struggle now, dream future, we
            bridge gap, proof others did it",
        "emotional_arc": "Dissatisfaction, Aspiration,
            Possibility, Inspiration"
    },
    "value_first": {
        "structure": [
            "Hook: Lead with biggest benefit",
            "Value: What you will achieve or avoid",
            "How: Our unique approach delivers this",
            "Different: Why alternatives cannot match",
            "Proof: Validation or traction",
            "CTA: Get this value"
        ],
        "best_for": "Time-constrained contexts, networking,
            customers who know their pain",
        "example_flow": "Here is the value, here is how we
            deliver it, here is why we are different",
        "emotional_arc": "Interest, Desire, Conviction,
            Action"
    },
    "story_based": {
        "structure": [
            "Hook: Relatable character or situation",
            "Journey: Struggle they faced",
            "Discovery: They found our solution",
            "Transformation: How things changed",
            "Insight: Why this matters broadly",
            "Invitation: Your turn for transformation",
            "CTA: Next step"
        ],
        "best_for": "Emotional buyers, consumer products,
            storytelling contexts (press, social)",
        "example_flow": "Meet someone like you, they
            struggled, found us, life improved, you can too",
        "emotional_arc": "Connection, Empathy, Curiosity,
            Inspiration, Desire"
    }
}

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} strategy: "Most founders
    default to problem-solution because it feels logical. But
    transformation and value-first often work better for
    customer pitches. Story-based is powerful for press and
    social, weaker for investors who want data.")

CONTEXT_TO_STYLE_MAPPING = {
    "investor": "problem-solution or value-first (if
        traction exists)",
    "customer": "transformation (aspirational) or value-first
        (time-constrained)",
    "networking": "value-first (memorable) or story-based
        (builds connection)",
    "press": "story-based (narrative) or problem-solution
        (newsworthy angle)",
    "partnership": "value-first (mutual benefit) or
        problem-solution (market opportunity)",
    "hiring": "transformation (vision-driven) or story-based
        (cultural appeal)"
}

IF pitch_style == "all":
    FOR EACH CONTEXT in pitch_contexts:
        SELECT 2 MOST APPROPRIATE STYLES from mapping
        CREATE 2 STYLE VARIATIONS per context
ELSE:
    USE SPECIFIED pitch_style for all contexts

# =========================================================
# STEP 4: PITCH CONSTRUCTION
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Building pitch variations)

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} says: "Now for the main event.
    I will create complete pitches for each combination you
    requested. Each pitch is standalone - you can use any of
    them depending on situation.")

LENGTH_CONSTRAINTS = {
    "15_second": {
        "word_count": "30-40 words",
        "components": ["Hook", "Solution", "Value", "CTA"],
        "purpose": "Spark interest only",
        "use_case": "Quick intro, trade show, social bio"
    },
    "30_second": {
        "word_count": "70-85 words",
        "components": ["Hook", "Problem", "Solution",
            "Differentiation", "CTA"],
        "purpose": "Create curiosity and establish value",
        "use_case": "Networking, cold call opener, speed
            round"
    },
    "60_second": {
        "word_count": "140-160 words",
        "components": ["Hook", "Problem", "Solution",
            "How", "Differentiation", "Proof", "CTA"],
        "purpose": "Comprehensive value story with proof",
        "use_case": "Standard elevator pitch, pitch
            competitions, meetings"
    },
    "2_minute": {
        "word_count": "280-320 words",
        "components": "All components with deeper problem,
            solution, and proof",
        "purpose": "Full narrative with market context",
        "use_case": "Investor meetings, podcast interviews,
            presentations"
    }
}

FOR EACH CONTEXT in pitch_contexts:
    FOR EACH LENGTH in pitch_lengths:
        FOR EACH STYLE selected for this context:

            CREATE PITCH:

            ===============================================
            {LENGTH} {STYLE} PITCH - {CONTEXT} CONTEXT
            ===============================================

            [COMPLETE PITCH SCRIPT]

            (Actual word count: XX words)

            -----------------------------------------------
            PITCH BREAKDOWN
            -----------------------------------------------

            Structure:
                - Hook: [Explain what hook does and why]
                - Problem: [Explain problem framing]
                - Solution: [Explain solution positioning]
                - Differentiation: [Explain competitive
                    angle]
                - Proof: [Explain validation used]
                - CTA: [Explain call-to-action choice]

            Strategic Choices:
                [2-3 key decisions in this pitch version]

            Emphasis:
                Primary: [What this pitch emphasizes most]
                Secondary: [Supporting emphasis]
                Omitted: [What was left out and why]

            -----------------------------------------------
            ASSESSMENT
            -----------------------------------------------

            Strengths: [What works well in this pitch]
            Considerations: [What to watch for]
            Best Used When: [Specific situations]
            Confidence Rating: [5-star scale]
            Rationale: [Why this rating]

            ===============================================

# =========================================================
# STEP 5: DELIVERY GUIDANCE
# =========================================================

IF include_delivery_tips == True:

    FOR EACH PITCH CREATED:

        PROVIDE DELIVERY_TIPS:

        +-------------------------------------------------+
        | DELIVERY TIPS FOR THIS PITCH                    |
        +-------------------------------------------------+

        Pacing and Tone:
            - Speaking pace: [Recommended words per min]
            - Tone: [Conversational, Professional, etc.]
            - Emphasis points: [Which words to stress]
            - Pause moments: [Where to pause for effect]

        Body Language:
            - Opening stance: [How to begin physically]
            - Key gestures: [Where natural gestures fit]
            - Eye contact: [Pattern for this context]
            - Closing position: [How to finish strong]

        Adaptation Notes:
            - If interrupted: [How to pause and resume]
            - If time is shorter: [Which component to cut]
            - If they engage: [Natural dialogue points]
            - If they seem confused: [What to clarify]

        Practice Recommendations:
            - Record yourself: [What to listen for]
            - Mirror check: [What to watch for visually]
            - Feedback focus: [What to ask others]
            - Iterations needed: [Practice run count]

        +-------------------------------------------------+
        | END DELIVERY TIPS                               |
        +-------------------------------------------------+

# =========================================================
# STEP 6: PITCH QUALITY ASSESSMENT
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Evaluating pitch quality)

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} says: "Let me assess your
    pitches against six proven quality criteria. This helps
    you identify which pitches are strongest and where you
    might want to refine.")

QUALITY_CRITERIA = {
    "clarity": {
        "question": "Is it immediately clear what you do and
            for whom?",
        "green_flags": [
            "Non-technical person understands immediately",
            "Audience and offering are explicit within 15
                seconds",
            "No jargon or acronyms without context"
        ],
        "red_flags": [
            "Requires explanation or follow-up questions",
            "Uses industry jargon as shortcuts",
            "Vague positioning"
        ]
    },
    "relevance": {
        "question": "Does it address a problem the listener
            cares about?",
        "green_flags": [
            "Hooks into existing frustration or aspiration",
            "Problem is specific and relatable",
            "Listener can see themselves in scenario"
        ],
        "red_flags": [
            "Problem feels abstract or distant",
            "No emotional connection to pain point",
            "Solution looking for a problem"
        ]
    },
    "differentiation": {
        "question": "Is it clear why you are different?",
        "green_flags": [
            "Unique approach is explicit",
            "Competitive advantage is stated not implied",
            "Listener could not confuse you with others"
        ],
        "red_flags": [
            "Could be any company in your space",
            "Differentiation is vague (better, easier)",
            "No mention of what makes you unique"
        ]
    },
    "credibility": {
        "question": "Do you build trust that this is real
            and achievable?",
        "green_flags": [
            "Proof points included",
            "Realistic claims that do not oversell",
            "Specific outcomes not generic benefits"
        ],
        "red_flags": [
            "Grandiose claims without support",
            "No validation or social proof",
            "Sounds too good to be true"
        ]
    },
    "memorability": {
        "question": "Will they remember you 30 minutes
            later?",
        "green_flags": [
            "One clear sticky concept or analogy",
            "Surprising statistic or insight",
            "Vivid problem or solution contrast"
        ],
        "red_flags": [
            "Generic phrasing that sounds like others",
            "Information-dense but not distinctive",
            "No emotional or intellectual hook"
        ]
    },
    "action": {
        "question": "Is there a clear appropriate next
            step?",
        "green_flags": [
            "Specific low-friction call to action",
            "Appropriate to context and stage",
            "Easy for listener to say yes"
        ],
        "red_flags": [
            "Vague or no next step",
            "CTA is too aggressive for context",
            "Unclear how to follow up"
        ]
    }
}

FOR EACH PITCH CREATED:
    ASSESS AGAINST 6 CRITERIA:
        Rate each: Strong / Acceptable / Needs Work

    CREATE QUALITY_SCORECARD:

        PITCH QUALITY ASSESSMENT
        ========================

        Pitch: {Length} {Style} for {Context}

        Clarity: [rating] [Brief explanation]
        Relevance: [rating] [Brief explanation]
        Differentiation: [rating] [Brief explanation]
        Credibility: [rating] [Brief explanation]
        Memorability: [rating] [Brief explanation]
        Action: [rating] [Brief explanation]

        Overall Rating: [Strong/Good/Needs Refinement]

        Priority Improvements:
            1. [Most important thing to strengthen]
            2. [Second priority if applicable]

IF multiple pitches created for one context:

    #AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} says: "Let me compare your
        pitches side by side so you can see which works best
        for different situations.")

    CREATE PITCH_COMPARISON:

        PITCH COMPARISON MATRIX
        =======================

        Context: [e.g., Customer]

        Aspect      | Pitch A     | Pitch B     | Pick
        ------------+-------------+-------------+------
        Clarity     | [rating]    | [rating]    | [rec]
        Impact      | [rating]    | [rating]    | [rec]
        Completeness| [rating]    | [rating]    | [rec]
        Memorability| [rating]    | [rating]    | [rec]
        Best For    | [situation] | [situation] | [rec]
        ------------+-------------+-------------+------

        Recommendation: [Which to lead with and when to
        switch to the other]

# =========================================================
# STEP 7: CONTEXT ADAPTATION GUIDANCE
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Status: (Providing adaptation guidance)

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} says: "Pitches are not
    one-size-fits-all. Let me show you how to adapt your core
    pitch for specific situations within each context.")

CONTEXT_SPECIFIC_GUIDANCE = {
    "investor": {
        "emphasize": "Market size, growth trajectory, team
            credibility, competitive moats",
        "de_emphasize": "Product features, how it works
            technically, customer stories",
        "proof_priorities": "Traction metrics, user growth,
            revenue, LOIs",
        "danger_zones": "Vague TAM claims, dismissing
            competitors, unrealistic projections",
        "follow_up": "Clear ask: round size, timeline, what
            you need beyond capital"
    },
    "customer": {
        "emphasize": "Their pain, transformation, ease of
            getting started",
        "de_emphasize": "Technical complexity, competitive
            positioning, fundraising story",
        "proof_priorities": "Customer testimonials, before
            and after examples, free trial",
        "danger_zones": "Overselling, forcing urgency,
            feature dumping",
        "follow_up": "Low-friction: demo, trial, case study,
            conversation"
    },
    "networking": {
        "emphasize": "Memorable hook, who you help, what
            makes you distinctive",
        "de_emphasize": "Detailed explanation, competitive
            landscape, everything else",
        "proof_priorities": "One impressive metric or
            validation point",
        "danger_zones": "Going too long, being too salesy,
            not being conversational",
        "follow_up": "Exchange information, find connection
            points, stay memorable"
    },
    "press": {
        "emphasize": "What is newsworthy, human interest
            angle, trends you represent",
        "de_emphasize": "Sales pitch, feature lists,
            investment ask",
        "proof_priorities": "Unique data, surprising
            insights, visual story possibilities",
        "danger_zones": "Jargon, hype without substance, no
            clear story angle",
        "follow_up": "Offer exclusive access, data,
            interviews, story angles"
    },
    "partnership": {
        "emphasize": "Mutual value, complementary strengths,
            joint opportunity",
        "de_emphasize": "Your company full story, competitive
            threats, fundraising",
        "proof_priorities": "Examples of successful
            partnerships, integration ease",
        "danger_zones": "One-sided value prop, unclear
            benefit to them, vague collaboration",
        "follow_up": "Specific partnership proposal, pilot
            ideas, mutual customer benefits"
    },
    "hiring": {
        "emphasize": "Mission, vision, team culture, growth
            opportunity, impact",
        "de_emphasize": "Business metrics, fundraising,
            competitive positioning",
        "proof_priorities": "Team credentials, company
            trajectory, exciting challenges",
        "danger_zones": "Only talking about company not role,
            overselling, being vague",
        "follow_up": "Role specifics, culture fit
            conversation, team intro opportunity"
    }
}

FOR EACH CONTEXT in pitch_contexts:

    PROVIDE ADAPTATION_SCENARIOS:

        {CONTEXT} PITCH ADAPTATIONS
        ===========================

        Base Pitch: [Reference pitch]

        SCENARIO 1: [Specific situation]
            Adaptation: [What to change]
            Example: [Specific phrasing change]
            Reason: [Why this works]

        SCENARIO 2: [Another situation]
            [Same format]

        SCENARIO 3: [Third situation if relevant]
            [Same format]

        Common Objections in {CONTEXT} Context:

            Objection: [Typical pushback]
            Response: [How to address using components]
            Follow-up: [What to say next]

            [Repeat for 2-3 common objections]

# =========================================================
# STEP 8: COMMON MISTAKES AND FIXES
# =========================================================

#AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} reality check: "Let me save you
    from the mistakes I see repeatedly. These are the pitch
    killers that even experienced founders make.")

COMMON_MISTAKES = [
    {
        "mistake": "Feature Dumping",
        "looks_like": "Listing capabilities",
        "why_fails": "Features do not create emotional
            connection or communicate value",
        "fix": "Lead with outcomes, say helps you achieve X
            not has feature Y",
        "check": "If you are listing things, you are probably
            feature dumping"
    },
    {
        "mistake": "Jargon Overload",
        "looks_like": "Using industry acronyms and technical
            terms without context",
        "why_fails": "Confuses listeners, makes you seem less
            credible not more",
        "fix": "Use 8th-grade language. If your aunt would
            not understand it, simplify",
        "check": "Record pitch, count acronyms and technical
            terms - should be under 2 total"
    },
    {
        "mistake": "Weak Hook",
        "looks_like": "Starting with So we are building a
            platform that...",
        "why_fails": "Lost attention in first 5 seconds, no
            compelling reason to listen",
        "fix": "Start with provocative question, surprising
            stat, or relatable pain",
        "check": "Would someone put down their phone to hear
            your first sentence?"
    },
    {
        "mistake": "Vague Differentiation",
        "looks_like": "We are better faster easier than
            alternatives",
        "why_fails": "Everyone claims this, meaningless
            without specifics",
        "fix": "Name your unique approach: Unlike X which
            does Y, we do Z because...",
        "check": "Could a competitor claim your
            differentiation? If yes, too vague"
    },
    {
        "mistake": "No Proof",
        "looks_like": "Grand claims about outcomes with zero
            validation",
        "why_fails": "Credibility destroyed, sounds like
            vaporware or wishful thinking",
        "fix": "Include one concrete proof point: users,
            revenue, testimonial, data",
        "check": "If someone asks prove it, can you
            immediately?"
    },
    {
        "mistake": "Forgettable",
        "looks_like": "Accurate description but nothing
            sticky or memorable",
        "why_fails": "30 minutes later, they cannot remember
            who you are or what you do",
        "fix": "Include one distinctive element: analogy,
            stat, visual, or unique framing",
        "check": "What is the one thing someone would tell a
            friend about you?"
    },
    {
        "mistake": "Wrong Length",
        "looks_like": "Using 2-minute pitch in 30-second
            opportunity or vice versa",
        "why_fails": "Either rushed and incomplete or
            overstays welcome",
        "fix": "Have 15, 30, 60, 120-second versions ready,
            match to context",
        "check": "Practice with timer, know your length
            options cold"
    },
    {
        "mistake": "Weak CTA",
        "looks_like": "So yeah, let me know if you want to
            learn more",
        "why_fails": "Unclear next step, too passive, easy to
            ignore",
        "fix": "Specific appropriate ask: Can we schedule 15
            minutes next week?",
        "check": "Is your CTA a specific action or a vague
            hope?"
    }
]

FOR EACH MISTAKE:
    #AI->H::Note: ({PERSONA_NAME} warning: Watch for
        [mistake])
    [Provide mistake details and fix]

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires outputs from Target
   Audience Analyzer (RCP-004-001-002), Value Prop Crafter
   (RCP-004-001-004), and Competitive Edge Definer
   (RCP-004-001-005). Pain Point Identifier (RCP-004-001-003)
   is optional but enhances problem framing.

2. PERSONA FLEXIBILITY: The recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME}
   variable pattern. Default is Morgan (Strategic Brand
   Architect), the brand strategist bundled with this
   cookbook; it adapts to any BRAND_PERSONA object provided.

3. DOWNSTREAM RECIPE: The Elevator Pitch Portfolio Summary
   Block feeds Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007)
   and is also immediately usable for real pitching
   situations.

4. PITCHES SCORING "NEEDS WORK": That is normal and expected.
   Pitch quality depends on the strength of your inputs
   (value prop, competitive edge) and the inherent difficulty
   of your context. Use the quality assessment to prioritize
   refinement, fixing one criterion at a time, starting with
   the most impactful.

5. CHOOSING A STYLE: Start with the context-to-style mapping.
   Problem-solution works for logical audiences (B2B,
   investors). Transformation works for aspirational buyers.
   Value-first works when time is limited. Story-based works
   for emotional connection (press, consumers). Test 2-3
   styles against your actual audience.

6. MODULAR COMPONENTS: Each component (hook, problem,
   solution, etc.) is designed to be modular. Swap hooks
   between pitches or adjust proof points based on what you
   learn works best.

7. LIVING DOCUMENT: Update proof points quarterly as traction
   grows. Refresh hooks when market conditions change or
   competitors shift positioning. Review context adaptations
   after significant business pivots; the core value
   proposition and differentiation should remain stable
   unless fundamentals change.

# =========================================================

# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-001-007-BRAND-PROFILE-SYNTH

Description: Synthesizes the six prior Brand Foundation
recipe outputs into a comprehensive, reusable brand profile.
Integrates business context, audience, pain points, value
propositions, competitive advantages, and elevator pitches
into a unified brand operating system, and produces three
format options: a complete profile, a one-page brief, and a
quick reference card. Completes the Brand Foundation workflow
and emits the brand_messaging_pillars consumed downstream by
campaign planning. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (the brand
strategist bundled with this cookbook) for the synthesis.

# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 001

Recipe ID Numbers: 007

    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

    brand-profile, synthesis, brand-bible, brand-identity,

# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Brand Foundation
    persona, Morgan (Brand Strategist), carried forward
    through the Foundation sequence. The persona object is
    stored in PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence. Users may
    attach a custom persona to override the default.

    IF BRAND_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Morgan (Brand
        Strategist). Morgan synthesizes strategically rather
        than mechanically - integrating elements with
        connective tissue, surfacing "Have you considered"
        questions, and giving confidence ratings throughout.


STEP 1: Gather All Summary Blocks

    Collect the summary blocks from all six previous
    Foundation recipes before starting:

        RCP-004-001-001 (Brand Context Init): Business
            Context Block
        RCP-004-001-002 (Target Audience): Target Audience
            Profile Block
        RCP-004-001-003 (Pain Point ID): Pain Point Summary
            Block
        RCP-004-001-004 (Value Prop): Value Proposition
            Summary Block
        RCP-004-001-005 (Competitive Edge): Competitive
            Advantages Summary Block
        RCP-004-001-006 (Elevator Pitch Builder): Elevator
            Pitch Portfolio Block

    Have all six blocks ready to paste. This recipe cannot
    produce quality output without complete inputs from the
    previous Foundation recipes.


STEP 2: Configure Synthesis Parameters

    Set synthesis preferences: brand name; synthesis depth
    (standard or comprehensive); output formats (complete,
    brief, card - select which to generate); include visual
    guidelines (true/false); include community strategy
    (true/false). Standard mode produces core synthesis with
    3 values and 3 pillars; comprehensive mode adds extended
    examples, 5 values, and 5 pillars.


STEP 3: Brand Foundation Synthesis

    Extract and integrate the upstream context into brand
    purpose, mission, vision, and core values.

    From RCP-004-001-001 (Business Context): industry and
    market position, company stage and constraints, core
    offering, timeline and priorities, existing brand assets.
    From RCP-004-001-002 (Target Audience): primary audience
    definition, demographics and psychographics, core needs
    and motivations, communication preferences. From
    RCP-004-001-003 (Pain Points): top 3-5 priority pain
    points, severity and impact, current solution gaps.

    Synthesize into: a Brand Purpose statement (one
    compelling sentence on why the brand exists beyond
    profit); Mission (what you do, for whom, how) and Vision
    (the future state); and Core Values (3 standard / 5
    comprehensive), each with what it means and how it shows
    up. Note whether values are aspirational vs operational
    and bridge any gap. Emit a BRAND FOUNDATION SUMMARY
    BLOCK (purpose, mission, vision, values, target audience,
    key pain points) with a confidence rating.


STEP 4: Strategic Position Synthesis

    Integrate the positioning inputs.

    From RCP-004-001-004 (Value Proposition): primary UVP,
    supporting value propositions, benefit translations by
    segment, proof points. From RCP-004-001-005 (Competitive
    Advantages): key differentiators, defensibility,
    positioning statements, competitive landscape.

    Produce: the Primary UVP and supporting value props; a
    full and a concise Positioning Statement (For [audience]
    who [need], [brand] is a [category] that [benefit];
    unlike [alternative], we [differentiator]); a
    differentiation summary (primary differentiator,
    defensibility, position in market). Emit a STRATEGIC
    POSITION SUMMARY BLOCK with a confidence rating.


STEP 5: Brand Personality and Voice Synthesis

    Define personality traits (5 standard / 7 comprehensive),
    each with definition, behavioral example, and opposite.
    Define Brand Voice: core voice description; voice
    attributes on spectrums (tone, energy, expertise,
    warmth); "We Sound Like" vs "We Do NOT Sound Like";
    and tone variations by context (marketing, support,
    educational, social; comprehensive adds sales and
    crisis). Emit a BRAND PERSONALITY SUMMARY BLOCK with a
    confidence rating.


STEP 6: Messaging Architecture Synthesis

    From RCP-004-001-006 (Elevator Pitches) and prior
    context, build the messaging architecture - the
    brand_messaging_pillars that feed downstream campaign
    planning.

    Produce: Messaging Pillars (3 standard / 5 comprehensive),
    each with core message, why it matters, proof points, and
    best channels; a Message Hierarchy (primary / secondary /
    tertiary); Tagline Options (3 standard / 5 comprehensive)
    with style, best-for, strength, and consideration;
    Elevator Pitch integration (30s/60s; comprehensive adds
    15s/120s); and a Key Talking Points Library. Emit a
    MESSAGING ARCHITECTURE SUMMARY BLOCK (primary message,
    pillars, recommended tagline, condensed pitches, top
    talking points) with a confidence rating. This block is
    the brand_messaging_pillars handoff to the campaign
    section.


STEP 7: Brand Application Guidelines

    Create practical, channel-specific application guidance,
    each with on-brand approach plus Dos and Do-Nots:
    Website and Homepage (hero, key page types); Social Media
    (per-platform tone, content types, example posts); Email
    Communications (structure + per-type approaches and
    examples); Customer Support (philosophy, voice, scenario
    response templates); Documentation (philosophy, voice,
    per-type approaches). IF include_community_strategy:
    add Community Building (vision, values, engagement,
    guidelines, member welcome). Emit a BRAND APPLICATION
    SUMMARY BLOCK.


STEP 7.5: Visual Identity (Basic) - IF include_visual_guidelines

    Provide a strategic visual framework (not design
    execution): personality-aligned visual feel; color
    strategy (assess existing palette from
    RCP-004-001-001, else recommend an approach); typography
    approach; imagery style; and 3 design principles. Note
    that visual execution requires a designer.


STEP 8: Generate Three Output Formats

    Produce three copy-ready deliverables, each marked with
    === bars for clean copy/paste:

        Complete Brand Profile - comprehensive master
            document, all sections (2500-3500 words typical).
        One-Page Brand Brief - condensed for sharing
            (500-750 words).
        Quick Reference Card - daily brand compass
            (200-300 words).


STEP 9: Brand Evolution Framework

    Establish ongoing brand management: Quality Assessment
    Criteria (authenticity, clarity, consistency,
    differentiation, impact - rated Strong/Acceptable/Needs
    work); Brand Drift red flags (inconsistent voice, message
    confusion, personality shift, value dilution, competitive
    copying, team/audience uncertainty - 2+ flags trigger an
    audit); Quarterly Review Process (Q1 foundation, Q2
    market position, Q3 voice/consistency, Q4 performance);
    and When-to-Update triggers with what to change vs keep.
    Implementation roadmap phases: Phase 1 Foundation (wk
    1-2), Phase 2 Customer Touchpoints (wk 3-4), Phase 3
    Content (wk 5-6), Phase 4 Extended (wk 7-8), Phase 5
    Visual (wk 9-12). Emit a BRAND EVOLUTION SUMMARY BLOCK.
    Close with a final synthesis confirmation and 2-3
    strategic "Have you considered" questions.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: Do I need all six previous recipe outputs?

A: Yes. This recipe synthesizes the outputs of
   RCP-004-001-001 through RCP-004-001-006. Without complete
   inputs the brand profile will have gaps. Run the previous
   Foundation recipes first if you have not.

Q: What is the difference between standard and comprehensive?

A: Standard mode is faster and creates 3 values, 5 traits,
   and 3 messaging pillars. Comprehensive adds extended
   examples, 5 values, 7 traits, and 5 pillars.

Q: How long does this recipe take?

A: Standard mode takes 45-60 minutes. Comprehensive mode
   takes 60-90 minutes. Allow extra time for review.

Q: Can I skip sections like visual guidelines?

A: Yes. Set include_visual_guidelines or
   include_community_strategy to false if not needed.

Q: How often should I update the brand profile?

A: Review quarterly using the evolution framework. Make
   minor updates as needed; major updates only for pivots.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Morgan (Brand Strategist) as
   the default for the Brand Foundation section. To override,
   attach your own custom persona file; the recipe uses the
   {PERSONA_NAME} variable throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe synthesizes all six Brand Foundation recipe
outputs into a unified brand profile and the
brand_messaging_pillars handoff.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Morgan (Brand
   Strategist) carried through the Foundation sequence. Load
   BRAND_PERSONA if available, else activate the bundled
   Morgan default.

2. INPUT VALIDATION: Confirm all six summary blocks
   (RCP-004-001-001..006) are provided; check synthesis_depth
   and output_formats.

3. FOUNDATION SYNTHESIS (Steps 3-4): Integrate business
   context, audience, pain points, value props, and
   competitive advantages into purpose, mission, vision,
   values, and strategic position.

4. PERSONALITY AND VOICE (Step 5): Define personality traits
   and voice guidelines with tone variations.

5. MESSAGING ARCHITECTURE (Step 6): Build the messaging
   pillars, hierarchy, taglines, and talking points - the
   brand_messaging_pillars feed downstream.

6. APPLICATION GUIDELINES (Steps 7-7.5): Generate
   channel-specific guidance and the basic visual framework.

7. OUTPUT GENERATION (Step 8): Produce complete, brief, and
   card formats with copy-ready delimiters.

8. EVOLUTION FRAMEWORK (Step 9): Establish quality criteria,
   drift flags, review cadence, and implementation roadmap.

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Business Context Block (RCP-004-001-001)
    - Target Audience Profile Block (RCP-004-001-002)
    - Pain Point Summary Block (RCP-004-001-003)
    - Value Proposition Summary Block (RCP-004-001-004)
    - Competitive Advantages Summary Block (RCP-004-001-005)
    - Elevator Pitch Portfolio Block (RCP-004-001-006)

FEEDS INTO:
    - Campaign Architecture (RCP-004-002-001) - the brand
      profile seeds campaign planning
    - Messaging Matrix Builder (RCP-004-002-002) - consumes
      the brand_messaging_pillars produced here

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is three brand profile documents (complete
profile, one-page brief, quick reference card) plus the
BRAND_MESSAGING_PILLARS handoff that the campaign-planning
section reads. Secondary outputs include the per-section
summary blocks and the implementation/evolution framework.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Final Brand Foundation recipe that synthesizes all six prior
outputs into a comprehensive brand profile and the
brand_messaging_pillars handoff. Creates three formats:
complete profile, one-page brief, and quick reference card.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe after completing RCP-004-001-001 through
RCP-004-001-006 and before moving into campaign planning.

IDEAL TIMING:
    - After all six Foundation recipes are complete
    - When you need a comprehensive brand identity document
    - When you want multiple format options for different uses
    - When you are ready to implement your brand strategy
    - Before campaign planning needs the messaging pillars

PREREQUISITES:
    - All six Foundation summary blocks
      (RCP-004-001-001..006)
    - A defined brand or product name

Do not use this recipe when you have not completed the
previous six recipes, when you only need one element (like
taglines), when you need visual design execution, or when
starting brand development from scratch.

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Elevator Pitch Builder (RCP-004-001-006)
    - Completes: the Brand Foundation section (004-001)
    - Feeds: Campaign Architecture (RCP-004-002-001) and
      Messaging Matrix Builder (RCP-004-002-002)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: Restaurant Brand Profile

    Brand: Terra and Olive (fine dining)
    Inputs: all 6 Foundation blocks
    Settings: comprehensive; all 3 formats; visual +
        community guidelines on

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} synthesizes purpose ("Connecting
    people through farm-to-table culinary excellence"), 5
    core values, the audience profile, a primary UVP
    ("Seasonal menus that tell local farm stories"), 7
    personality traits (Warm, Sophisticated, Authentic,
    Seasonal, Local, Artisanal, Welcoming), a professional-
    warm voice, 4 messaging pillars (quality, locality,
    seasonality, experience), tagline options, and full
    application guidelines - emitted as the complete profile
    (operations manual), brief (staff orientation), and card
    (daily decisions). Strong synthesis, clear
    differentiation, authentic voice.


Example 2: B2B Consulting Brand

    Brand: GreenPath Solutions (environmental consulting)
    Inputs: all 6 Foundation blocks
    Settings: standard; all 3 formats; visual on, community
        off

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} synthesizes purpose ("Making
    sustainability practical for growing businesses"), 3 core
    values (Pragmatism, Impact, Partnership), a mid-market
    audience, a primary UVP ("Sustainability strategy without
    the complexity"), 5 personality traits, an expert-but-
    accessible voice, 3 messaging pillars, and a tagline
    ("Sustainable growth, simplified"). {PERSONA_NAME} note:
    "Have you considered focusing implementation on LinkedIn
    and proposals first? For a B2B firm those are your
    highest-ROI touchpoints." Strong, realistic positioning.

                        how it operates today, name the gap
                        explicitly and bridge it rather than
                        shipping aspirational values as fact."},
                    {"key": "VISUAL OVERREACH",
                     "body": "The visual section is a strategic
                        brief only. Do not produce final color
                        codes, font picks, or logo direction as
                        if they were design decisions - frame
                        them as input for a designer."}
                ]
            },
            {
                "type": "prose",
                "body": "QUALITY BAR - the recipe succeeds when
                    it emits a self-contained brand profile a
                    campaign recipe could consume with zero
                    prior context: the brand_messaging_pillars
                    are stable, named, and copy-paste ready;
                    every element traces back to one of the six
                    upstream blocks; the three formats are
                    genuinely tiered (complete is exhaustive,
                    brief fits a page, card fits a glance); and
                    confidence ratings tie to stated inputs, not
                    invented percentages."
            }
        ],
        "lessons_learned": [
            {"key": "PILLARS-ARE-THE-HANDOFF",
             "body": "The brand_messaging_pillars are the real
                cross-section output - the campaign section
                keys off them. Emit them as a stable, named,
                copy-paste block so RCP-004-002-002 can consume
                them without re-deriving brand messaging from
                scratch."},
            {"key": "INTEGRATE-DO-NOT-RESTACK",
             "body": "A synthesis recipe fails the moment it
                just concatenates its inputs. The value is the
                connective tissue between the six blocks -
                purpose informing position informing voice
                informing messaging - so the profile reads as
                one brand, not six recipe outputs stapled
                together."},
            {"key": "TIER-THE-THREE-FORMATS",
             "body": "Complete / brief / card must be genuinely
                different densities (2500-3500 / 500-750 /
                200-300 words). If the brief is just a trimmed
                complete profile, the user loses the daily-
                compass utility that makes the card and brief
                worth generating at all."}
        ]
    }
)

# =========================================================
# END RECIPE-ID: RCP-004-001-007-BRAND-PROFILE-SYNTH-v3.00a
# =========================================================


# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires all six Brand Foundation
   outputs (RCP-004-001-001 through RCP-004-001-006). It
   cannot synthesize a quality profile from a partial set.

2. DOWNSTREAM HANDOFF: The brand_messaging_pillars produced
   in Step 6 are consumed by the Messaging Matrix Builder
   (RCP-004-002-002); the overall brand profile seeds
   Campaign Architecture (RCP-004-002-001).

3. PERSONA FLEXIBILITY: The recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME}
   variable pattern. Default is Morgan (Brand Strategist);
   it adapts to any BRAND_PERSONA object provided.

4. THREE FORMATS: Complete profile (2500-3500 words),
   one-page brief (500-750 words), and quick reference card
   (200-300 words) serve different use cases - keep their
   densities distinct.

5. LIVING DOCUMENT: The brand profile is a living document.
   Review quarterly using the evolution framework; update
   for pivots, new audiences, or market shifts.

6. VISUAL GUIDELINES: The visual section is a strategic brief
   for a designer, not finished design - keep it directional.

7. VALIDATION: Aim for "Strong" or "Acceptable" on every
   quality dimension (authenticity, clarity, consistency,
   differentiation, impact) before declaring the profile
   ready for implementation.

# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-002-001-CAMPAIGN-ARCH

Description: Defines overall campaign structure, phases,
milestones, escalation model, and risk assessment. Creates
the strategic foundation that all subsequent Campaign
Planning recipes build upon, transforming brand identity
work into actionable campaign blueprints. First recipe in
the Campaign Planning section - it ACTIVATES {PERSONA_NAME}
(the campaign strategist bundled with this cookbook) and
stores the persona in PROJECT_VARIABLES so the whole section
runs under one continuous SME.

# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
        - Competitive intelligence gathering
        - Proprietary business information
        - Marketing claims requiring substantiation
        - Platform-specific policy considerations
    If potential conflict detected, note that campaign
    planning involves strategic business decisions and that
    recommendations are strategic guidance, not guarantees
    of results.


STEP 0.5: Persona Activation (Section Entry Point)

    This recipe OPENS the Campaign Planning section, so it
    activates the section's persona, Maggie (Strategic
    Campaign Architect), and stores it in PROJECT_VARIABLES
    as CAMPAIGN_PERSONA for persistence across every
    downstream Campaign Planning recipe. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default.

    IF CAMPAIGN_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Maggie (Strategic
        Campaign Architect) and store it in
        PROJECT_VARIABLES. Maggie is an integrated marketing
        campaign strategist who combines creative
        storytelling with rigorous, KPI-driven planning;
        she works professional-yet-accessible, metrics-
        forward, and challenges unrealistic timelines or
        resource assumptions.

    Maggie's focus for this recipe is strategic campaign
    foundation: phase architecture, milestone mapping,
    escalation design, and risk assessment, with every
    tactical decision traceable to business impact.
    Methodology: RACE Framework (Reach, Act, Convert,
    Engage) plus Agile Marketing.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Opening:

    "Let us dive into your campaign objectives and build
    something remarkable. I am {PERSONA_NAME}, your strategic
    partner for campaign architecture. My approach combines
    creative storytelling with rigorous planning - great
    campaigns need both art and science. Before we design
    your structure, I need to understand your foundation:
    every marketing effort should be traceable to business
    impact, so let us build a framework that makes
    measurement meaningful."


STEP 1: Gather Campaign Inputs

    Collect the inputs before starting.

    Required:
        - Brand profile block from the Brand Profile
          Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007) or equivalent
        - Campaign name (identifier for this campaign)
        - Campaign type (launch, awareness, community-
          building, conversion, hybrid)
        - Total duration (campaign length)

    Optional:
        - Phase count (or let the recipe calculate)
        - Escalation model (gradual, burst, sustained, wave)
        - Key dates (launches, events, deadlines)
        - Resource constraints (time, budget, team)
        - Target platforms (social and content platforms)
        - Primary CTA (main call to action)
        - Success metrics (KPIs for the campaign)


STEP 2: Analyze Campaign Context

    Extract the strategic foundation from the brand work;
    campaign architecture must be built on a solid brand
    identity, not noise.

    Brand Foundation Summary: core purpose/mission relevant
    to the campaign, key brand values to surface, brand
    personality traits to maintain, voice and tone guides.

    Target Audience Alignment: primary personas and
    motivations, pain points the campaign addresses, platform
    preferences, decision-making triggers.

    Value Proposition Core: primary benefits to communicate,
    competitive differentiators, proof points and
    credibility markers, objection handlers.

    Messaging Foundation: core messaging pillars from the
    brand work, taglines/elevator pitches available, key
    phrases and terminology, messages to avoid.

    Then synthesize against the campaign-specific parameters
    (name, type, duration, key dates, resource constraints,
    platforms, primary CTA, success metrics) into a 150-250
    word Campaign Context Summary, and give a strategic
    assessment of brand-to-campaign alignment, noting gaps or
    tensions and a foundation-strength confidence rating.


STEP 3: Define Campaign Phases

    Each phase must have a distinct strategic objective that
    builds toward the ultimate goal.

    Phase calculation: IF phase_count is specified, use it;
    ELSE calculate from campaign duration (longer = more
    phases), campaign type (launch needs pre/during/post),
    key dates (natural phase boundaries), and resource
    constraints (fewer if limited).

    Typical phase structures by campaign type:

    LAUNCH (6 months):
        Phase 1: Foundation and Anticipation (4-6 weeks)
        Phase 2: Pre-Launch Momentum (4-6 weeks)
        Phase 3: Launch Activation (2-4 weeks)
        Phase 4: Sustained Engagement (8-12 weeks)
        Phase 5: Optimization and Scale (remaining)

    AWARENESS:
        Phase 1: Establish Presence
        Phase 2: Build Recognition
        Phase 3: Deepen Engagement
        Phase 4: Sustain and Grow

    COMMUNITY-BUILDING:
        Phase 1: Seed Community
        Phase 2: Nurture Early Adopters
        Phase 3: Empower Advocates
        Phase 4: Scale and Sustain

    CONVERSION:
        Phase 1: Awareness and Interest
        Phase 2: Consideration and Education
        Phase 3: Decision and Action
        Phase 4: Retention and Referral

    Build a Phase Definition Matrix: for each phase capture
    Phase | Name | Duration | Primary Objective | Secondary
    Objectives | Key Message Theme | Success Indicator. Then
    explain the strategic rationale, how phases build on each
    other, and the critical transition points.


STEP 4: Map Milestones

    Create measurable checkpoints across four categories.

    Launch Milestones (external events): product/feature
    launches, major announcements, event dates, deadline-
    driven moments.

    Growth Milestones (quantitative): follower/subscriber
    targets, signup/conversion goals, engagement-rate
    targets, traffic milestones.

    Content Milestones (production): content-series launches,
    asset-creation completions, campaign-material readiness,
    platform-presence establishment.

    Community Milestones (qualitative): first user-generated
    content, community engagement thresholds, advocacy
    activation, testimonial/case-study acquisition.

    For each milestone capture: Name, Target Date, Phase,
    Category, Success Criteria, Leading Indicators,
    Contingency (if missed), and Dependencies. Then show
    milestone dependencies and the critical path, flag the
    highest-risk milestones, and suggest early-warning
    indicators.


STEP 5: Design Escalation Model

    Design the intensity progression - strategic energy
    distribution; launch intensity cannot be maintained
    forever.

    GRADUAL (default, resource-constrained): start low, build
    steadily, peak at launch, sustain at 70-80% of peak.
    Visual ___/----------. Best for solo operators, long
    campaigns.

    BURST (time-sensitive launches): moderate baseline, rapid
    increase approaching key dates, peak at the launch
    moment, quick drop to sustainable level. Visual
    ___/\___/\___. Best for event-driven campaigns.

    SUSTAINED (awareness): consistent rhythm throughout, minor
    variations for variety, consistency over peaks. Visual
    -------------. Best for brand building.

    WAVE (community-building): regular intensity peaks with
    recovery/analysis valleys, a predictable pattern
    audiences anticipate, each wave slightly higher than the
    last. Visual ~^~^~^~^~. Best for engagement-focused
    campaigns.

    Build an Escalation Schedule (Phase | Weeks | Posts/Week
    Primary | Posts/Week Secondary | Active Platforms |
    Content Intensity Low/Med/High) plus a Platform Activation
    Timeline (phased rollout: primary platforms first, add
    secondary, then full presence, adjusting on performance).
    Close with an honest assessment of sustainable intensity,
    flagging any unrealistic expectations and suggesting
    efficiency tactics for limited resources.


STEP 6: Assess Risks

    Identify risks and contingencies across four categories.

    Resource Risks: time-availability changes, budget
    constraints, tool/platform access issues, energy/burnout.

    External Risks: platform algorithm changes, competitor
    actions, market/industry shifts, news-cycle interference.

    Execution Risks: content-quality inconsistency, message
    drift off-brand, platform-specific failures, technical
    issues.

    Audience Risks: lower-than-expected engagement, negative
    feedback, wrong-audience attraction, community-management
    challenges.

    Build a Risk Assessment Matrix (Risk | Likelihood H/M/L |
    Impact H/M/L | Mitigation Strategy | Contingency Plan) and
    define Circuit Breakers (Yellow Alert condition->response;
    Red Alert condition->response; Pause Trigger condition->
    full pause for reassessment). Prioritize the top 3-5 risks
    for the specific situation with proactive mitigations and
    early-warning signs.


STEP 7: Generate Architecture Blueprint

    Bring everything together into the master Campaign
    Architecture Blueprint (the master reference for all
    tactical planning), including:

    - Strategic Foundation: primary/secondary objectives,
      target audience, core value proposition, primary CTA.
    - Phase Overview: visual timeline with key dates; phase
      names, dates, objectives.
    - Escalation Model: ASCII visualization of intensity over
      time; platform activation timeline.
    - Milestone Summary: critical-path milestones by date with
      success criteria.
    - Platform Strategy: primary/secondary/tertiary tiers with
      frequency guidelines per tier.
    - Success Metrics: leading indicators, lagging indicators,
      review cadence.
    - Top Risks and Mitigations: prioritized list with
      specific strategies.
    - Resource Requirements: time, tools, dependencies.

    OPTIONAL Phase 1 Deep-Dive (when the user is ready to
    execute): expand Phase 1 into week-by-week themes, content
    focus, platform priorities, Phase 1 milestones, success
    criteria (quantitative + qualitative), and the transition-
    to-Phase-2 criteria with a go/no-go decision date.


STEP 8: Create Integration Handoff

    Produce the copy-paste ARCHITECTURE OUTPUT BLOCK that
    feeds every downstream Campaign Planning and content
    recipe. The block contains: campaign name and type,
    duration and escalation model, the complete phase matrix,
    key dates and milestones, platform strategy summary,
    success-metrics list, brand-voice summary, and target-
    persona summary.

    This block feeds:
        - Messaging Matrix Builder (RCP-004-002-002):
          uses phases, personas, platforms
        - Content Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003):
          uses phases, brand voice, objectives
        - Channel Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004):
          uses platform strategy, escalation model
        - Campaign Timeline Architect (RCP-004-002-005):
          uses phases, milestones, key dates
        - Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001):
          uses all of the above outputs
        - Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002):
          uses phase context, brand voice
        - Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003):
          uses phases, messaging themes
        - Campaign Performance Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004):
          uses success metrics, milestones

    Close by recommending the next recipe (Messaging Matrix
    Builder, RCP-004-002-002) and asking the user to confirm
    the architecture aligns with their vision before
    finalizing.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: Do I need to complete the Brand Profile Synthesizer
   (RCP-004-001-007) first?

A: Recommended but not required. You can proceed with
   abbreviated brand context, but the architecture is
   stronger with a complete brand foundation.

Q: How do I choose the right escalation model?

A: Match it to your resources and campaign type. Gradual
   for limited resources, Burst for event-driven, Wave for
   community focus, Sustained for brand building.

Q: What if my key dates change after planning?

A: The architecture is built for flexibility. Adjust phase
   boundaries at transition points. Major date shifts may
   require an architecture revision.

Q: Can I run multiple campaigns simultaneously?

A: Yes, but each needs its own architecture. Weigh resource
   constraints carefully when planning parallel campaigns.

Q: How detailed should the Phase 1 breakdown be?

A: The optional deep-dive provides week-by-week themes for
   Phase 1. Later phases get detailed as you approach them.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Maggie (Strategic Campaign
   Architect) as the default for the Campaign Planning
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona
   file; the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable
   throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe creates the strategic campaign architecture -
phases, milestones, escalation model, and risk assessment -
that all subsequent Campaign Planning recipes build upon. As
the section entry point, it activates and persists the
section persona.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for marketing claims needing
   substantiation or competitive/proprietary concerns.

2. PERSONA ACTIVATION: Activate Maggie (Strategic Campaign
   Architect) and store her as CAMPAIGN_PERSONA in
   PROJECT_VARIABLES for the whole section; honor a custom
   persona override if one is attached.

3. GATHER INPUTS: Collect required/optional campaign inputs.

4. CONTEXT ANALYSIS: Extract the brand foundation (from
   RCP-004-001-007 or equivalent) and synthesize it with
   campaign parameters; assess alignment.

5. PHASE DEFINITION: Calculate the optimal phase count and
   define each phase's objectives and transitions.

6. MILESTONE MAPPING: Set measurable checkpoints across four
   categories with success criteria and contingencies.

7. ESCALATION DESIGN: Select the intensity model and build
   the platform-activation timeline.

8. RISK ASSESSMENT: Identify risks across four categories,
   prioritize them, and define circuit breakers.

9. BLUEPRINT SYNTHESIS: Combine everything into the master
   Architecture Blueprint (plus optional Phase 1 deep-dive).

10. INTEGRATION HANDOFF: Emit the Architecture Output Block
    for downstream recipe consumption.

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Brand profile block (from Brand Profile Synthesizer
      RCP-004-001-007, or equivalent brand documentation)
    - Campaign name, type, and total duration

FEEDS INTO:
    - Messaging Matrix Builder (RCP-004-002-002)
    - Content Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003)
    - Channel Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004)
    - Campaign Timeline Architect (RCP-004-002-005)
    - Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001)
    - Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002)
    - Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)
    - Campaign Performance Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004)

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is the ARCHITECTURE_OUTPUT_BLOCK containing
campaign name/type, duration, escalation model, the complete
phase matrix, key dates and milestones, platform strategy,
success metrics, brand voice summary, and target persona
summary. Secondary outputs include the Phase Definition
Matrix, Escalation Schedule, Milestone Checklist, Risk
Assessment Matrix, and the optional Phase 1 Detailed
Breakdown.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

The first Campaign Planning recipe - it creates the strategic
campaign architecture (phases, milestones, escalation model,
and risk assessment) and activates the campaign strategist
persona for the whole section.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe when:
    - You have completed brand foundation work
    - You are starting a new marketing campaign
    - You need strategic structure before tactical planning
    - You want to coordinate multi-phase campaigns
    - You need to align a team on campaign approach

Do not use this recipe when:
    - You need only tactical content creation
    - You are modifying an existing campaign
    - You lack basic brand positioning
    - You need immediate content (use Social Post Creator,
      RCP-004-003-002)

PREREQUISITES:
    - Brand profile block (RCP-004-001-007 or equivalent)
    - Campaign name, type, and total duration

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Brand Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007)
    - Precedes: Messaging Matrix Builder (RCP-004-002-002)
    - Feeds: all Campaign Planning recipes
      (RCP-004-002-002/003/004/005) and the content-execution
      recipes (RCP-004-003-001/002/003/004)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: Product Launch Campaign

    Business: TaskFlow (project management SaaS)
    Stage: Beta launch February 2026
    Duration: 6 months; Resources: solo founder, part-time
    Platforms: 4 primary, 3 secondary
    Goal: Build community, drive signups

    Execution: campaign_type "launch", escalation_model
    "gradual", key_dates [Dec 1 Pre-Beta, Feb 1 Beta, Apr 30
    End], resource_constraints {time: part-time, team: solo},
    platforms [Twitter, LinkedIn, YouTube, TikTok], primary_
    cta "Join the Beta".

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} designs a 5-phase architecture
    (Foundation Nov 18-Dec 15 Low-Med; Pre-Beta Dec 1-Jan 31
    Med; Beta Launch Feb 1-28 High; Community Mar 1-31 Med-
    High; Optimize Apr 1-30 Med), gradual-with-burst
    escalation, 15 mapped milestones, top-5 risks with
    mitigations, and a tiered platform strategy. Confidence:
    85%. {PERSONA_NAME} note: "Your part-time constraint is
    actually an advantage - it forces focus."


Example 2: B2B Awareness Campaign

    Business: GreenPath Solutions (consulting)
    Stage: Launched 6 months ago; Duration: 3 months
    Resources: small team (2 people)
    Goal: Increase recognition, grow email list

    Execution: campaign_type "awareness", escalation_model
    "sustained", resource_constraints {team: 2 people, time:
    dedicated}.

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} designs a 3-phase campaign
    (Establish Weeks 1-4; Build Recognition Weeks 5-8; Deepen
    Engagement Weeks 9-12), sustained intensity, consistent
    quality content, weekly milestone checkpoints. Confidence:
    90% - well-resourced.


Example 3: Community Building

    Business: Open source developer tool
    Stage: Released, needs contributors; Duration: 6 months
    Resources: core team of 3
    Goal: Grow contributors from 5 to 50

    Execution: campaign_type "community-building",
    escalation_model "wave".

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} designs a wave-based 4-phase
    campaign (Seed Weeks 1-6; Nurture Weeks 7-12; Empower
    Advocates Weeks 13-18; Scale and Sustain Weeks 19-24),
    wave pattern with monthly peaks, contributor-count
    milestone targets. Confidence: 75% - community building is
    unpredictable, flexibility built in.

# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Recipe Code (Copy This To Use)

# =========================================================
# START RECIPE-ID: RCP-004-002-001-CAMPAIGN-ARCH-v3.00a
# =========================================================


# =========================================================
# PERSONA CONFIGURATION
# =========================================================

# Default Campaign Persona - ACTIVATED here (section entry
# point) and stored in PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence
# across the whole Campaign Planning section. Users may
# attach a custom persona to override. This cookbook bundles
# the tier-less Maggie
# (PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MAGGIE-CARD.txt).

CAMPAIGN_PERSONA = {
    "name": "Maggie",
    "title": "Strategic Campaign Architect",

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. SECTION ENTRY POINT: This is the FIRST recipe in the
   Campaign Planning section. It activates Maggie (Strategic
   Campaign Architect) and stores CAMPAIGN_PERSONA in
   PROJECT_VARIABLES so the whole section runs under one SME -
   the campaign analogue of how BRAND-CONTEXT-INIT
   (RCP-004-001-001) activates Morgan for Brand Foundation.

2. BRAND INPUT: The brand profile block comes from the Brand
   Profile Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007) or equivalent
   external brand documentation. It SHOULD precede this
   recipe but the recipe CAN proceed with abbreviated context.

3. PERSONA FLEXIBILITY: The recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME}
   variable pattern. Default is Maggie; it adapts to any
   CAMPAIGN_PERSONA object provided.

4. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: The Architecture Output Block feeds the
   Messaging Matrix Builder (RCP-004-002-002), Content Pillar
   Planner (RCP-004-002-003), Channel Strategy Developer
   (RCP-004-002-004), Campaign Timeline Architect
   (RCP-004-002-005), Content Calendar Generator
   (RCP-004-003-001), Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002),
   Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003), and Campaign
   Performance Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004).

5. PHASE TRANSITIONS: Keep phase transitions criteria-based,
   not date-locked. Review the architecture at each
   transition; major key-date shifts may require revision.

6. ESCALATION SUSTAINABILITY: Match the escalation model to
   real resources. Run the reality check - an unsustainable
   intensity curve is the most common architecture failure.

7. RISK CIRCUIT BREAKERS: The Yellow/Red/Pause circuit
   breakers turn the risk matrix into an actionable response
   plan. Customize the trigger conditions to the campaign.

8. VALIDATION: Target 80% confidence on the architecture;
   milestones should be 100% measurable and time-bound, and
   risk mitigations actionable rather than theoretical.
