# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-002-002-MSG-MATRIX

Description: Maps messaging pillars to campaign phases,
platforms, and personas. Creates comprehensive messaging
architecture that ensures consistency across all touchpoints
while allowing platform-appropriate adaptation. Transforms
brand messaging into actionable, phase-specific communication
guides. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (the campaign strategist
bundled with this cookbook) for strategic messaging alignment.


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 002

Recipe ID Numbers: 002

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Campaign Planning

Recipe Tags:
    messaging-strategy, multi-channel, brand-consistency,
    messaging-matrix, campaign-messaging, persona-alignment,
    platform-adaptation, content-foundation

Recipe Recommended Personas: Maggie (Strategic Campaign
    Architect) - bundled default; Quinn (Multi-Channel
    Content Strategist) for the content-execution handoff

Recipe Difficulty: Advanced


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
        - Marketing claims requiring substantiation
        - Competitive comparisons
        - Platform-specific policy considerations
        - Claims about AI capabilities or outcomes
    If potential conflict detected, note that messaging
    involves claims that should be substantiable, and keep
    recommendations focused on authentic, defensible
    messaging.


STEP 0.5: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Campaign Planning
    persona, Maggie (Strategic Campaign Architect), carried
    forward from the Campaign Architecture recipe
    (RCP-004-002-001). The persona object is stored in
    PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default.

    IF CAMPAIGN_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Maggie (Strategic
        Campaign Architect). Maggie works peer-to-peer,
        metrics-forward, and direct - she leads with the
        matrix, not definitions.

    Maggie's focus for this recipe is messaging architecture
    and consistency: multi-channel message adaptation,
    persona-specific communication, brand voice consistency,
    platform culture alignment, and conversion-focused
    copywriting. Methodology: Pillar -> Persona -> Platform
    -> Phase mapping, with every message tracing back to the
    brand foundation.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Opening:

    "Welcome back. Now we are getting into my favorite
    territory - messaging architecture. Your campaign
    architecture gives us the when and how much. Now we
    need the what to say and how to say it.

    Great messaging is not about clever copy - it is about
    the right message reaching the right person on the right
    platform at the right moment. Let us build a system that
    makes that automatic."


STEP 1: Pillar Activation Mapping

    Map which messaging pillars activate in which phases.
    Not all pillars should be equally loud at all times;
    each phase has a primary messaging job, and certain
    pillars support that job better than others.

    From the brand messaging pillars provided, extract a
    pillar review table (Pillar | Name | Core Message | Best
    Use | Register; register options: Inspire, Educate,
    Convince, Connect). Then, for each phase from the
    Campaign Architecture, build a Phase-Pillar Activation
    Matrix (Phase | Primary | Secondary | Supporting |
    Minimize) with an activation rationale per phase (primary
    pillar + why, message emphasis, and what to avoid at that
    stage). Explain how pillars build across phases, which
    combinations create synergy, and which messaging
    conflicts to avoid.


STEP 2: Persona-Message Alignment

    Map which messages resonate with which audience personas.
    For each persona, capture primary pain points, core
    desires, decision triggers, objections to address,
    preferred platforms, content preferences, and language
    style. Build a Persona-Pillar Resonance Matrix (rate each
    pillar High/Medium/Low per persona, plus the best hook
    for low-resonance pairings). Then give persona-specific
    message angles - how to frame each pillar so it is
    relevant to THAT persona. Highlight where resonance
    patterns differ, persona-specific hooks for difficult
    messages, and universal messages that work across all
    personas.


STEP 3: Platform-Message Fit

    Adapt message style per platform culture while keeping
    brand voice consistent. For each active platform, define:
    platform culture, which personas are present, content
    that works, voice adaptation (formality/emoji/length),
    character/length guidance, posting rhythm, and per-pillar
    adaptation. Provide a Platform Voice Spectrum (formal to
    casual) and cross-posting adaptation rules (core message
    stays consistent; format adapts; tone shifts; CTA matches
    platform behavior; timing considers platform). Explain the
    balance between brand consistency and platform adaptation,
    platform-specific risks/opportunities, and which platforms
    pair well for cross-posting.


STEP 4: Moment Mapping

    Pre-plan messaging for high-stakes campaign moments
    (launch, milestone, community, transition, crisis). For
    each key moment, script: date/phase, objective, primary
    pillar, target personas, emotional target, a platform-
    neutral core message, and platform-specific versions
    (X/Twitter, LinkedIn, YouTube title+hook, TikTok hook),
    plus CTA, link, and 3 follow-up content ideas. Include a
    crisis moment template (acknowledge -> explain -> impact
    -> action -> timeline -> gratitude; honest, humble,
    action-oriented; avoid excuses and over-apologizing).
    Note which moments need the most preparation and which
    need real-time adaptation.


STEP 5: Matrix Generation

    Bring it together into the master messaging matrix across
    three dimensions: Phase x Pillar (Primary/Support/Minimal
    per cell), Persona x Platform (High/Medium/Low fit), and
    Phase x Content Type (Educational/BTS/Community/Promo/
    Thought-Leadership percentages). Provide a comprehensive
    lookup table: generate 5-10 of the most common
    Phase+Persona+Platform combinations, each resolving to
    primary pillar, message angle, tone, content type, and an
    example hook.


STEP 6: Message Library

    Build reusable message components so content creation
    scales without losing quality: a Hook Library (curiosity,
    pain-point, benefit, community, credibility), Pillar
    Statements (long/medium/short/hashtag forms per pillar),
    a CTA Library (awareness/engagement/conversion/community),
    a Proof Point Library, Objection Handlers (pre-written
    responses to common pushbacks), and a Hashtag Library
    (core/topic/community/platform-specific). Treat the
    library as a living document; suggest a review cadence
    and an A/B testing approach.


STEP 7: Messaging Synthesis and Handoff

    Package everything into a copy-paste output block that
    feeds cleanly into the downstream content recipes. Emit
    the MESSAGING MATRIX OUTPUT BLOCK (messaging pillars +
    short forms; phase-pillar priority; persona summary with
    platforms and key angle; platform voice notes; key moment
    dates + core messages; CTA by phase; message-library
    highlights) plus a one-page Phase Messaging Guide per
    phase. This block is the input for Content Pillar Planner
    (RCP-004-002-003), Channel Strategy Developer
    (RCP-004-002-004), and the content-execution recipes -
    Content Calendar (RCP-004-003-001), Social Post Creator
    (RCP-004-003-002), and Blog Content Planner
    (RCP-004-003-003). Close by recommending the next recipe
    and asking the user to confirm the pillar activations and
    persona alignments feel right.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: Can I use this recipe without completing the Campaign
   Architecture recipe (RCP-004-002-001)?

A: Campaign Architecture provides the phase structure and
   escalation model that this recipe maps to. You can adapt
   the recipe if you have equivalent planning from another
   source, but the phase-by-phase mapping assumes a defined
   phase structure.

Q: How many messaging pillars should I have?

A: Standard is 5 pillars. Use 3 for simpler campaigns, up to
   7 for complex products. Each pillar should represent a
   distinct value or theme.

Q: What if my personas are very similar?

A: If personas share significant overlap, consider
   consolidating. The goal is distinct communication
   strategies, not artificial segmentation.

Q: How often should I update the message library?

A: Review monthly during active campaigns. Add winning hooks
   and CTAs as you discover them; remove underperformers
   quarterly.

Q: Can I skip platforms I am not using?

A: Yes. Focus depth on 2-4 primary platforms rather than
   spreading thin across many. The recipe adapts to your
   actual platform selection.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Maggie (Strategic Campaign
   Architect) as the default for the Campaign Planning
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona
   file; the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable
   throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe creates comprehensive messaging architecture
that ensures brand consistency across all campaign
touchpoints while allowing platform-appropriate adaptation.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for marketing claims that need
   substantiation or competitive comparisons needing care.

2. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Maggie (Strategic
   Campaign Architect) carried from the Campaign Architecture
   recipe. Load CAMPAIGN_PERSONA if available, else activate
   the bundled Maggie default.

3. PILLAR ACTIVATION: Map which of the 4-5 brand messaging
   pillars to emphasize in each campaign phase.

4. PERSONA-MESSAGE ALIGNMENT: Determine which messages
   resonate with which audience personas; create per-persona
   angles for each pillar.

5. PLATFORM-MESSAGE FIT: Adapt messaging style/tone per
   platform while maintaining brand consistency; define
   cross-posting rules.

6. MOMENT MAPPING: Script messaging for key campaign moments
   including launches, milestones, and crisis scenarios.

7. MATRIX GENERATION: Create the master matrix combining
   phase x pillar, persona x platform, and phase x content
   type.

8. MESSAGE LIBRARY: Build reusable hooks, pillar statements,
   CTAs, proof points, objection handlers, and hashtags.

9. SYNTHESIS AND HANDOFF: Package outputs into the Messaging
   Matrix Output Block for downstream recipes.

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Campaign Architecture output (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Brand messaging pillars (from Brand Profile Synthesizer
      RCP-004-001-007, or equivalent)
    - Target persona definitions

FEEDS INTO:
    - Content Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003)
    - Channel Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004)
    - Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001)
    - Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002)
    - Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is the MESSAGING_MATRIX_OUTPUT_BLOCK
containing pillar definitions and priorities by phase,
persona summaries with platform preferences, platform voice
notes, key moment dates and core messages, CTAs by phase,
and message library highlights. Secondary outputs include
Phase Messaging Guides for quick reference.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Maps messaging pillars to campaign phases, platforms, and
personas. Creates the messaging bible that ensures every
piece of content connects to the brand foundation while
adapting to each channel.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe after completing the Campaign Architecture
recipe (RCP-004-002-001) and before creating any campaign
content.

IDEAL TIMING:
    - After campaign phases are defined
    - Before content calendar creation
    - When brand messaging pillars exist
    - When target personas are documented

PREREQUISITES:
    - Campaign Architecture Output Block (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Brand messaging pillars (4-5 core themes)
    - Target persona definitions with characteristics
    - List of active social platforms

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Campaign Architecture (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Precedes: Content Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003)
    - Parallel: Channel Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004)
    - Feeds: Content execution recipes (RCP-004-003-001/002/003)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: B2B SaaS Product Launch

    Campaign: Enterprise productivity tool launch
    Pillars: Time Savings, Integration, Security, Support,
        Innovation
    Personas: IT Director, End User, CFO
    Platforms: LinkedIn, X/Twitter, YouTube

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces a Phase-Pillar Activation
    optimized for B2B buying (Phase 1 Security primary for the
    IT Director; Phase 2 Time Savings for End Users; Phase 3
    Integration for IT approval; Phase 4 Support for risk
    reduction; Phase 5 Innovation for future-proofing), per-
    persona messaging (IT Director: security/compliance/
    integration; End User: time savings/ease/daily wins; CFO:
    ROI/TCO/risk), platform strategy (LinkedIn 70%, X 20%,
    YouTube 10%), 6 scripted key moments, and 40+ library
    components. Confidence: 80% - strong B2B framework applied.


Example 2: Consumer App Launch

    Campaign: Fitness app launch (3 months)
    Pillars: Results, Community, Science-Backed, Accessibility,
        Motivation
    Personas: Fitness Beginner, Busy Professional, Fitness
        Enthusiast
    Platforms: Instagram, TikTok, YouTube

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces a Phase-Pillar Activation
    for consumer engagement (Phase 1 Accessibility primary to
    lower the barrier; Phase 2 Science-Backed for credibility;
    Phase 3 Results for proof points), per-persona messaging
    (Beginner: accessibility/no judgment/small wins; Busy Pro:
    efficiency/quick workouts/results; Enthusiast: science/
    advanced features/community), platform strategy (TikTok
    40%, Instagram 40%, YouTube 20%), 5 scripted key moments,
    and 50+ library components. Confidence: 85% - consumer
    engagement optimized.

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires output from the Campaign
   Architecture recipe (RCP-004-002-001). The phase structure
   and escalation model provide the framework for messaging
   mapping.

2. BRAND INPUT: Messaging pillars come from the Brand Profile
   Synthesizer (RCP-004-001-007) or equivalent external brand
   documentation.

3. PERSONA FLEXIBILITY: The recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME}
   variable pattern. Default is Maggie (Strategic Campaign
   Architect); it adapts to any CAMPAIGN_PERSONA object
   provided.

4. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: The Messaging Matrix Output Block feeds
   the Content Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003), Channel
   Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004), Content Calendar
   Generator (RCP-004-003-001), Social Post Creator
   (RCP-004-003-002), and Blog Content Planner
   (RCP-004-003-003).

5. LIVING DOCUMENT: The message library should be treated as
   a living document that evolves as you learn what resonates.

6. PLATFORM EVOLUTION: Platform adaptation guides may need
   updates as platforms change algorithms, features, or
   culture. Review quarterly.

7. CRISIS MESSAGING: The crisis moment template provides a
   framework for unexpected situations. Customize to your
   specific risk scenarios.

8. VALIDATION: Target 80% confidence on the messaging matrix.
   Lower-confidence areas should be tested early.

# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-002-003-CONTENT-PILLAR

Description: Defines content categories with ratios, formats,
and example topics. Creates the structural framework for
balanced content creation that supports campaign objectives
while maintaining audience engagement - content variety
without losing strategic focus. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (the
campaign strategist bundled with this cookbook) for content
strategy.


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 002

Recipe ID Numbers: 003

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Campaign Planning

Recipe Tags:
    content-strategy, content-planning, content-pillars,
    topic-banks, content-ratios, format-strategy,
    cross-platform, campaign-content

Recipe Recommended Personas: Maggie (Strategic Campaign
    Architect) - bundled default; Quinn (Multi-Channel
    Content Strategist) for the content-execution handoff

Recipe Difficulty: Advanced


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
        - Content that requires expertise disclaimers
        - Claims that need substantiation
        - User-generated content liability considerations
    If potential conflict detected, note that content
    planning carries responsibility for published material,
    and keep recommendations focused on appropriate
    disclaimers where needed.


STEP 0.5: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Campaign Planning
    persona, Maggie (Strategic Campaign Architect), carried
    forward from the Campaign Architecture recipe
    (RCP-004-002-001) and the Messaging Matrix recipe
    (RCP-004-002-002). The persona object is stored in
    PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default.

    IF CAMPAIGN_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Maggie (Strategic
        Campaign Architect). Maggie works peer-to-peer,
        metrics-forward, and direct - she leads with the
        content system, not definitions.

    Maggie's focus for this recipe is content architecture:
    content category design, editorial calendar strategy,
    content mix optimization, repurposing and scaling
    content, and audience engagement patterns. Methodology:
    Goals -> Categories -> Ratios -> Formats -> Topics, with
    every pillar serving a strategic purpose.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Opening:

    "Perfect - we are building your content engine now.
    Content pillars are the categories that organize
    everything you create. Without them, you end up either
    too promotional (audience tunes out) or too scattered
    (no strategic momentum).

    The goal is a balanced diet of content that keeps your
    audience engaged while steadily moving them toward your
    campaign objectives. Let us design a system you can
    actually sustain."


STEP 1: Pillar Definition

    Define 4-6 content categories based on goals and capacity.
    Pillars should be distinct enough to feel different but
    connected enough to tell a cohesive story; each pillar
    has a job in the campaign.

    CONTENT GOAL ANALYSIS - map provided content_goals to
    pillar needs:

    | Goal               | Pillar Type    | Purpose          |
    |--------------------|----------------|------------------|
    | educate            | Educational    | Build expertise  |
    | build_community    | Community      | Foster belonging |
    | convert            | Promotional    | Drive action     |
    | establish_authority| Thought Lead   | Position voice   |
    | build_trust        | Behind-Scenes  | Show authenticity|
    | retain_audience    | Entertainment  | Keep returning   |

    RECOMMENDED PILLAR STRUCTURE (launch campaigns):

        CONTENT PILLAR ARCHITECTURE
        -------------------------------------------
        EDUCATIONAL        40%  Core value delivery
        BEHIND-THE-SCENES  20%  Trust and authenticity
        COMMUNITY          20%  Engagement and belonging
        PROMOTIONAL        15%  CTAs and offers
        THOUGHT LEADERSHIP  5%  Industry authority
        -------------------------------------------

    For each pillar, define PURPOSE, DESCRIPTION, CONTENT
    TYPES, BRAND VOICE in that pillar, SUCCESS INDICATORS,
    and STRATEGIC ROLE:

    PILLAR 1: EDUCATIONAL (Target 40%)
        Purpose: deliver genuine value, build expertise
        perception, give the audience reasons to follow.
        Description: content that teaches, explains, or helps
        the audience solve problems - "give before you ask,"
        pure value with no strings.
        Content types: how-to guides/tutorials; tips and
        tricks; concept explanations; best practices and
        frameworks; problem-solution posts; tool comparisons
        and recommendations.
        Brand voice: helpful and generous; expert but not
        condescending; practical and actionable.
        Success indicators: saves/bookmarks; "this is useful"
        shares; questions for more detail; "thank you"
        comments.
        Strategic role: builds trust and authority - "if free
        content is this good, paid must be amazing."

    PILLAR 2: BEHIND-THE-SCENES (Target 20%)
        Purpose: build trust through transparency, humanize
        the brand, create emotional connection.
        Description: content showing the real work,
        challenges, wins, and human side of building - the
        "building in public" content that creates authentic
        connection.
        Content types: development updates/progress reports;
        challenges faced and how solved; decision-making
        reveals; wins and milestone celebrations; day-in-the-
        life; honest reflections and lessons learned.
        Brand voice: authentic and vulnerable; honest about
        challenges; enthusiastic about wins (without
        bragging).
        Success indicators: encouraging/support comments;
        "I am rooting for you" sentiment; personal DMs and
        connection requests; increased loyalty metrics.
        Strategic role: creates emotional investment -
        audience becomes personally invested in your success.

    PILLAR 3: COMMUNITY (Target 20%)
        Purpose: foster belonging, encourage participation,
        make the audience feel like insiders.
        Description: content that highlights, engages with,
        and celebrates the community - turning followers into
        members and customers into advocates.
        Content types: user spotlights/success stories;
        community questions and discussions; polls and
        opinion requests; UGC features; community milestone
        celebrations; welcome posts; AMA sessions.
        Brand voice: welcoming and inclusive; curious and
        interested in others; celebratory of community
        achievements.
        Success indicators: high comment counts; members
        tagging each other; UGC submissions; strong reply
        rates.
        Strategic role: builds network effects - engaged
        community attracts more members and reduces churn.

    PILLAR 4: PROMOTIONAL (Target 15%)
        Purpose: drive specific actions, communicate offers,
        convert interest into commitment.
        Description: content with clear calls-to-action -
        signups, downloads, purchases. Keep the ratio low to
        maintain goodwill, but make confident asks when you
        do.
        Content types: product/feature announcements; beta/
        launch invitations; limited-time offers; benefit-
        focused posts; testimonial features; case study
        highlights; direct CTAs.
        Brand voice: confident but not pushy; clear about the
        value proposition; honest about what you are offering.
        Success indicators: click-through rates; conversion
        rates; signup/download numbers; revenue (if
        applicable).
        Strategic role: converts attention into business
        results; low ratio ensures asks do not erode trust.

    PILLAR 5: THOUGHT LEADERSHIP (Target 5%)
        Purpose: establish industry authority, contribute to
        larger conversations, position as visionary.
        Description: content sharing perspective on industry
        trends, future directions, and bigger-picture ideas -
        positioning you as worth listening to beyond your
        product.
        Content types: industry trend analysis; future
        predictions; commentary on news/developments;
        contrarian or unique viewpoints; original research/
        data insights; framework introductions.
        Brand voice: thoughtful and considered; confident in
        perspective; open to dialogue and debate.
        Success indicators: shares with commentary; media/
        influencer pickup; speaking/podcast invitations;
        "interesting take" responses.
        Strategic role: builds reputation beyond product;
        creates PR and partnership opportunities.

    Close by explaining the rationale for the recommended
    40-20-20-15-5 ratios (battle-tested for launch
    campaigns), how the pillars work together, and how to
    adjust based on the specific campaign context.


STEP 2: Ratio Allocation by Phase

    Adjust the content mix per campaign phase. Default ratios
    are the baseline, but each phase has different priorities:
    early phases need more education, launch phases need more
    promotion.

    PHASE-ADJUSTED RATIO MATRIX:

    | Phase | Edu | BTS | Com | Pro | TL  |
    |-------|-----|-----|-----|-----|-----|
    | 1     | 45% | 25% | 15% | 10% | 5%  |
    | 2     | 40% | 20% | 20% | 15% | 5%  |
    | 3     | 30% | 15% | 20% | 30% | 5%  |
    | 4     | 35% | 20% | 30% | 10% | 5%  |
    | 5     | 40% | 15% | 25% | 10% | 10% |

    Edu = Educational, BTS = Behind-the-Scenes,
    Com = Community, Pro = Promotional, TL = Thought
    Leadership.

    RATIO ADJUSTMENT RATIONALE:
        Phase 1 (Foundation/Anticipation): Educational HIGH
        (45%) to establish expertise before asking; BTS HIGH
        (25%) to build connection in the quiet period;
        Promotional LOW (10%) - too early to push hard.
        Phase 2 (Momentum/Pre-Launch): balanced mix
        maintaining value while building urgency; Community
        increasing (early adopter identity); Promotional
        rising (tease what is coming).
        Phase 3 (Launch): Promotional PEAK (30%) - time to
        ask; Educational drops as focus shifts to action; BTS
        drops (less building, more launching).
        Phase 4 (Community Building): Community PEAK (30%) to
        nurture new users; Promotional LOW (10%) to let users
        settle; Educational returns to help users succeed.
        Phase 5 (Optimization): Thought Leadership rises
        (10%) for long-term authority; balanced maintenance;
        data-informed adjustments based on what worked.

    VISUAL: PHASE CONTENT MIX EVOLUTION

    Ph1     Ph2     Ph3     Ph4     Ph5
    EDU ##  EDU ##  EDU #   EDU #   EDU ##
    BTS #   BTS #   BTS .   BTS #   BTS .
    COM .   COM #   COM #   COM ##  COM #
    PRO .   PRO .   PRO ##  PRO .   PRO .
    TL  .   TL  .   TL  .   TL  .   TL  .

    Explain ratio discipline (promotional never exceeds 30%
    even at launch), the over-promotion trap, and how to
    handle promotional pressure.


STEP 3: Format Specification

    Define content formats per pillar and platform. Each
    pillar has formats that work best for it; each platform
    has formats that perform - map the intersections.

    PILLAR-FORMAT MATRIX:

    | Format      | Edu | BTS | Com | Pro | TL  |
    |-------------|-----|-----|-----|-----|-----|
    | Text post   | +++ | ++  | +++ | ++  | +++ |
    | Thread      | +++ | ++  | +   | ++  | +++ |
    | Image       | ++  | +++ | +++ | ++  | +   |
    | Carousel    | +++ | ++  | +   | +++ | ++  |
    | Short video | ++  | +++ | ++  | ++  | +   |
    | Long video  | +++ | ++  | +   | ++  | +++ |
    | Poll        | +   | +   | +++ | +   | ++  |
    | Story       | +   | +++ | ++  | ++  | +   |
    | Live        | ++  | ++  | +++ | +   | ++  |
    | Article     | +++ | ++  | +   | ++  | +++ |

    +++ = Excellent fit, ++ = Good fit, + = Occasional.

    PLATFORM-FORMAT PRIORITY:
        X/Twitter: Primary text posts, threads, images;
        Secondary polls, short video clips; Avoid long-form
        (use threads).
        LinkedIn: Primary text posts, carousels, articles;
        Secondary native video, polls; Avoid casual/meme
        content.
        YouTube: Primary long-form video (8-15 min);
        Secondary Shorts (60 sec), community posts; Avoid
        text-only.
        TikTok: Primary short video (30-60 sec); Secondary
        live streams, stitches/duets; Avoid static content,
        long text.
        Dev.to: Primary long-form articles, tutorials;
        Secondary discussion posts; Avoid promotional-heavy
        content.
        GitHub: Primary README content, documentation;
        Secondary discussion posts, issue templates; Avoid
        marketing speak.

    FORMAT RECOMMENDATION BY PILLAR - for each pillar provide
    TOP PERFORMERS, QUICK FORMATS, and AVOID:
        EDUCATIONAL - Top: threads (X step-by-step),
        carousels (LinkedIn how-tos), tutorials (YouTube),
        articles (Dev.to deep-dives). Quick: single-tip
        posts, 60-sec tip videos, infographics. Avoid: walls
        of text, videos without clear takeaways.
        BEHIND-THE-SCENES - Top: candid photos/screenshots,
        short work videos, progress-update threads, live
        streams. Quick: screen recordings, "working on X
        today" posts, win/challenge reflections. Avoid: over-
        produced content, TMI personal content.
        COMMUNITY - Top: polls/questions, user spotlights,
        UGC reshares with commentary, discussion prompts.
        Quick: simple question posts, quote-tweets with
        praise, milestone welcome posts. Avoid: one-way
        broadcast, engagement bait without substance.
        PROMOTIONAL - Top: announcement posts, benefit
        carousels, testimonial features, demo videos. Quick:
        simple CTA posts, countdown/urgency posts, benefit
        bullets. Avoid: salesy tone, unsubstantiated claims,
        too many CTAs.
        THOUGHT LEADERSHIP - Top: opinion threads, long-form
        articles, commentary videos, data visualizations.
        Quick: hot-take posts, quote + commentary, prediction
        posts. Avoid: uninformed opinions, controversy for
        its own sake, obvious/generic takes.


STEP 4: Topic Bank Generation

    Create starter topics per pillar to remove the "what
    should I post about" friction - evergreen ideas to rotate
    plus seasonal/timely topics to mix in.

    TOPIC BANK STRUCTURE - for each pillar provide:
        - 10-15 evergreen topics (use anytime)
        - 5-7 campaign-specific topics (aligned to phases)
        - 3-5 reactive topic templates (respond to events)

    EDUCATIONAL TOPIC BANK:
        Evergreen: "How to [core concept]"; "X mistakes
        people make with [pain point]"; "The difference
        between [A] and [B]"; "Why [common approach] does not
        work"; "A beginner guide to [topic]"; "Advanced tips
        for [topic]"; "[N] ways to improve [outcome]"; "What I
        wish I knew about [topic] earlier"; "The complete
        guide to [process]"; "How to choose between
        [options]"; "[Tool/technique] explained simply";
        "Common questions about [topic] answered".
        Campaign-specific: "What is [your product/
        methodology]"; "[Key concept] vs regular approaches";
        "How to create your first [deliverable]";
        "Understanding [key feature/benefit]"; "When to use
        [A] vs [B]"; "[Product] across different [contexts]";
        "Building your first [project] with [product]".
        Reactive: "How [news/trend] relates to
        [methodology]"; "[New development] and how to use it";
        "Responding to [common question]".

    BEHIND-THE-SCENES TOPIC BANK:
        Evergreen: "What I am working on this week"; "A
        challenge I am facing and how I am solving it";
        "Something that went wrong (and what I learned)"; "A
        small win worth celebrating"; "My current workflow
        setup"; "Why I made [decision]"; "The story behind
        [feature/element]"; "What a typical day looks like";
        "Tools I am currently using and why"; "Honest
        reflection on progress so far".
        Campaign-specific: "Project [X] progress update";
        "Building the [product]: current state"; "How I use
        [methodology] for this campaign"; "Deciding which
        features make the cut"; "The [time period] journey to
        here".
        Reactive: "How [recent event] is affecting timeline";
        "Pivoting because [reason] - here is why"; "Community
        feedback that changed direction".

    COMMUNITY TOPIC BANK:
        Evergreen: "What is your biggest [pain point]
        struggle"; "Show me your [workflow/setup]"; "What
        would you want to learn about"; "Unpopular opinion:
        [topic] - what is yours"; "This or that: [A] vs [B]";
        "What is one tip you would share with beginners";
        "Celebrating [member] for [achievement]"; "Welcome to
        our newest community members"; "Friday wins: what went
        well this week"; "Ask me anything about [topic]".
        Campaign-specific: "What features do you want in
        [product]"; "Early adopter spotlight: [member]"; "How
        are you planning to use [product]"; "Community
        challenge update"; "Community milestone: [N]
        members".
        Reactive: "Great question from [member] - let us
        discuss"; "Featuring amazing UGC from [member]";
        "Community response to [announcement]".

    PROMOTIONAL TOPIC BANK:
        Evergreen: "Why [product/service] exists"; "[N]
        reasons to try [product]"; "What makes [product]
        different"; "Success story: how [user] achieved
        [result]"; "Testimonial feature: what [user] said";
        "Quick demo: [feature] in action"; "FAQ: answering
        your questions about [product]".
        Campaign-specific: "Waitlist is open - here is what
        you get"; "Early adopter benefits explained"; "Limited
        opportunity: [offer details]"; "[Phase] starts [date]
        - join now"; "Why join now (not wait for launch)";
        "[N] days until launch"; "Last chance: early access
        closing soon".
        Reactive: "Just hit [milestone] - thank you";
        "[Testimonial] just came in - wow"; "Responding to
        [objection] with [proof]".

    THOUGHT LEADERSHIP TOPIC BANK:
        Evergreen: "Where [industry] is heading"; "Why most
        [common approach] fails"; "The future of [category]";
        "What [trend] means for [audience]"; "Lessons from
        [related field] for [our field]"; "The case for
        [contrarian position]"; "What nobody talks about
        regarding [topic]".
        Campaign-specific: "Why [domain] needs structure";
        "[Principles] applied to [field]"; "The problem with
        [status quo] as we know it"; "What [time period] of
        experimentation taught me"; "Why frameworks beat
        ad-hoc approaches".
        Reactive: "My take on [industry news/announcement]";
        "Why [viral trend] matters (or does not)";
        "Predicting the impact of [new development]".

    Close with usage tips: treat the bank as a menu not a
    checklist; explain rotation strategies and which topics
    suit which phases.


STEP 5: Cross-Platform Mapping

    Map which pillars perform best on which platforms and
    define the content distribution strategy.

    PILLAR-PLATFORM FIT MATRIX:

    | Platform  | Edu | BTS | Com | Pro | TL  |
    |-----------|-----|-----|-----|-----|-----|
    | X/Twitter | +++ | +++ | +++ | ++  | +++ |
    | LinkedIn  | +++ | ++  | ++  | ++  | +++ |
    | YouTube   | +++ | +++ | ++  | ++  | +++ |
    | TikTok    | ++  | +++ | ++  | +   | +   |
    | Dev.to    | +++ | ++  | ++  | +   | +++ |
    | GitHub    | ++  | ++  | ++  | +   | +   |

    +++ = Primary focus, ++ = Regular use, + = Occasional/
    careful use.

    PLATFORM-SPECIFIC PILLAR RECOMMENDATIONS:
        X/Twitter (most versatile - all pillars work): lead
        with Educational (threads) + BTS (build-in-public);
        community engagement strong; promotional OK but keep
        ratio strict.
        LinkedIn (professional positioning): lead with
        Educational (thought-leadership angle) + Thought
        Leadership; BTS if framed as professional journey;
        community less natural; promotional needs a soft
        approach.
        YouTube (deep content): lead with Educational
        (tutorials) + BTS (vlogs); Thought Leadership through
        analysis; community via community tab; promotional via
        integrated CTAs, not standalone.
        TikTok (entertainment-first): lead with BTS + quick-
        tip Educational; Thought Leadership harder; promotional
        very challenging; adapt all pillars to platform energy.
        Dev.to (technical community): lead with Educational
        (technical deep-dives) + Thought Leadership; community
        via discussions; BTS if technically relevant;
        promotional almost prohibited by community norms.
        GitHub (code-first): lead with Educational
        (documentation) + BTS (changelog); not a true social
        platform; promotional through README quality, not
        posts.

    CONTENT DISTRIBUTION STRATEGY - CREATE ONCE -> ADAPT
    EVERYWHERE:

        Core: Educational tutorial (YouTube long)
            |-- X/Twitter: thread summary + link
            |-- LinkedIn: key insight post + link
            |-- TikTok: 60-sec hook + "full video linked"
            |-- Dev.to: written version (expanded)
            |-- Bluesky: discussion prompt + key takeaway

        Core: BTS update (quick video)
            |-- TikTok: native short
            |-- YouTube: Short
            |-- X/Twitter: screenshot/clip + context
            |-- LinkedIn: professional angle on same update
            |-- Stories: behind-the-scenes moment


STEP 6: UGC Strategy (if included)

    IF include_ugc_strategy == True, create a user-generated
    content strategy. UGC is authentic, scales, and builds
    community - but it must be made easy and rewarding.

    1. UGC TRIGGERS (encourage creation):
        Make it easy: provide fill-in templates; create
        memorable, unique hashtags; give clear prompts ("Show
        us your [X]"); share examples of what you want.
        Make it rewarding: feature UGC prominently; respond
        to and engage with all UGC; run competitions/
        challenges; offer tangible rewards (access, swag,
        features).
        Make it natural: ask for feedback genuinely (then
        share it); celebrate user wins; create shareable
        moments in the user experience; build "screenshot-
        worthy" features.

    2. UGC TYPES TO ENCOURAGE: success stories/results;
       product-use screenshots; user-discovered tips and
       tricks; feedback and suggestions; answers to community
       questions; creative applications/use cases;
       testimonials and reviews.

    3. UGC HANDLING PROCESS:
        UGC SPOTTED -> ACKNOWLEDGE (reply with thanks within
        24 hours) -> EVALUATE (feature-worthy?)
            +-- YES: request permission -> feature with full
            |        credit
            +-- NO: continue engagement

    4. UGC CAMPAIGN IDEAS: #My[Product]Story (share your
       experience); #[Community]Spotlight (why you joined);
       #[Product]Win (results achieved); showcase challenges;
       "most creative use" competitions; feedback features.

    Package everything into a copy-paste output block that

    the CONTENT PILLAR OUTPUT BLOCK and a Quick Reference
    Card.

# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: How many content pillars should I have?

A: Standard is 5 pillars. Use 3 for simpler campaigns
   (Educational, Promotional, Community), up to 6-7 for
   complex campaigns with dedicated content teams.

Q: Can I adjust the ratios?

A: Yes, ratios are guidelines. Authority-focused campaigns
   might raise Thought Leadership to 15%; community-focused
   campaigns might raise Community to 30%. Keep Educational
   highest.

Q: What if my content does not fit any pillar?

A: Good content usually fits one primary pillar. If it
   genuinely does not, consider whether it serves your
   campaign goals - content without strategic purpose should
   be reconsidered.

Q: How do I track pillar ratios?

A: Review weekly or monthly. Count posts per pillar and
   calculate percentages; adjust upcoming content to
   rebalance if needed.

Q: Should I use all pillars on all platforms?

A: No. Match pillars to platforms where they perform best -
   TikTok emphasizes BTS, LinkedIn emphasizes Thought
   Leadership. See the Pillar-Platform Fit Matrix.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Maggie (Strategic Campaign
   Architect) as the default for the Campaign Planning
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona
   file; the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable
   throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe creates the structural framework for balanced
content creation that supports campaign objectives while
maintaining audience engagement.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for content that requires expertise
   disclaimers or substantiation.

2. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Maggie (Strategic
   Campaign Architect) carried from the Campaign Architecture
   (RCP-004-002-001) and Messaging Matrix (RCP-004-002-002)
   recipes. Load CAMPAIGN_PERSONA if available, else activate
   the bundled Maggie default.

3. PILLAR DEFINITION: Define 5 content categories based on
   campaign goals; map goals to pillar types and create
   detailed definitions for each.

4. RATIO ALLOCATION: Adjust the content mix per campaign
   phase - early phases emphasize education, launch phases
   allow more promotion.

5. FORMAT SPECIFICATION: Map content formats to pillars and
   platforms; define which formats work best for each pillar.

6. TOPIC BANK GENERATION: Create starter topics per pillar -
   evergreen, campaign-specific, and reactive templates.

7. CROSS-PLATFORM MAPPING: Map which pillars perform best on
   which platforms and define the distribution strategy.

8. UGC STRATEGY: If included, create a UGC strategy with
   triggers, types, handling process, and campaign ideas.

9. SYNTHESIS: Package all outputs into the Content Pillar
   Output Block for downstream recipes.

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Campaign Architecture output (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Brand voice characteristics

OPTIONAL:
    - Messaging Matrix output (RCP-004-002-002)
    - Platform list
    - Existing content inventory

FEEDS INTO:
    - Channel Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004)
    - Campaign Timeline Architect (RCP-004-002-005)
    - Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001)
    - Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002)
    - Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is the CONTENT_PILLAR_OUTPUT_BLOCK containing
pillar definitions with ratios, the phase-adjusted ratio
matrix, format priorities per pillar, platform-pillar fit
mapping, topic bank summary, and UGC strategy status.
Secondary output is the Quick Reference Card for fast content
categorization decisions.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Defines content categories with ratios, formats, and topic
banks. Creates the structural framework for balanced content
creation that supports campaign objectives while maintaining
variety.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe after completing the Campaign Architecture
recipe (RCP-004-002-001) and optionally the Messaging Matrix
recipe (RCP-004-002-002). Execute before creating content
calendars.

IDEAL TIMING:
    - After campaign phases are defined
    - Before content calendar creation
    - When content goals are clear
    - When team capacity is understood

PREREQUISITES:
    - Campaign Architecture Output Block (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Brand voice characteristics
    - Content goals in priority order
    - Content creation capacity assessment

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Campaign Architecture (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Follows: Messaging Matrix (RCP-004-002-002) optional
    - Precedes: Channel Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004)
    - Precedes: Campaign Timeline Architect (RCP-004-002-005)
    - Feeds: Content execution recipes (RCP-004-003-001/002/003)

Example 2: Consumer App Launch

    Campaign: Fitness app launch (3 months)
    Content Goals: educate, build_community, convert
    Capacity: Moderate (small team)
    Platforms: Instagram, TikTok, YouTube

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces a standard 5-pillar
    structure with community emphasis (Educational 40%:
    fitness tips, nutrition; Behind-the-Scenes 20%: app
    development, team workouts; Community 25%: user
    transformations, challenges - elevated; Promotional 10%:
    app features, download CTAs; Thought Leadership 5%:
    fitness industry trends), a UGC strategy
    (#MyTransformation challenge, user workout video features,
    before/after spotlights), visual/video platform focus with
    a high-energy motivational tone, and topic banks of 50+
    topics with fitness-specific hooks. Confidence: 90% -
    consumer engagement optimized.

content creation.

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires output from the Campaign
   Architecture recipe (RCP-004-002-001). The phase structure
   provides context for the ratio adjustments.

2. MESSAGING ALIGNMENT: If the Messaging Matrix recipe
   (RCP-004-002-002) is completed, use it to ensure content
   pillars align with the messaging pillars for consistency.

3. RATIO DISCIPLINE: The 40-20-20-15-5 split is battle-tested
   but adjustable. Never let promotional exceed 30% in any
   phase, and keep educational as the highest ratio.

4. TOPIC BANKS: Treat topic banks as living documents. Add
   new topics as you learn what resonates; remove
   underperformers quarterly.

5. UGC STRATEGY: User-generated content requires consistent
   nurturing. If capacity is limited, skip the UGC strategy
   and focus on the core pillars.

6. PLATFORM FIT: Not all pillars work equally on all
   platforms. Use the Pillar-Platform Fit Matrix to focus
   efforts where they will have the most impact.

7. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: The Content Pillar Output Block feeds
   the Channel Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004), Campaign
   Timeline Architect (RCP-004-002-005), Content Calendar
   Generator (RCP-004-003-001), Social Post Creator
   (RCP-004-003-002), and Blog Content Planner
   (RCP-004-003-003).

8. VALIDATION: Target 85% confidence on the pillar
   architecture. Lower-confidence areas should be tested early
   in the campaign.

#          Branding & Identity §004-002 Campaign Planning)
# Creator: Auguste (Content Creator)
# Upgraded by: P062-Cat (SP11 Branding & Identity cookbook)
# Status: Ready for Validation
# =========================================================
# RE-HOME NOTE (SP11 H025, Richard-approved Option 1): this
# recipe's content is campaign channel strategy, so it is
# placed in the Campaign Planning section (004-002) under
# Maggie, NOT the Brand Foundation section. Source internal id
# RCP-005-001-004 (CAT-005 Campaign Planning) normalized to the
# canonical Branding & Identity slot RCP-004-002-004. The
# uploaded filename slot 004-001-004 was the OLD mis-slot.
# =========================================================


# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-002-004-CHANNEL-STRAT

Description: Creates platform-specific strategies with
frequency, format, tactics, and engagement approaches.
Develops detailed playbooks for each active channel that
respect platform culture while maintaining brand consistency.
Completes the Strategic Layer of campaign planning. Activates
{PERSONA_NAME} (the campaign strategist bundled with this
cookbook) for channel expertise and platform optimization.


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 002

Recipe ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Campaign Planning

Recipe Tags:
    channel-strategy, platform-playbooks, engagement-tactics,
    multi-channel, frequency-planning, cross-posting,
    platform-optimization, campaign-strategy

Recipe Recommended Personas: Maggie (Strategic Campaign
    Architect) - bundled default; Quinn (Multi-Channel
    Content Strategist) for the content-execution handoff

Recipe Difficulty: Advanced


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
        - Platform terms-of-service considerations
        - Automation and scheduling policies
        - Growth tactics that may violate platform rules
    If a potential conflict is detected, note that channel
    strategy must respect platform policies, and keep all
    recommended tactics compliant with platform terms of
    service.


STEP 0.5: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Campaign Planning
    persona, Maggie (Strategic Campaign Architect), carried
    forward from the Campaign Architecture recipe
    (RCP-004-002-001) and the Messaging Matrix recipe
    (RCP-004-002-002). The persona object is stored in
    PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default.

    IF CAMPAIGN_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Maggie (Strategic
        Campaign Architect). Maggie works peer-to-peer,
        metrics-forward, and direct - she leads with the
        playbook, not definitions.

    Maggie's focus for this recipe is platform strategy and
    channel optimization: platform-specific best practices,
    algorithm-friendly content strategies, engagement
    optimization tactics, cross-platform content distribution,
    and per-platform community building. Methodology: Audit ->
    Strategy -> Tactics -> Integration, with every tactic
    respecting platform culture.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Opening:

    "We are now building your platform playbooks. This is
    where strategy becomes specific. Each platform is its own
    ecosystem with unique culture, algorithm preferences, and
    audience expectations.

    The goal is not to be everywhere doing everything - it is
    to be strategic about where you invest effort and what you
    do on each platform. Let us build playbooks you can
    actually execute with your available resources."


STEP 1: Platform Audit

    Assess current state and opportunity per platform before
    strategizing; an honest audit prevents wasted effort on
    platforms that do not serve the goals. Build a Platform
    Audit Matrix (Platform | Current state New/Established |
    Audience High/Med | Effort High/Med | Score 1-10) across
    the candidate platforms (e.g. X/Twitter, LinkedIn,
    YouTube, TikTok, Bluesky, Mastodon, Dev.to, GitHub).

    Calculate a priority score (1-10) per platform using the
    PRIORITY SCORE FORMULA: Audience Fit (40%) + Growth
    Potential (25%) + Effort Efficiency (20%) + Strategic
    Importance (15%). Score bands: HIGH 8-10 (primary, daily),
    MEDIUM 5-7 (regular, 3-4x weekly), LOW 1-4 (maintenance,
    weekly).

    From the scores, assign each platform to a PLATFORM TIER
    (a platform-prioritization tier, NOT a persona tier):
        TIER 1 - PRIMARY (daily focus)
        TIER 2 - SECONDARY (regular presence)
        TIER 3 - TERTIARY (maintenance mode)
        TIER 4 - MONITOR ONLY (not active yet)
    Each entry carries score + rationale. Then explain the
    tier-assignment rationale, platforms that might surprise
    the user, and platforms that might change tiers during the
    campaign.


STEP 2: Platform Persona Fit

    Personas do not distribute evenly across platforms; map
    where each audience persona actually spends time so the
    user knows who they are addressing where. Build a Persona-
    Platform Mapping (Platform | Primary persona | Secondary |
    Tertiary | Notes) and a Persona Concentration visual that
    rates each persona's presence per platform (High / Medium /
    Low). Then state the content implications - which platform
    addresses all personas (highest overlap), which platform
    leads with which persona's messaging, and which platforms
    are single-persona (e.g. developer-only technical
    credibility channels).


STEP 3: Frequency Planning

    Set sustainable posting frequency per platform per phase -
    consistency over maximum volume. Provide a Frequency Matrix
    by Tier across phases (Tier 1 Primary, Tier 2 Secondary,
    Tier 3 Tertiary, Tier 4 Monitor; columns Phase 1-2, Phase 3
    Launch, Phase 4-5). Then give a Platform-Specific Frequency
    Guide per active platform, each defining: tier, baseline
    cadence, a content breakdown (originals / threads or
    articles / engagement / format-specific items), optimal
    timing windows, and phase adjustments. Cover at minimum:

        - X/Twitter (1-2 posts/day; threads, engagement
          replies, quote tweets; weekday and weekend windows)
        - LinkedIn (1 post/day; feed posts, articles, comments,
          carousels; Tue-Thu best; links in first comment)
        - YouTube (1 long-form/week + 2-3 Shorts/week; community
          posts; quality over quantity)
        - TikTok (3-4 videos/week; duets/stitches; rewards
          posting consistency)
        - Secondary social (Bluesky, Mastodon: 3-5/week each;
          cross-post adapted X content; Mastodon values
          intentional, anti-algorithm, authentic participation)
        - Developer platforms (Dev.to: 1-2 articles/month, deep
          technical; GitHub: presence not posting - README +
          docs + issue responses within 48h; depth over
          frequency)

    Provide a Weekly Posting Schedule Template (moderate-
    capacity day-by-platform grid; L = long-form video, S =
    short video) totaling ~5-7 pieces/day. Close with a
    reality check: a reduced-capacity alternative, which posts
    can be batched/repurposed, and which platforms to
    deprioritize if needed.


STEP 4: Format Optimization

    Define the best-performing content formats per platform so
    content plays to each platform's native strengths. Build a
    Platform Format Playbook per platform listing top
    performers and an AVOID list:

        - X/Twitter: threads (5-12 tweets, hook critical, CTA +
          save prompt), single tweets with images (2-3x
          engagement, alt text), engagement posts (questions,
          polls <=4 options). AVOID: links in main tweet, >3
          hashtags, walls of text, engagement bait.
        - LinkedIn: personal story posts (first-person,
          1,200-1,500 chars, frequent line breaks), carousels
          (8-12 slides, mobile-readable, CTA final slide),
          native video (1-3 min, captions). AVOID: external
          links in body, >5 hashtags, overly casual tone,
          engagement pods.
        - YouTube: long-form (8-15 min; Hook 0-30s -> Setup ->
          Content -> CTA; curiosity/benefit titles; face+text
          thumbnails; keyword-front descriptions), Shorts (<60s,
          hook in 1-2s, one insight, 9:16, text overlays),
          community posts (polls, BTS, teasers, questions).
        - TikTok: talking head + screen share (30-60s),
          trending sound + relevant content (move fast, never
          force trends), POV / day-in-the-life. Success factors:
          hook in first 1-2 seconds, captions always, authentic
          over polished, reply to comments. AVOID: over-
          produced content, hard sales pitches, horizontal
          video, ignoring trends entirely.


STEP 5: Engagement Tactics

    Posting is only half the game; engagement builds real
    community. Provide an Engagement Tactics Library. Start
    with Universal Engagement Principles (response timing -
    present in first hour, reply to every comment within 24h,
    meaningful over emoji-only; proactive engagement - comment
    before posting, add value not self-promotion; community
    building - remember returning commenters, ask follow-ups,
    create conversation; tone - match platform energy, be
    genuinely helpful, show personality within brand voice).

    Then give per-platform daily/weekly action checklists,
    tactics-that-work, and AVOID lists for:
        - X/Twitter (reply to 5-10 niche posts/day, quote-tweet
          1-2, weekly discussion threads / Spaces; AVOID generic
          "great post!", product-injection, arguing)
        - LinkedIn (thoughtful comments on 5-10 posts/day,
          personalized welcomes, group discussions; "comment as
          mini-post"; AVOID automated messages, pitching in
          comments, pods)
        - YouTube (pin a value comment, heart+reply in 24h,
          prompt comments; community tab between uploads; AVOID
          ignoring comments, subscribe-begging)
        - TikTok (reply in first hour, video replies to
          comments for visibility, duets/stitches; first-hour
          comments and creator replies boost reach; AVOID
          ignoring comments, over-formality, follow-for-follow)


STEP 6: Cross-Posting Strategy

    Creating unique content for many platforms is impossible
    with limited resources; create core content once and adapt
    it intelligently. Provide a Content Repurposing Matrix
    showing how each hub format fans out, e.g.:
        - YouTube long-form -> X thread, LinkedIn post, TikTok
          clip, YouTube Short, Dev.to article, blog post
        - LinkedIn carousel -> X thread, TikTok slide video,
          narrated Short, condensed Bluesky
        - X thread -> expanded LinkedIn post, Bluesky cross-
          post, adapted Mastodon, TikTok visual script
        - TikTok video -> YouTube Short, X native video,
          LinkedIn (if professional)

    Provide Adaptation Rules (DO: adjust tone, optimize format,
    platform-appropriate CTAs, stagger timing, customize hooks.
    DO NOT: copy-paste identical content, leave in platform-
    specific elements, ignore length limits, post simultaneously
    everywhere, reuse identical hashtags). Provide a Timing
    Strategy (primary platform first with the best version;
    secondary 2-4 hours later; tertiary 24-48 hours later;
    evergreen weeks/months later). Close with a Weekly Content
    Production Flow (Mon create core; Tue primary push; Wed
    repurpose wave 1; Thu repurpose wave 2; Fri engagement +
    community; weekend maintenance + prep).


STEP 7: Channel Strategy Synthesis and Handoff

    Compile everything into platform playbooks and a copy-paste
    output block that feeds the downstream recipes. Generate a
    one-page Platform Strategy Card per platform (handle, tier,
    priority score, target personas, posting frequency, top
    formats, content-pillar mix percentages, key tactics, and
    an AVOID line). Then emit the CHANNEL STRATEGY OUTPUT BLOCK
    containing: PLATFORM_TIERS, FREQUENCY_SUMMARY,
    PERSONA_DISTRIBUTION, FORMAT_PRIORITIES, ENGAGEMENT_TARGETS,
    CROSS_POSTING_PRIORITY, and OPTIMAL_TIMING per platform.

    This block is the input for the Campaign Timeline Architect
    (RCP-004-002-005), the Content Calendar Generator
    (RCP-004-003-001), the Social Post Creator
    (RCP-004-003-002), and the Blog Content Planner
    (RCP-004-003-003). Close by confirming the Strategic Layer
    is complete (Campaign Architecture RCP-004-002-001,
    Messaging Matrix RCP-004-002-002, Content Pillars
    RCP-004-002-003, Channel Strategy RCP-004-002-004),
    recommending the next recipe (Campaign Timeline Architect,
    RCP-004-002-005), and asking the user to confirm the
    platform tier assignments and frequencies are realistic for
    their capacity.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: How many platforms should I focus on?

A: For part-time solo operators, focus on 2-3 Tier 1
   platforms maximum. Add more only after establishing a
   consistent rhythm on your primary platforms.

Q: Can I just cross-post identical content?

A: No. Each platform has unique culture and format
   preferences. Adapt tone, format, and CTAs for each
   platform, even when repurposing the same core content.

Q: How do I choose which platforms to prioritize?

A: Use the Priority Score formula: Audience Fit (40%) +
   Growth Potential (25%) + Effort Efficiency (20%) +
   Strategic Importance (15%). Focus where your target
   personas are most active.

Q: What if I cannot maintain the recommended frequencies?

A: Reduce to sustainable levels. Consistency beats volume -
   better to post 3x/week consistently than 10x then 0.
   Adjust tier assignments as needed.

Q: Should I automate cross-posting?

A: Semi-automation with manual review works best. Fully
   automated identical posts perform poorly and can damage
   your reputation on platforms that value authenticity.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Maggie (Strategic Campaign
   Architect) as the default for the Campaign Planning
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona file;
   the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe creates platform-specific strategies with
detailed playbooks for each active channel that respect
platform culture while maintaining brand consistency.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for platform terms-of-service
   considerations and automation/growth-tactic policies.

2. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Maggie (Strategic
   Campaign Architect) carried from the Campaign Architecture
   and Messaging Matrix recipes. Load CAMPAIGN_PERSONA if
   available, else activate the bundled Maggie default.

3. PLATFORM AUDIT: Assess current state and opportunity per
   platform; calculate priority scores; assign platform tiers.

4. PLATFORM PERSONA FIT: Map which personas spend time on
   which platforms; define content implications per platform.

5. FREQUENCY PLANNING: Set posting frequency per platform per
   phase; produce a weekly posting schedule template.

6. FORMAT OPTIMIZATION: Define best content formats per
   platform; create platform format playbooks.

7. ENGAGEMENT TACTICS: Define platform-specific engagement
   strategies; create the engagement tactics library.

8. CROSS-POSTING STRATEGY: Define content adaptation and
   distribution workflow; create the repurposing matrix and
   weekly production flow.

9. SYNTHESIS AND HANDOFF: Compile platform strategy cards and
   the Channel Strategy Output Block for downstream recipes.

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Campaign Architecture output (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Messaging Matrix output (RCP-004-002-002)

OPTIONAL:
    - Content Pillar output (RCP-004-002-003)
    - Current metrics baseline
    - Platform handles

FEEDS INTO:
    - Campaign Timeline Architect (RCP-004-002-005)
    - Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001)
    - Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002)
    - Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is the CHANNEL_STRATEGY_OUTPUT_BLOCK containing
platform tier assignments, frequency summary per platform,
persona distribution, format priorities, engagement targets,
cross-posting priority, and optimal timing per platform.
Secondary outputs include Platform Strategy Cards (one-page
playbook per platform).


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Creates platform-specific strategies with frequency, format,
tactics, and engagement approaches. Develops detailed
playbooks for each active channel that respect platform
culture while maintaining brand consistency.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe after completing the Campaign Architecture
(RCP-004-002-001), Messaging Matrix (RCP-004-002-002), and
Content Pillar (RCP-004-002-003) recipes, and before creating
content calendars.

IDEAL TIMING:
    - After the strategic foundation is complete
    - Before content calendar creation
    - When the platform list is finalized
    - When resource constraints are clear

PREREQUISITES:
    - Campaign Architecture Output Block (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Messaging Matrix Output Block (RCP-004-002-002)
    - Content Pillar Output Block (RCP-004-002-003, optional)
    - List of active platforms
    - Resource constraints (time, team, tools)

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Content Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003)
    - Precedes: Campaign Timeline Architect (RCP-004-002-005)
    - Feeds: Content execution recipes (RCP-004-003-001/002/003)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: B2B SaaS Product Launch

    Campaign: Enterprise software launch
    Platforms: LinkedIn, X/Twitter, YouTube, Dev.to, GitHub,
        Bluesky (6 platforms)
    Resources: Solo, part-time
    Current State: New on most platforms

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces platform tiering (Tier 1
    LinkedIn + X/Twitter daily; Tier 2 YouTube regular; Tier 3
    Dev.to + Bluesky maintenance; Tier 4 GitHub presence only),
    a moderate-capacity weekly volume of ~25 pieces achievable
    through strategic repurposing, an engagement strategy
    (primary daily, secondary when posting, tertiary weekly
    check-ins), and a cross-posting workflow with the LinkedIn
    carousel as content hub repurposed to 4+ platforms.
    Confidence: 85% - achievable with discipline.
    {PERSONA_NAME} note: "For solo part-time, drop to Tier 1+2
    only for Phase 1. Build your systems before expanding."


Example 2: Consumer App Launch

    Campaign: Fitness app launch (3 months)
    Platforms: TikTok, Instagram, YouTube, X/Twitter, Facebook
        (5 platforms)
    Resources: Small team, full-time
    Current State: Established on 2 platforms

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces platform tiering (Tier 1
    TikTok + Instagram daily, visual-first for fitness; Tier 2
    YouTube weekly long-form; Tier 3 X/Twitter + Facebook
    maintenance), an intensive-capacity weekly volume of ~50+
    pieces with a video-first repurposing strategy, and an
    engagement strategy (TikTok heavy in first hour; Instagram
    Stories + DMs; YouTube community tab active). Confidence:
    90% - a well-resourced team can execute.

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires output from the Campaign
   Architecture (RCP-004-002-001) and Messaging Matrix
   (RCP-004-002-002) recipes, and optionally the Content
   Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003). The strategic foundation
   informs platform-specific decisions.

2. PLATFORM CULTURE: Each platform has unique culture.
   X/Twitter rewards threads, LinkedIn rewards stories, TikTok
   rewards authenticity. Never copy-paste identical content.

3. RESOURCE REALITY: Be honest about capacity. Part-time solo
   operators should focus on 2-3 Tier 1 platforms maximum. Add
   more only after establishing consistent rhythm.

4. ENGAGEMENT PRIORITY: Posting is half the work. Engagement
   (responding, initiating, participating) builds real
   community. Budget time accordingly.

5. CROSS-POSTING EFFICIENCY: The goal is one core piece of
   content adapted to 4+ platforms. This requires planning but
   dramatically reduces total content creation burden.

6. TIMING FLEXIBILITY: Optimal posting times are starting
   points. Test and adjust based on your specific audience
   analytics.

7. QUARTERLY REVIEW: Platforms change constantly. Review and
   update channel strategy quarterly to reflect algorithm
   changes, new features, and performance data.

8. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: The Channel Strategy Output Block feeds
   the Campaign Timeline Architect (RCP-004-002-005), Content
   Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001), Social Post Creator
   (RCP-004-003-002), and Blog Content Planner
   (RCP-004-003-003).

9. PLATFORM TIER vs PERSONA: The Tier 1-4 labels in this
   recipe are PLATFORM-prioritization tiers (priority-score
   driven), not persona tiers. Personas in this cookbook are
   tier-less.

# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-002-005-TIMELINE-ARCH

Description: Transforms strategic campaign elements into a
week-by-week execution timeline with themes, milestones,
escalation patterns, and blog integration. Creates the
temporal backbone that connects strategy to daily execution -
mapping campaign architecture, messaging, and content pillars
onto a dated calendar with intensity curves and milestone
content windows. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (the campaign
strategist bundled with this cookbook) for timeline
development and execution planning.

    escalation-modeling, blog-integration, campaign-execution,

Recipe Recommended Personas: Maggie (Strategic Campaign
