Recipe Difficulty: Advanced


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
        - Proprietary campaign information
        - Competitive timing intelligence
        - Platform-specific algorithm details
    If a potential conflict is detected, note that the
    timeline may involve sensitive business timing and keep
    dates and strategy confidential as requested.


STEP 0.5: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Campaign Planning
    persona, Maggie (Strategic Campaign Architect), carried
    forward from the Campaign Architecture recipe
    (RCP-004-002-001) and through the messaging, pillar, and
    channel recipes. The persona object is stored in
    PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default.

    IF CAMPAIGN_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Maggie (Strategic
        Campaign Architect). Maggie works peer-to-peer,
        metrics-forward, and direct - she maps strategy onto
        the calendar and builds momentum, not just task lists.

    Maggie's focus for this recipe is timeline development and
    execution planning: multi-channel campaign strategy,
    campaign timing and pacing, customer journey mapping, and
    content calendar architecture. Methodology: RACE
    (Reach, Act, Convert, Engage) + Agile Marketing, expressed
    as timeline visualizations, escalation curves, and
    milestone mapping, with confidence percentages on timing
    recommendations.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Opening:

    "Let us dive into your campaign objectives and build
    something remarkable. We are taking all our strategic work
    - architecture, messaging, content pillars - and mapping
    it onto the calendar. This is where campaigns become real.

    A well-designed timeline does not just organize tasks; it
    creates momentum. Let us build that momentum together."


STEP 1: Input Validation and Context Loading

    Validate strategic inputs and load campaign context.

    REQUIRED INPUT VERIFICATION. If any required input is
    missing or empty, halt and request it - do not invent
    phases, themes, or pillars:
        - campaign_architecture (from Campaign Architecture,
          RCP-004-002-001) - extract campaign_name, total
          duration, phase_count, phase definitions (names,
          durations), escalation model (gradual/burst/
          sustained/wave), milestone list, resource
          constraints.
        - messaging_matrix (from Messaging Matrix,
          RCP-004-002-002) - extract phase messaging themes,
          pillar activation by phase, key moment scripts.
        - content_pillars (from Content Pillar Planner,
          RCP-004-002-003) - extract pillar definitions
          (categories), phase ratios (mix per phase), topic
          bank.

    OPTIONAL INPUT PROCESSING:
        - channel_strategy (from Channel Strategy Developer,
          RCP-004-002-004) - if provided, extract platform
          frequencies, optimal posting times, and platform
          priorities to optimize timing per platform. If
          absent, fall back to default platform timing
          (X/Twitter daily ~9am/12pm; LinkedIn 3-5/week ~8am/
          12pm; YouTube weekly ~Thu 3pm; TikTok 3-4/week ~7pm/
          9pm) and note that running Channel Strategy first is
          recommended.

    DATE VALIDATION:
        - Validate start_date (YYYY-MM-DD); if invalid, ask
          for the campaign start date and await response.
        - Calculate end_date = start_date + total_duration and
          total_weeks.
        - Process key_milestones: validate each format, sort
          chronologically, and flag any milestone outside the
          campaign window.

    Close with a {PERSONA_NAME} Context Summary echoing
    campaign overview (name, duration/weeks, start-end,
    phases, escalation model), which strategic inputs loaded,
    and the count of key milestones identified.


STEP 2: Week Definition

    Define the weekly structure with dates and phase
    alignment.

    GENERATE WEEK GRID: for each week (Week 1 to total),
    compute week_number, week_start_date (from start_date),
    week_end_date (+6 days), and phase_assignment, plus a
    phase_position of early/middle/late.

    PHASE BOUNDARY MARKING: identify phase transitions; mark
    each transition week, note its phase-shift implications,
    and flag any milestone overlap.

    Emit a WEEK_GRID_TABLE (Week | Dates | Phase | Position).
    Close with a {PERSONA_NAME} Week Definition Analysis:
    phase-by-phase week ranges and durations, longest/shortest
    phase, and the weeks on which phase transitions occur
    (transition weeks get dedicated transition content).


STEP 3: Theme Assignment

    Assign primary themes to each week based on phase
    messaging.

    THEME MAPPING LOGIC: retrieve phase messaging themes from
    the messaging_matrix. For each week, determine its phase,
    its primary phase_theme, and its position, then apply
    theme modulation:
        - early   -> focus "Introduction/Setup", building
          awareness
        - middle  -> focus "Deep dive", peak engagement
        - late    -> focus "Transition/Summary", preparing for
          the next phase
    Assign a weekly_theme = primary theme + weekly focus +
    messaging priority (from pillar activation) + supporting
    themes.

    THEME VARIATION STRATEGY: prevent theme fatigue - if a
    phase exceeds 4 weeks, introduce sub-themes within the
    main theme, rotate emphasis across messaging pillars, and
    plan "change of pace" weeks. Ensure theme coherence so
    adjacent weeks flow logically and transitions feel
    natural, not abrupt.

    Emit a THEME_CALENDAR (Week | Primary Theme | Weekly
    Focus). Close with a {PERSONA_NAME} Theme Strategy: phase
    themes applied, the theme rhythm pattern (introduce ->
    deepen -> summarize/transition), and how this builds a
    storytelling arc within each phase while keeping overall
    coherence.


STEP 4: Milestone Placement

    Place milestones on the timeline with pre/post content
    planning.

    MILESTONE CLASSIFICATION: classify each milestone by type
    (LAUNCH = product launches, beta openings, feature
    releases; EVENT = holidays, industry events, company
    dates; CAMPAIGN = phase transitions, promotion peaks,
    community moments; EXTERNAL = partner activities, market
    events, seasonal factors). For each, assign an impact
    level (HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW), compute weeks-from-start, and note
    content implications.

    MILESTONE CONTENT WINDOWS: for each HIGH/MEDIUM milestone,
    define a pre-window (HIGH: 2-3 weeks before, build
    anticipation/tease; MEDIUM: 1 week before, announce/
    prepare) and a post-window (HIGH: 1-2 weeks after,
    celebrate/showcase results; MEDIUM: 3-5 days after, quick
    recap/move forward), and flag those weeks for milestone
    content.

    MILESTONE CONFLICT DETECTION: if multiple HIGH milestones
    fall within 2 weeks, caution on clustering and recommend
    spreading or combining messaging. If a milestone lands on
    a phase transition, note the overlap and recommend using
    the milestone to amplify the transition message.

    Emit a MILESTONE_CALENDAR (Week | Date | Milestone | Type
    | Prep). Close with a {PERSONA_NAME} Milestone Analysis
    grouping milestones by impact tier (with prep lead times),
    milestone density by phase, and the flagged critical prep
    windows.


STEP 5: Intensity Mapping

    Map posting intensity based on the escalation model and
    phase progression.

    ESCALATION MODEL APPLICATION: retrieve escalation_model
    from campaign_architecture and apply the matching pattern:
        - GRADUAL: steady low-to-high climb (~40% building ->
          100% peak), linear progression with a slight curve.
        - BURST: concentrated peaks (~50% maintenance baseline,
          ~80% pre-milestone, 100% milestone weeks, ~60%
          post-milestone), driven by milestone proximity.
        - SUSTAINED: consistent high activity (75-85%
          throughout, ~95% at milestones, ~70% at transition
          resets), minimal variation.
        - WAVE: cyclical peaks and valleys (build 50->75% ->
          100% crest -> 60% recovery -> 40% trough), typically
          a 3-4 week cycle.

    INTENSITY TO POSTS TRANSLATION: define base posts/week per
    platform (X/Twitter 7, LinkedIn 4, YouTube 1, TikTok 4,
    Bluesky 5, Mastodon 4, Dev.to 1, GitHub 0.5). For each
    week and platform, actual_posts = ROUND(base x intensity/
    100), with a minimum of 1 for active platforms and a
    maximum of 2x base for peaks.

    Emit an INTENSITY_CHART (ASCII bar chart of the escalation
    curve) and a WEEKLY_POST_COUNTS table (Week | Int% | per-
    platform counts | Blog). Close with a {PERSONA_NAME}
    Intensity Analysis: pattern description, peak/build/
    recovery weeks, weekly content volume (low/average/peak),
    and an approximate content-creation hours/week at peak
    (with a confidence note, e.g. ~75%, varying by content
    complexity).


STEP 6: Blog Integration

    Integrate blog content with weekly themes and social
    amplification.

    BLOG CADENCE APPLICATION: apply blog_cadence
    (twice-weekly ~8/month; weekly ~4/month; bi-weekly
    ~2/month; monthly ~1/month) and compute total_blogs =
    total_weeks x blogs_per_week.

    BLOG-THEME ALIGNMENT: for each blog slot, retrieve the
    weekly theme, phase messaging, and content-pillar ratios,
    then assign a blog focus that matches the weekly theme,
    ensures pillar variety across blogs, and aligns with
    milestone content where applicable. Build a blog_entry per
    slot (week, publish date - optimal Tue/Thu, topic category
    from pillars, theme alignment, title direction, social
    amplification platforms, CTA focus).

    BLOG-SOCIAL COORDINATION: for each blog, plan a 3-day
    promotion cycle - pre (teaser 1-2 days before, "coming
    soon" hook), launch day (primary announcement across
    platforms, platform-adapted), and post (pull quotes/
    highlights 2-3 days after, discussion prompts, thread/
    carousel expansion).

    Emit a BLOG_SCHEDULE (Week | Publish | Topic Direction |
    Social) plus a Blog-Pillar Distribution summary
    (Educational / Behind-the-Scenes / Thought Leadership /
    Promotional counts and percentages). Close with a
    {PERSONA_NAME} Blog Strategy: total blogs over the
    campaign, blog rhythm/optimal days, pillar balance, and
    the per-blog amplification cycle.


STEP 7: Visual Timeline Generation

    Create visual timeline representations.

    Emit a MASTER_TIMELINE (ASCII): a header (campaign name,
    start-end dates), a PHASES band (name, week range, theme
    per phase), a MILESTONES row (week markers with milestone
    labels), and an INTENSITY CURVE row (per-week intensity
    percentages). Then emit a COMPACT_WEEKLY_VIEW table (Week
    | Theme | Milestones | Intensity/Posts).

    Close with a {PERSONA_NAME} Timeline Visualization: how to
    read the timeline (phases, milestone markers, intensity
    bars, content volume) and the quick reference points -
    campaign peak week, critical milestone weeks, phase
    transition weeks, and the highest-volume week.


STEP 8: Timeline Summary Output and Handoff

    Generate the complete timeline output block for downstream
    recipes.

    Emit the CAMPAIGN_TIMELINE_OUTPUT_BLOCK (copy-paste ready)
    containing:
        - TIMELINE METADATA: campaign, duration, total weeks,
          phases, escalation model, blog cadence, total blog
          posts planned.
        - PHASE SUMMARY: per phase - weeks, dates, theme,
          intensity range, key milestones, blog count.
        - WEEKLY TIMELINE DETAIL: per week - phase, theme,
          focus, milestones, intensity %, estimated posts
          (per platform), blog topic, messaging priority.
        - MILESTONE REGISTRY: Date | Week | Milestone | Type |
          Impact.
        - BLOG SCHEDULE REGISTRY: Week | Publish | Topic
          Direction | Pillar.
        - INTENSITY SCHEDULE: Week | Intensity | Posts |
          Primary Focus.

    Provide a TIMELINE QUICK REFERENCE CARD (duration, phases,
    escalation, blog cadence/total, key milestones, critical
    weeks, content volume).

    USAGE: this block provides temporal structure for the
    content-execution recipes - Content Calendar Generator
    (RCP-004-003-001) uses the WEEKLY DETAIL, Social Post
    Creator (RCP-004-003-002) references weekly themes, and
    Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003) uses the BLOG
    REGISTRY. Close with a {PERSONA_NAME} Closing Summary
    (timeline architecture recap, what it enables, a
    confidence assessment, and the next recommended recipe),
    then recommend the user confirm the timeline before
    proceeding.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: What if I need to adjust the timeline mid-campaign?

A: The modular structure supports phase-by-phase
   regeneration. Update the CAMPAIGN_TIMELINE_OUTPUT_BLOCK
   directly and re-run the downstream recipes for the
   affected weeks.

Q: How flexible is the intensity mapping?

A: Intensity percentages are guidelines. The escalation
   model provides the pattern, but actual numbers should be
   adjusted with real performance data and your true content
   capacity.

Q: Can I use a different blog cadence than the options
   provided?

A: Yes. The recipe handles any cadence. Common options are
   twice-weekly, weekly, bi-weekly, and monthly, but you can
   specify a custom cadence.

Q: What if milestones cluster in the same weeks?

A: The recipe flags milestone clustering and recommends
   either spreading milestones or combining messaging.
   Intentional clustering for a big launch moment is valid
   but requires increased capacity planning.

Q: How do I handle external milestones I cannot control?

A: Mark them as EXTERNAL type with the appropriate impact
   level. Plan content windows around them, but keep
   flexibility for date changes.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Maggie (Strategic Campaign
   Architect) as the default for the Campaign Planning
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona file;
   the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe transforms strategic campaign elements into a
week-by-week execution timeline.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for proprietary campaign
   information and competitive timing intelligence.

2. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Maggie (Strategic
   Campaign Architect) carried from the Campaign Architecture
   recipe. Load CAMPAIGN_PERSONA if available, else activate
   the bundled Maggie default.

3. INPUT VALIDATION: Verify required inputs from Campaign
   Architecture (RCP-004-002-001), Messaging Matrix
   (RCP-004-002-002), and Content Pillar Planner
   (RCP-004-002-003). Extract phases, themes, and content
   pillars.

4. WEEK DEFINITION: Generate a week grid with dates, phase
   assignments, and position indicators.

5. THEME ASSIGNMENT: Map messaging themes to weeks based on
   phase progression and position.

6. MILESTONE PLACEMENT: Position milestones on the timeline
   with pre/post content windows and conflict detection.

7. INTENSITY MAPPING: Apply the escalation model to generate
   weekly intensity percentages and translate to post counts.

8. BLOG INTEGRATION: Schedule blog posts aligned with weekly
   themes and social amplification.

9. VISUAL TIMELINE: Generate ASCII visualizations of the
   complete campaign timeline.

10. SYNTHESIS: Package all outputs into the
    CAMPAIGN_TIMELINE_OUTPUT_BLOCK for downstream recipes.

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Campaign Architecture output (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Messaging Matrix output (RCP-004-002-002)
    - Content Pillar Planner output (RCP-004-002-003)

OPTIONAL:
    - Channel Strategy Developer output (RCP-004-002-004)

FEEDS INTO:
    - Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001)
    - Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002)
    - Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is the CAMPAIGN_TIMELINE_OUTPUT_BLOCK
containing timeline metadata, phase summary with milestones,
weekly timeline detail (themes, intensity), a milestone
registry, a blog schedule registry, and an intensity
schedule. Visual outputs include the Master Timeline,
Intensity Chart, and Compact Weekly View.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Transforms strategic campaign elements into a week-by-week
execution timeline with themes, milestones, escalation
patterns, and blog integration. Creates the temporal backbone
connecting strategy to daily execution.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe after completing Campaign Architecture
(RCP-004-002-001), Messaging Matrix (RCP-004-002-002),
Content Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003), and ideally Channel
Strategy Developer (RCP-004-002-004). This is the final
strategic recipe in the Campaign Planning section before
moving to content execution.

IDEAL TIMING:
    - After all strategic foundation work is complete
    - Before content calendar creation
    - When campaign dates are confirmed
    - When external milestones are known

PREREQUISITES:
    - Campaign Architecture Output Block (RCP-004-002-001)
    - Messaging Matrix Output Block (RCP-004-002-002)
    - Content Pillar Output Block (RCP-004-002-003)
    - Start date (YYYY-MM-DD format)
    - Key milestones with dates (optional)
    - Blog cadence preference

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Campaign Architecture (RCP-004-002-001),
      Messaging Matrix (RCP-004-002-002), Content Pillar
      Planner (RCP-004-002-003), Channel Strategy Developer
      (RCP-004-002-004)
    - Precedes: Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001)
    - Precedes: Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002)
    - Precedes: Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: B2B SaaS Product Launch

    Campaign: Enterprise software launch (6 months)
    Start Date: 2026-01-15
    Escalation Model: GRADUAL
    Blog Cadence: weekly
    Key Milestones: Beta Launch (2026-03-01), Public Launch
        (2026-04-15), Feature Release (2026-06-01)

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} maps 26 weeks (Jan 15 - Jul 15,
    2026) across 5 phases with distinct themes, a gradual
    escalation from 40% to 100% intensity, milestone mapping
    (Week 7 Beta Launch HIGH impact with 2-week prep; Week 13
    Public Launch HIGH impact with 3-week prep; Week 20
    Feature Release MEDIUM impact), 26 scheduled blog posts,
    ~450 total social posts planned, and a peak week of 28
    posts at 100% intensity. Confidence: 85% - solid execution
    framework.


Example 2: Consumer App Launch

    Campaign: Fitness app launch (3 months)
    Start Date: 2026-03-01
    Escalation Model: BURST
    Blog Cadence: bi-weekly
    Key Milestones: Early Access (2026-04-01), Public Launch
        (2026-05-15)

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} maps 12 weeks (Mar 1 - May 31,
    2026) across 3 phases with burst escalation (50% baseline,
    100% peaks at milestones), milestone mapping (Week 5 Early
    Access HIGH impact, burst; Week 11 Public Launch HIGH
    impact, burst), 6 scheduled blog posts, ~180 total social
    posts planned, and two burst peaks at 100% intensity.
    Confidence: 90% - concentrated execution approach.

# =========================================================
# PERSONA CONFIGURATION

# Default Campaign Persona - stored in PROJECT_VARIABLES for
# persistence across the Campaign Planning section. Users may
# attach a custom persona to override. This cookbook bundles
# the tier-less Maggie
# (PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MAGGIE-CARD.txt).

CAMPAIGN_PERSONA = {
    "name": "Maggie",
    "title": "Strategic Campaign Architect",
    "greeting": "Let us map your strategy onto the calendar -
        themes, milestones, and momentum, week by week.",
    "methodology": "RACE (Reach, Act, Convert, Engage) +
        Agile Marketing",
    "formality": 6,
    "explanation_depth": "concise",
    "file_reference": "PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-MAGGIE-CARD.txt"
}

PERSONA_NAME = CAMPAIGN_PERSONA["name"]
PERSONA_TITLE = CAMPAIGN_PERSONA["title"]
PERSONA_GREETING = CAMPAIGN_PERSONA["greeting"]
PERSONA_METHODOLOGY = CAMPAIGN_PERSONA["methodology"]


# =========================================================
# RECIPE DEFINITION
# =========================================================

CAMPAIGN_TIMELINE_ARCHITECT = Recipe(
    recipe_id="RCP-004-002-005-TIMELINE-ARCH-v3.00a",
    title="Campaign Timeline Architect",
    description="""
        Transforms strategic campaign elements into a

        milestones, escalation patterns, and blog

        connects strategy to daily execution. Activates
        {PERSONA_NAME} (Strategic Campaign Architect) to guide

    """,
    category="CAT-004-BRAND-IDENTITY",
    subcategory="SUBCAT-002-CAMPAIGN-PLANNING",
    difficulty="advanced",
    estimated_time="35-45 minutes",
    version="3.00a",

    dependencies={
        "required_inputs": [
            {
                "source": "RCP-004-002-001-CAMPAIGN-ARCH",
                "input": "campaign_architecture",
                "description": "Phases, milestones, and
                    escalation model"

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires output from Campaign
   Architecture (RCP-004-002-001), Messaging Matrix
   (RCP-004-002-002), and Content Pillar Planner
   (RCP-004-002-003). Channel Strategy Developer
   (RCP-004-002-004) is optional but recommended for
   optimized platform timing.

2. ESCALATION MODELS: Four escalation patterns are supported -
   GRADUAL (steady increase low to high), BURST (concentrated
   high-intensity at milestones), SUSTAINED (consistent high
   activity throughout), and WAVE (cyclical peaks and
   valleys).

3. MILESTONE TYPES: Four milestone classifications - LAUNCH
   (product launches, beta openings), EVENT (holidays,
   industry events), CAMPAIGN (phase transitions, promotion
   peaks), and EXTERNAL (partner activities, market events).

4. INTENSITY TRANSLATION: Base posts per week are multiplied
   by the intensity percentage. Minimum is 1 post for active
   platforms; maximum is 2x base for peak weeks.

5. BLOG INTEGRATION: Blog posts are automatically distributed
   across the campaign with a 3-day social promotion cycle
   (teaser, launch, highlights).

6. VISUAL OUTPUTS: ASCII visualizations are designed for
   plaintext environments. They can be converted to graphical
   formats for presentations.

7. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: The CAMPAIGN_TIMELINE_OUTPUT_BLOCK
   feeds the Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001),
   Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002), and Blog Content
   Planner (RCP-004-003-003).

8. ADJUSTMENTS: The timeline can be regenerated phase-by-phase
   if external factors require changes. The modular structure
   supports partial updates.

# =========================================================

    - {PERSONA_METHODOLOGY} - Persona methodology approach
    - {date} - Date of output block generation

    (promoted from the former metadata changelog block).

# recipe's content is content-execution calendaring, so it is

# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-003-001-CONTENT-CAL

Description: Transforms campaign timeline, channel strategy,
and content pillars into specific, actionable content slots
with dates, platforms, content types, topics, and CTAs.
Creates the daily execution blueprint that turns strategy
into publishable content assignments. As the first recipe in
the Content Execution section, it activates {PERSONA_NAME}
(the multi-channel content strategist bundled with this
cookbook) for the section's calendar and content work.


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 003

Recipe ID Numbers: 001

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Content Execution

Recipe Tags:
    content-calendar, scheduling, editorial-planning,
    multi-channel, content-batching, cta-strategy,
    essential, frequently-used

Recipe Recommended Personas: Quinn (Multi-Channel Content
    Strategist) - bundled default for the Content Execution
    section

Recipe Difficulty: Advanced


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
        - Proprietary content strategies
        - Competitive posting patterns
        - Platform-specific algorithm gaming
    If potential conflict detected, note that the calendar
    may involve sensitive scheduling strategies, keep
    calendar details confidential as requested, and keep
    recommendations focused on authentic, defensible content.


STEP 0.5: Persona Activation and Continuity

    This recipe is the ENTRY POINT of the Content Execution
    section. It activates the cookbook's Content Execution
    persona, Quinn (Multi-Channel Content Strategist), and
    stores the CONTENT_PERSONA object in PROJECT_VARIABLES so
    the downstream content recipes (Social Post Creator,
    Blog Content Planner, Performance Analyzer) inherit it.
    Users may attach a custom persona to override the default.

    IF CONTENT_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Quinn (Multi-Channel
        Content Strategist) and store it in PROJECT_VARIABLES.
        Quinn is execution-focused and systems-minded - she
        turns strategy into a calendar you can actually run.

    Quinn's focus for this recipe is content-calendar
    development and batch planning: multi-channel content
    planning, editorial calendar management, content batching
    and efficiency, platform-specific optimization, and CTA
    strategy and placement. Methodology: RACE Framework +
    Content Matrix Planning; output style: calendar grids,
    content matrices, and batch plans; quality check:
    confidence percentages for content recommendations.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Opening:

    "Let us turn your strategy into a content machine. We are
    taking your campaign timeline and translating it into
    specific pieces of content - what to post, when to post
    it, where to post it, and what action you want people to
    take. By the end of this, you will have a calendar you can
    actually execute."


STEP 1: Input Validation and Scope Definition

    Validate required inputs and define calendar scope.

    1.1 REQUIRED INPUT VERIFICATION:

    CHECK campaign_timeline: if not provided or empty, signal
        that the Campaign Timeline from Timeline Architecture
        (RCP-004-002-005) is required and HALT. Extract:
        total_weeks, phase_definitions, weekly_themes,
        weekly_intensity, milestone_registry, blog_schedule
        (if present).

    CHECK channel_strategy: if not provided or empty, signal
        that the Channel Strategy from Channel Strategy
        Developer (RCP-004-002-004) is required and HALT.
        Extract: platform_playbooks, posting_frequencies,
        optimal_posting_times, platform_content_formats,
        engagement_tactics.

    CHECK content_pillars: if not provided or empty, signal
        that the Content Pillars from Content Pillar Planner
        (RCP-004-002-003) is required and HALT. Extract:
        pillar_definitions (5 categories), phase_ratios,
        topic_bank, format_recommendations.

    (Optional input: the Messaging Matrix from
    RCP-004-002-002 enhances content alignment when present.)

    1.2 SCOPE DEFINITION - process calendar_scope:
        - single-week: require scope_identifier (e.g.,
          "Week 3"); calendar_range = 1 week.
        - two-weeks: require scope_identifier (e.g., "Weeks
          3-4"); calendar_range = 2 weeks.
        - phase: require scope_identifier (e.g., "Phase 1");
          look up phase_weeks from campaign_timeline;
          calendar_range = phase duration.
        - full-campaign: calendar_range = total_weeks;
          caution that this is extensive and offer to start
          phase-by-phase instead.

    1.3 DETAIL LEVEL CONFIGURATION:
        - topics-only: slot = [date, platform, pillar,
          topic_direction]; ~2-3 min/slot to review.
        - with-hooks: slot = [date, platform, pillar,
          topic_direction, hook_idea, cta,
          hashtag_suggestions]; ~5-7 min/slot.
        - full-briefs: slot adds key_points,
          visual_recommendation, cross_post_notes;
          ~10-15 min/slot.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Scope Summary: confirm calendar scope,
    range, weeks covered, detail level, output format, and the
    loaded content sources (Campaign Timeline, Channel
    Strategy, Content Pillars; Messaging Matrix optional),
    then proceed.


STEP 2: Calendar Framework Creation

    Build the date structure and allocate platform slots.

    2.1 DATE GRID GENERATION: for each week in calendar_range,
    retrieve from campaign_timeline (week_number, date_range
    Mon-Sun, phase, weekly_theme, intensity_percentage,
    milestones, blog_slot). For each day (Mon-Sun), create a
    day_slot capturing date, day_of_week, week_number, phase,
    theme, intensity, is_milestone_day (+ milestone_name),
    is_blog_day, and an empty platform_slots list.

    2.2 PLATFORM SLOT ALLOCATION: retrieve posting_frequencies
    from channel_strategy and compute daily/weekly targets per
    platform (X/Twitter, LinkedIn, YouTube, TikTok, Bluesky,
    Mastodon, Dev.to, GitHub). Frequency function:
        adjusted = base_frequency * (intensity / 100),
        rounded with a minimum of 1.

    2.3 WEEKLY POST DISTRIBUTION: per week, compute total
    posts per platform and distribute across days -
    prioritize high-engagement days (Tue-Thu), avoid Sunday
    unless platform-appropriate, cluster around milestone
    days, and keep an even spread for consistency. Produce a
    weekly_distribution_map (per-day platform counts).

    2.4 FRAMEWORK OUTPUT: generate the CALENDAR_FRAMEWORK
    block with a weekly post-target table:

        CALENDAR FRAMEWORK - {scope_identifier}
        Dates: {start_date} to {end_date}
        -------------------------------------------
        WEEKLY POST TARGETS:
        | Week | X  | LI | YT | TT | BS | Blog | Other|
        |------|----|----|----|----|----|----- |------|
        | Wk N | {X}| {X}| {X}| {X}| {X}| {X}  | {X}  |
        -------------------------------------------

    {PERSONA_NAME} Framework Analysis: summarize total content
    slots, platform distribution, high-activity days, any
    milestone dates, and blog publication days.


STEP 3: Platform Slot Assignment

    Assign specific platform slots with optimal timing.

    3.1 SLOT CREATION LOGIC: for each day and each platform
    with posts scheduled, retrieve optimal_posting_times,
    preferred content_formats, and engagement_tactics from
    channel_strategy. For each post_slot, select a posting
    time (distribute across optimal times for multiple posts;
    use the primary optimal time for a single post) and create
    a content_slot with: slot_id (unique), date, day, week,
    platform, posting_time, phase, weekly_theme, and null
    placeholders for pillar, topic, content_type, hook, cta,
    and a notes list. Add it to the day's platform_slots.

    3.2 SPECIAL SLOT HANDLING:
        - Milestone days: flag all slots "milestone-related,"
          prioritize milestone messaging on primary platforms,
          add milestone_context to slot notes.
        - Blog publication days: create a blog_slot (slot_id
          "W{n}-{DAY}-BLOG-1", Blog platform, 10:00 AM,
          Long-form article, topic from blog_schedule,
          social_amplification ["X","LinkedIn"]) plus
          amplification slots on social - a teaser (day
          before), a launch announcement (same day), and a
          pull-quote slot (day after).

    3.3 PLATFORM SLOT SUMMARY: generate a SLOT_SUMMARY table
    (Platform | Slots | Typical Times) covering X/Twitter
    (9am, 12pm, 5pm), LinkedIn (8am, 12pm), YouTube (Thursday
    3pm), TikTok (7pm, 9pm), Bluesky (10am, 3pm), Blog
    ({blog_day} 10am), plus a TOTAL row.


STEP 4: Content Assignment

    Assign content pillars, topics, formats, and hooks.

    4.1 PILLAR DISTRIBUTION LOGIC: retrieve phase_ratios from
    content_pillars (e.g., Educational 40%, Behind-the-Scenes
    20%, Community 20%, Promotional 15%, Thought Leadership
    5%). For each pillar, target_slots = total_slots *
    (ratio/100), rounded, ensuring the sum equals total_slots.

    4.2 PILLAR ASSIGNMENT STRATEGY: assign pillars to slots
    via weighted distribution using priority rules -
        1. Milestone days: Promotional or Community
        2. Blog days: Educational (for the blog)
        3. Blog amplification: mix based on blog topic
        4. Monday: Educational (start week with value)
        5. Friday: Community or BTS (engagement focus)
        6. Primary platforms: balanced across pillars
        7. Technical platforms: Educational focus
    Avoid: same pillar on consecutive days on the same
    platform, promotional clustering, and all-educational on
    low-engagement days. Update slot.pillar and increment the
    per-pillar count.

    4.3 TOPIC ASSIGNMENT: from topic_bank[pillar], filter by
    weekly_theme alignment, platform appropriateness, and
    recency (avoid repetition); select per rules (milestone +
    Promotional -> milestone-specific; blog_amplification ->
    derived from blog topic; else best fit). Update slot.topic
    and mark the topic used for the week.

    4.4 CONTENT TYPE ASSIGNMENT: from format_recommendations
    (content_pillars) and platform_formats (channel_strategy),
    select a format per the PLATFORM_FORMAT_MATRIX -
        | Platform  | Primary Formats             |
        | X/Twitter | Text, Thread, Image, Poll   |
        | LinkedIn  | Text, Article, Carousel     |
        | YouTube   | Video (long), Shorts        |
        | TikTok    | Video (short), Duet         |
        | Bluesky   | Text, Thread, Image         |
        | Dev.to    | Article, Tutorial           |
    factoring platform primary formats, pillar format
    preferences, weekly variety (no repeats), and resource
    requirements. Update slot.content_type.

    4.5 HOOK GENERATION (if detail_level is with-hooks or
    full-briefs): for each slot, generate a hook from topic
    direction, platform conventions, weekly theme, and pillar
    approach, using per-pillar hook patterns -
        Educational: "Did you know...", "Here is how to...",
            "The mistake..."
        Behind-the-Scenes: "Here is what I am working on...",
            "Real talk:"
        Community: "Question for you:", "What is your
            experience with..."
        Promotional: "Exciting news:", "Limited time:",
            "Join us for..."
        Thought Leadership: "Hot take:", "The future of...",
            "Why I think..."
    Update slot.hook.

    4.6 PILLAR BALANCE CHECK: compute actual distribution per
    pillar, compare to target ratios, and flag any pillar more
    than 5% off (recommend swapping slots from over- to
    under-weighted pillars). Generate a PILLAR_BALANCE_REPORT
    table (Pillar | Target | Actual | Status).


STEP 5: CTA Mapping

    Assign calls-to-action to each content slot.

    5.1 CTA LIBRARY DEFINITION:
        PRIMARY (direct conversion): "Sign up for early
            access", "Join the waitlist", "Get started today",
            "Visit our website"
        ENGAGEMENT (community building): "What do you think?",
            "Share your experience", "Follow for more", "Join
            the conversation", "Tag someone who needs this"
        CONTENT (consumption): "Read the full article",
            "Watch the tutorial", "Check the thread below",
            "Link in bio"
        SOFT (awareness): "More coming soon", "Stay tuned",
            "This is just the beginning"

    5.2 CTA ASSIGNMENT LOGIC: per slot, determine cta_type by
    the pillar-CTA mapping -
        Educational: 60% Engagement, 30% Content, 10% Primary
        Behind-the-Scenes: 50% Engagement, 30% Soft,
            20% Primary
        Community: 80% Engagement, 10% Content, 10% Primary
        Promotional: 60% Primary, 25% Content, 15% Engagement
        Thought Leadership: 50% Engagement, 30% Content,
            20% Soft
    Select the specific CTA by platform conventions, content
    type (Thread -> "Check thread below"), phase urgency
    (closer to launch -> more Primary), and daily variety (no
    repeat CTA twice per day). Update slot.cta.

    5.3 CTA DISTRIBUTION CHECK: compute the distribution and
    verify balance - Primary 15-25% (not too salesy),
    Engagement 40-50% (community focus), Content 20-30%
    (drive consumption), Soft 5-15% (awareness).

    {PERSONA_NAME} CTA Analysis: report the distribution with
    assessment, where Primary CTAs concentrate, how Engagement
    CTAs spread, and the CTA focus on milestone days.


STEP 6: Calendar Generation

    Format the calendar output.

    6.1 DAILY VIEW FORMAT: for each day, generate a DAY_VIEW
    header (day name, date, week, phase, theme, intensity,
    milestone flag) followed by each content slot (time,
    platform, slot_id; pillar; type; topic; and, by detail
    level, hook, cta, key points, visual, hashtags) and a day
    total.

    6.2 WEEKLY SUMMARY VIEW: for each week, generate a
    WEEKLY_SUMMARY with a per-day platform-count grid
    (Mon-Sun across X, LI, YT, TT, BS, Other, Total), a totals
    row, and highlights (milestones, blogs, special notes).

    6.3 CSV-READY FORMAT (if output_format includes csv):
    emit CSV with header
        slot_id,date,day,week,platform,time,phase,theme,
        pillar,topic,content_type,hook,cta,hashtags,notes
    and one row per slot, ready for import into scheduling
    tools or spreadsheets.


STEP 7: Batch Identification

    Group content for efficient batch creation.

    7.1 BATCH GROUPING LOGIC - four strategies:
        1. BY_PLATFORM: group by platform; stay in platform
           mindset.
        2. BY_PILLAR: group by pillar; research once, create
           multiple.
        3. BY_FORMAT: group by format (threads, videos);
           efficient production workflow.
        4. BY_DAY: group by day; minimize context switching.
    Recommend by scope: single-week -> BY_DAY or BY_PLATFORM;
    phase -> BY_PILLAR or BY_FORMAT; full-campaign ->
    BY_FORMAT (especially video).

    7.2 BATCH OUTPUT: generate a BATCH_CREATION_GUIDE - per
    batch: name, content count, estimated creation time,
    included slot_ids (with brief descriptions), and
    preparation needed; plus a batch summary (total batches,
    total pieces, estimated total time) and a recommended
    creation schedule.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Batching Analysis: explain why the
    recommended strategy fits the scope, the time investment
    (batches, hours per batch, total), and the pro tip to
    block dedicated creation time per batch.


STEP 8: Calendar Output Block

    Package everything into the structured output block.

    8.1 STRUCTURED OUTPUT BLOCK - emit:

        === CONTENT_CALENDAR_BLOCK ===
        Generated: {date}
        Recipe: RCP-004-003-001-CONTENT-CAL-v3.00a

        CALENDAR METADATA - scope, range, dates, detail
            level, total content slots, active platforms.
        CONTENT DISTRIBUTION SUMMARY - by platform, by pillar
            (count + %), by CTA type (count + %).
        DAILY CALENDAR - full daily view from Step 6.1.
        WEEKLY SUMMARIES - from Step 6.2.
        BATCH CREATION GUIDE - from Step 7.2.
        MILESTONE CONTENT FOCUS - per milestone: pre-,
            day-of, and post-milestone slot_ids.
        BLOG AMPLIFICATION SCHEDULE - per blog: teaser,
            launch, and follow-up slot_ids.
        === END CONTENT_CALENDAR_BLOCK ===

    This block provides execution-ready content assignments
    for the Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002) - individual
    slots as input - plus direct scheduling, team assignments,
    and progress tracking.

    8.2 QUICK REFERENCE CARD: emit a bordered card with range,
    total content, detail level, daily average, busiest and
    quietest day, creation batches, estimated creation time,
    and recommended batch strategy.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Closing Summary: recap what the user has
    (total slots with platform/time/pillar/topic/CTA, batch
    count, estimated hours), next steps (take slots to the
    Social Post Creator RCP-004-003-002, use the batch guide
    to schedule creation, or export CSV), a confidence
    assessment (target ~85%), and the pro tip to batch and
    schedule rather than create everything at once.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: Should I generate the full campaign calendar at once or
   phase by phase?

A: For manageability, generate phase by phase. Full-campaign
   calendars are extensive and harder to review.
   Phase-by-phase allows adjustments based on performance
   data.

Q: What detail level should I choose?

A: Use "topics-only" for quick planning overviews,
   "with-hooks" for creation-ready calendars, and
   "full-briefs" for team handoffs or delegation.

Q: How do I handle content that does not fit the pillar
   ratios exactly?

A: The recipe flags variances over 5%. Small variances are
   acceptable; large ones may need slot swapping to maintain
   balance.

Q: Can I update the calendar after generating it?

A: Yes. Regenerate specific weeks or phases as needed. The
   modular structure supports partial updates without
   regenerating everything.

Q: What if I do not have time for all the content?

A: Reduce intensity in the Timeline Architecture recipe
   (RCP-004-002-005), or focus on primary platforms only.
   Quality and consistency beat volume.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Quinn (Multi-Channel Content
   Strategist) as the default for the Content Execution
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona file;
   the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe transforms campaign timeline, channel strategy,
and content pillars into specific, actionable content slots
with dates, platforms, content types, topics, and CTAs.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for proprietary content strategies
   and competitive posting patterns.

2. PERSONA ACTIVATION: Activate Quinn (Multi-Channel Content
   Strategist) and store CONTENT_PERSONA in PROJECT_VARIABLES
   for the Content Execution section; load it if already
   present.

3. INPUT VALIDATION: Verify required inputs from Content
   Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003), Channel Strategy
   Developer (RCP-004-002-004), and Timeline Architecture
   (RCP-004-002-005). Define calendar scope and detail level.

4. CALENDAR FRAMEWORK: Generate the date grid, allocate
   platform slots based on frequencies and intensity, and
   distribute posts across days.

5. PLATFORM SLOT ASSIGNMENT: Create specific content slots
   with unique IDs and optimal posting times, with special
   handling for milestones and blogs.

6. CONTENT ASSIGNMENT: Assign pillars via weighted
   distribution, select topics from the topic bank, determine
   content types, and generate hooks.

7. CTA MAPPING: Assign calls-to-action based on the
   pillar-CTA mapping and phase urgency.

8. CALENDAR GENERATION: Format daily views, weekly summaries,
   and optional CSV export.

9. BATCH IDENTIFICATION: Group content for efficient creation
   using the optimal batching strategy.

10. OUTPUT BLOCK: Package all outputs into the
    CONTENT_CALENDAR_BLOCK for execution.

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Campaign Timeline (RCP-004-002-005)
    - Channel Strategy (RCP-004-002-004)
    - Content Pillars (RCP-004-002-003)

OPTIONAL:
    - Messaging Matrix (RCP-004-002-002)

FEEDS INTO:
    - Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002)
    - Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)
    - Performance Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004)
    - Direct execution and scheduling tools

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is the CONTENT_CALENDAR_BLOCK containing
calendar metadata, content distribution summary (by platform,
pillar, CTA type), the daily calendar with all slots, weekly
summaries, the batch creation guide, milestone content focus,
and the blog amplification schedule.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Transforms campaign timeline into specific, actionable
content slots with dates, platforms, content types, topics,
and CTAs. Creates the daily execution blueprint for
publishable content.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe after completing the Campaign Planning
section (RCP-004-002-001 through RCP-004-002-005). This is
the first recipe in the Content Execution section (004-003).

IDEAL TIMING:
    - After the campaign timeline is complete
    - When ready to begin content creation
    - Before delegation to team members
    - When scheduling tools need populating

PREREQUISITES:
    - Campaign Timeline Output Block (RCP-004-002-005)
    - Channel Strategy Output Block (RCP-004-002-004)
    - Content Pillar Output Block (RCP-004-002-003)
    - Scope decision (single-week, phase, etc.)
    - Detail level preference

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Campaign Planning section (RCP-004-002-001..005)
    - Precedes: Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002)
    - Precedes: Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)
    - Precedes: Performance Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004)


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: Single Week Calendar

    Scope: Week 3 of campaign
    Detail Level: with-hooks
    Output Format: structured-text

    Inputs: campaign_timeline (RCP-004-002-005),
        channel_strategy (RCP-004-002-004), content_pillars
        (RCP-004-002-003); calendar_scope "single-week";
        scope_identifier "Week 3"; detail_level "with-hooks".

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces 7 days of content slots,
    35 total content pieces (each with hook ideas and CTAs),
    pillar distribution (Educational 14/40%, Behind-the-Scenes
    7/20%, Community 7/20%, Promotional 5/14%, Thought
    Leadership 2/6%), and a BY_DAY batch recommendation
    (7 batches, ~2 hours each, ~14 hours total). Confidence:
    85%.


Example 2: Phase Calendar

    Scope: Phase 2 - Momentum Building
    Detail Level: full-briefs
    Output Format: both (structured + CSV)

    Inputs: calendar_scope "phase"; scope_identifier
        "Phase 2"; detail_level "full-briefs"; output_format
        "both".

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces 6 weeks of content slots,
    210 total content pieces with full briefs for team
    handoff, a CSV export ready for import into Buffer or
    Hootsuite, and a BY_PILLAR batch recommendation (5 batches,
    ~8-10 hours each, ~45 hours total). Confidence: 80% -
    large scope requires flexibility.

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires output from the Content
   Pillar Planner (RCP-004-002-003), Channel Strategy
   Developer (RCP-004-002-004), and Timeline Architecture
   (RCP-004-002-005). The Messaging Matrix (RCP-004-002-002)
   is optional but enhances content alignment.

2. SECTION ENTRY POINT: As the first recipe in the Content
   Execution section, it activates Quinn (Multi-Channel
   Content Strategist) and stores CONTENT_PERSONA in
   PROJECT_VARIABLES for the downstream content recipes.

3. SCOPE SELECTION: single-week for detailed creation
   planning; phase for most use cases; full-campaign for an
   overview only (detail later).

4. DETAIL LEVELS: topics-only (~2-3 min/slot), with-hooks
   (~5-7 min/slot), full-briefs (~10-15 min/slot).

5. PILLAR DISTRIBUTION: Content is distributed across pillars
   based on phase ratios from the Content Pillar Planner;
   variances over 5% are flagged for review.

6. CTA BALANCE: Primary CTAs (conversion-focused) should not
   exceed 25% of total; the recipe checks distribution and
   flags imbalances.

7. BATCH STRATEGIES: BY_PLATFORM (solo creators), BY_PILLAR
   (research-heavy content), BY_FORMAT (video production),
   BY_DAY (daily publishing rhythm).

8. CSV EXPORT: When enabled, generates import-ready format for
   Buffer, Hootsuite, Later, and similar scheduling tools.

9. ITERATIVE USE: The recipe can be run multiple times for
   different scopes or to regenerate specific weeks based on
   performance data.

10. DOWNSTREAM RECIPES: Individual content slots can be passed
    to the Social Post Creator (RCP-004-003-002) for full copy
    generation, and the calendar feeds the Performance
    Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004).

# RE-HOME NOTE (SP11 H025, Richard-approved Option 1): this
# recipe composes platform-native social posts from calendar
# slots and the messaging matrix's message library, so it is

# =========================================================
# GENERAL SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Type: How-to Instructions

Name: RCP-004-003-002-SOCIAL-POST

Description: Generates platform-optimized, copy-paste-ready
social media content from content-calendar slots. Applies
brand voice, platform conventions, and engagement best
practices to produce publishable posts with A/B test
variations and visual specs. Composes from the messaging
matrix's message library so every post traces back to the
brand foundation. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (the content
strategist bundled with this cookbook) for platform-native
content creation.


# =========================================================
# CATEGORIES SECTION
# =========================================================

Multi-Recipe Combo Stages: Single Recipe

Recipe Is Part Of This Cookbook: CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID

Recipe Category ID Numbers: 004

Recipe Subcategory ID Numbers: 003

Recipe ID Numbers: 002

Recipe Status: Official

Recipe Categories:
    CFT-FWK-COOKBK-BRAND-ID - CRAFT Brand Identity Cookbook

Recipe Subcategories: Content Execution

Recipe Tags:
    social-media, content-creation, copywriting,
    platform-optimization, ab-testing, engagement,
    copy-paste-ready, multi-platform

Recipe Recommended Personas: Quinn (Multi-Channel Content
    Strategist) - bundled default; carries forward from the
    Content Calendar recipe (RCP-004-003-001)

Recipe Difficulty: Intermediate


# =========================================================
# INSTRUCTIONS SECTION
# =========================================================

STEP 0: Policy Pre-Check

    Scan prompt for sensitive categories:
        - Misleading claims about a product
        - Aggressive promotional tactics
        - Platform policy violations
    If a potential conflict is detected, note that the
    content may conflict with platform policies and adjust
    to comply with platform guidelines, keeping copy
    authentic and defensible.


STEP 0.5: Persona Continuity and Activation

    This recipe runs under the cookbook's Content Execution
    persona, Quinn (Multi-Channel Content Strategist),
    carried forward from the Content Calendar recipe
    (RCP-004-003-001). The persona object is stored in
    PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence. Users may attach a
    custom persona to override the default.

    IF CAMPAIGN_PERSONA is defined in PROJECT_VARIABLES:
        Continue with the established persona.
    ELSE:
        Activate the bundled default: Quinn (Multi-Channel
        Content Strategist).

    Quinn's focus for this recipe is platform-native content
    creation: platform-specific content optimization,
    copywriting for conversion, A/B testing and variations,
    visual content strategy, and engagement psychology.
    Methodology: Hook -> Body -> CTA structure with
    per-platform optimization; output is copy mockups with
    character counts and ready-to-publish content, plus
    engagement-likelihood estimates.

    {PERSONA_NAME} Opening:

    "Let us create content that converts. We are taking your
    calendar slots and turning them into actual posts -
    optimized for {target_platform}, aligned with your brand
    voice, and designed to drive engagement. Time to make
    this real."


STEP 1: Context Loading

    Load the content context and platform specifications.

    1.1 CALENDAR ENTRY PARSING: Parse the
    content_calendar_entry and extract slot_id, date, day,
    week, platform, posting_time, phase, weekly_theme,
    pillar, topic, content_type, hook (if provided), cta,
    and notes. If required fields are missing, request at
    minimum platform, pillar, topic, and cta, then halt.

    1.2 PLATFORM SPECIFICATION LOADING: Retrieve the
    platform_spec for the target platform (character_limit,
    optimal_length, hashtag_count, media_options,
    best_practices, avoid_list). Built-in specifications:

        X/Twitter: 280 chars (optimal 240-270); 2-3
            hashtags; links auto-shorten to 23 chars; thread
            support; hook in first line, line breaks, end
            with an engagement prompt.
        LinkedIn: 3000 chars (optimal 150-300 words); 3-5
            hashtags; link in first comment; strong hook in
            first 2 lines, white space, personal angle.
        YouTube: title 100 (optimal 50-60); description
            5000; 5-15 tags; keyword front-loaded, hook in
            first 5 seconds, timestamps.
        TikTok: caption 2200 (optimal 50-150); 3-5 hashtags;
            15-60s optimal; hook in 1-3 seconds, trending
            sounds, text overlay.
        Bluesky: 300 chars (optimal 200-280); 1-2 hashtags;
            thread support; authentic voice, community
            engagement.
        Mastodon: 500 chars (optimal 300-450); 2-4 hashtags
            (critical for discovery); alt text for images,
            content warnings when appropriate, CamelCase
            hashtags.

    1.3 BRAND VOICE LOADING: Parse brand_voice for tone
    descriptors, language preferences, authenticity markers,
    and avoid patterns. If a messaging_matrix is provided
    (the MESSAGING_MATRIX_OUTPUT_BLOCK from
    RCP-004-002-002), retrieve the phase-specific messaging
    guidance and pillar-specific language patterns rather
    than re-deriving them. Confirm the loaded slot details,
    content direction, platform specs, and brand voice back
    to the user before crafting.


STEP 2: Hook Development

    2.1 HOOK STRATEGY BY PILLAR: Select a hook approach
    matched to the slot's pillar. Strategy banks:
        Educational: curiosity gap, promise of value,
            surprising fact, problem identification, myth
            busting.
        Behind-the-Scenes: transparency opener, process
            reveal, vulnerability, journey share, work in
            progress.
        Community: direct question, poll setup, celebration,
            invitation, shared experience.
        Promotional: news announcement, limited opportunity,
            problem-solution, social proof, direct value.
        Thought Leadership: bold take, industry observation,
            future prediction, contrarian view, pattern
            recognition.

    2.2 HOOK GENERATION: If a hook was provided in the
    calendar entry, use it as the starting point and refine
    for platform specs. Otherwise generate from the selected
    strategy, topic direction, platform character
    constraints, and brand voice. Produce three hook
    variations: v1 direct/clear, v2 curiosity-driven, v3
    emotional/relatable. (Reuse hook components from the
    Message Library's Hook Library when the messaging matrix
    is available.)

    2.3 PLATFORM HOOK OPTIMIZATION: Apply platform rules -
    X/Twitter: hook under 100 chars, no hashtags in the hook
    line, consider thread-opener format. LinkedIn: hook must
    compel the "see more" click, first 2 lines visible,
    professional but intriguing. TikTok: hook = first 1-3
    seconds, text overlay or spoken, immediate pattern
    interrupt. Bluesky/Mastodon: Twitter-like with slightly
    more space and a community tone.

    Present the three hook options with a recommendation and
    rationale, and confirm the selected hook.


STEP 3: Body Content Creation

    3.1 CONTENT STRUCTURE BY POST TYPE: Select a structure
    (format, tone, length, key elements) based on post type:
        educational: Hook - Value Point(s) - Example/Proof -
            CTA; helpful expert tone; medium-long.
        announcement: Hook (News) - What is New - Why It
            Matters - CTA; excited but not hypey; medium.
        engagement: Hook (Question/Poll) - Context -
            Invitation; conversational; short-medium.
        behind-scenes: Hook (Real Talk) - What is Happening
            - Reflection - Invite; authentic, human; medium.
        promotional: Hook (Problem/Solution) - Offer - Proof
            - CTA; confident, value-focused; medium.
        thought-leadership: Hook (Take) - Argument -
            Evidence - Discussion Invite; thoughtful,
            authoritative; medium-long.
        blog-amplification: Hook (Teaser) - Key Insight -
            Link CTA; intriguing; short-medium.

    3.2 BODY GENERATION: Generate the body from the selected
    structure, calendar topic direction, brand voice
    guidelines, platform character limits, and the pillar's
    messaging approach. Apply brand-voice filters
    (professional yet approachable, technically informed
    without intimidating, honest and transparent, avoids
    hype-driven marketing speak).

    3.3 PLATFORM-SPECIFIC FORMATTING:
        X/Twitter: line breaks, 1-2 sentence paragraphs;
            consider thread if > 200 chars; if content > 280
            chars, split into a thread (Tweet 1 hook + core
            message, 2-N supporting points, final tweet CTA).
        LinkedIn: white space between paragraphs, arrows for
            flow, emoji as bullet alternatives, 2-3 sentence
            paragraphs max.
        TikTok: format as a video script with timestamped
            HOOK (0:00-0:03), BODY (0:03-0:45), CTA
            (0:45-0:60) sections.
        Bluesky/Mastodon: Twitter-like; Mastodon include alt
            text placeholders; Bluesky note thread capability.
        Dev.to: article structure (# Title, ## Introduction,
            ## Main Content, ## Conclusion, Tags).

    3.4 BODY OUTPUT: Emit PRIMARY_POST_BODY with the
    complete platform-formatted body, a character count
    (count/limit), and the format (text/thread/script/
    article).


STEP 4: CTA Integration

    4.1 CTA PLACEMENT STRATEGY: Determine placement by
    platform and post type - X/Twitter: final line (short),
    final tweet (threads), or in-body question (engagement).
    LinkedIn: after the final paragraph, separated by a line
    break, often as a question; link goes in the first
    comment, not the post body. TikTok: final 3-5 seconds,
    text overlay plus verbal CTA. Bluesky/Mastodon: final
    line, subtle and community-appropriate. Dev.to: end of
    article plus optional in-content CTAs.

    4.2 CTA REFINEMENT: Retrieve the assigned CTA from the
    calendar entry and rewrite it in the platform's voice
    (e.g. "Sign up for early access" becomes a waitlist link
    on X, "Interested? Link in comments." on LinkedIn, "Link
    in bio to join" on TikTok). Pull from the Message
    Library's CTA Library when the messaging matrix is
    available.

    4.3 CTA OUTPUT: Emit the platform-optimized FINALIZED_CTA
    and its placement (end/inline/first-comment).


STEP 5: Hashtag Strategy

    5.1 HASHTAG SELECTION: Retrieve hashtag_count from the
    platform spec and select by topic relevance, platform
    hashtag culture, brand hashtags, and trending relevance
    (without chasing). Categorize into Primary (1-2, directly
    topic-related), Secondary (1-2, broader category), and
    Brand (0-1, campaign/brand specific). Draw from the
    Message Library's Hashtag Library when available.

    5.2 PLATFORM HASHTAG RULES: X/Twitter 2-3 at end (not in
    threads except the final tweet); LinkedIn 3-5 at the very
    end (popular + niche mix); TikTok 3-5 in caption (one
    trending if relevant, #fyp only if truly relevant);
    Bluesky 1-2 or none; Mastodon 2-4, critical for
    discovery, CamelCase; Dev.to use up to 4 established tags
    (one broad, others specific).

    5.3 HASHTAG OUTPUT: Emit the HASHTAG_SET (Primary,
    Secondary, Brand) with placement.


STEP 6: Variation Creation

    If include_variations is True, create A/B variations
    that test different hooks, CTAs, formats, or angles:
        Variation A (Primary): the complete post from Steps
            2-5.
        Variation B (Hook Test): same body and CTA,
            alternative hook from Step 2.2.
        Variation C (CTA Test): same hook and body,
            alternative CTA (engagement vs. conversion).
    Emit the A/B test variations block with the tested
    dimension labeled per variation. If variations are
    disabled, generate a single version and note that
    include_variations enables A/B options.


STEP 7: Visual Specification

    If include_visual_spec is True, assess the visual need
    (platform requirements, post type, content complexity,
    engagement goals) and recommend a visual:
        X/Twitter: single image / screenshot / simple
            infographic / GIF / none; 1200x675 (1.91:1) or
            1200x1200 (1:1), minimal text, subtle branding.
        LinkedIn: document carousel / professional image /
            infographic / screenshot; carousel 1080x1350
            (4:5), single 1200x627 (1.91:1).
        TikTok: video spec (duration, vertical 9:16, style,
            sound, text overlay, visual hook).
        YouTube: video spec (16:9, thumbnail concept) plus
            thumbnail spec (1280x720, text overlay, face,
            high contrast).
        Bluesky/Mastodon: Twitter-like; Mastodon include alt
            text.
    Emit the visual recommendation (type, format, concept,
    text overlay, alt text, notes). If disabled, skip and
    note that include_visual_spec enables recommendations.


STEP 8: Final Post Output

    8.1 PRIMARY POST ASSEMBLY: Assemble the complete
    copy-paste-ready post with a metadata header (slot ID,
    platform, scheduled date/time, pillar, post type), the
    copy-paste content block, character count (count/limit),
    and the hashtag set. Include the thread breakdown
    (numbered tweets) when in thread format, and the first
    comment block (link + context) for LinkedIn.

    8.2 VARIATIONS SECTION (if enabled): Emit Variation B
    (Hook Test) and Variation C (CTA Test) as complete
    alternative versions, each with its own character count.

    8.3 VISUAL SECTION (if enabled): Emit the visual
    specification (recommended visual, dimensions, concept,
    text overlay, alt text, creation notes).

    8.4 POST COMPLETE SUMMARY: Emit the summary line (slot
    ID, platform, post type, characters/limit, hashtag
    count, variations Yes/No, visual Yes/No, ready-to-publish
    status), then a {PERSONA_NAME} quality check covering
    brand voice, platform optimization, hook strength, CTA
    clarity, and character count, with an engagement
    likelihood (Low/Medium/High) and a brief rationale.
    Close by confirming the post is ready to copy directly
    into the platform.


# =========================================================
# CUSTOM FIELDS SECTION
# =========================================================


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Recipe FAQ
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Q: Should I enable variations for every post?

A: For important posts (milestones, promotions), yes. For
   daily content, single versions are often sufficient.
   Variations are most valuable when you plan to actually
   test them.

Q: How do I handle thread format for X/Twitter?

A: The recipe automatically splits content over 280
   characters into thread format. Each tweet is numbered and
   the CTA goes in the final tweet.

Q: What if the generated hook does not feel right?

A: The recipe provides three hook options. If none fit,
   provide your own hook in the calendar entry and the
   recipe will refine it for the platform.

Q: How accurate are the engagement likelihood estimates?

A: These are directional, based on platform best practices
   and content structure. Actual engagement depends on
   audience, timing, and many other factors.

Q: Can I use this for platforms not listed?

A: The recipe covers the major platforms. For others, adapt
   the closest platform specifications and adjust for the
   specific platform conventions.

Q: Can I use a different persona than the default?

A: Yes. This cookbook bundles Quinn (Multi-Channel Content
   Strategist) as the default for the Content Execution
   section. To override, attach your own custom persona
   file; the recipe uses the {PERSONA_NAME} variable
   throughout.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# How A.I. Reads This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

This recipe generates platform-optimized, copy-paste-ready
social media content from content-calendar slots.

EXECUTION FLOW:

1. POLICY PRE-CHECK: Scan for misleading claims, aggressive
   tactics, or platform policy issues.

2. PERSONA CONTINUITY: Continue with Quinn (Multi-Channel
   Content Strategist) carried from the Content Calendar
   recipe. Load CAMPAIGN_PERSONA if available, else activate
   the bundled Quinn default.

3. CONTEXT LOADING: Parse the calendar entry, load platform
   specifications, load brand voice guidelines (and the
   messaging matrix if provided).

4. HOOK DEVELOPMENT: Generate three hook options based on
   pillar strategy, optimize for platform, select the best
   approach.

5. BODY CONTENT CREATION: Apply structure based on post
   type, generate the body using brand voice, format for
   platform specifications.

6. CTA INTEGRATION: Determine placement strategy, refine the
   CTA for platform voice, finalize the CTA.

7. HASHTAG STRATEGY: Select hashtags based on platform
   rules, categorize by type, determine placement.

8. VARIATION CREATION: Generate A/B test variations for
   hooks and CTAs (if enabled).

9. VISUAL SPECIFICATION: Recommend visual content type,
   dimensions, concept, and alt text (if enabled).

10. FINAL OUTPUT: Assemble the copy-paste-ready post with
    character count verification and a quality check.

DEPENDENCIES:

REQUIRES:
    - Content calendar entry (RCP-004-003-001)
    - Brand voice guidelines

OPTIONAL:
    - Messaging Matrix output (RCP-004-002-002)
    - Channel Strategy output (RCP-004-002-004)

FEEDS INTO:
    - Direct publishing to social platforms
    - Social media scheduling tools
    - Team review workflows
    - Performance Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004)

OUTPUT FORMAT:

Primary output is SOCIAL_POST containing copy-paste-ready
content, character count verification, the hashtag set,
thread format (if applicable), and first-comment content (if
applicable). Optional outputs include A/B variations and
visual specifications.

# Recipe Short Description
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Generates platform-optimized, copy-paste-ready social media
content from calendar slots. Applies brand voice, platform
conventions, and engagement best practices to produce
publishable posts.


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# When To Use This Recipe
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Use this recipe after generating your content calendar
(RCP-004-003-001). Take individual calendar slots and
transform them into actual publishable posts.

IDEAL TIMING:
    - After the content calendar is complete
    - During batch content creation sessions
    - When preparing posts for scheduling
    - Before team review and approval

PREREQUISITES:
    - Content calendar entry (slot details)
    - Brand voice guidelines
    - Platform selection

RELATIONSHIP TO OTHER RECIPES:
    - Follows: Content Calendar Generator (RCP-004-003-001)
    - Parallel: Blog Content Planner (RCP-004-003-003)
    - Precedes: Performance Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004)
    - Output: Direct to social platforms


# ---------------------------------------------------------
# Actual Examples of the Recipe in Use
# ---------------------------------------------------------

Example 1: X/Twitter Educational Post

    Calendar Entry:
        - slot_id: W3-TUE-X-1
        - platform: X/Twitter
        - pillar: Educational
        - topic: "Common mistakes in [your field]"
        - cta: "What do you think?"

    Execution: run with content_calendar_entry (above),
    brand_voice "Professional yet approachable",
    target_platform "X/Twitter", post_type "educational",
    include_variations True, include_visual_spec True.

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces a copy-paste post
    ("Most people get this completely wrong about [topic]..."
    with a mistake, a better approach, and an engagement
    question) at 247/280 chars with hashtags #[topic]
    #[industry]; a Variation B hook test; and a visual spec
    (single image, 1200x675, quote card with the key
    mistake, alt text). Engagement Likelihood: HIGH.


Example 2: LinkedIn Announcement Post

    Calendar Entry:
        - slot_id: W5-MON-LI-1
        - platform: LinkedIn
        - pillar: Promotional
        - topic: "New feature announcement"
        - cta: "Sign up for early access"

    Execution: run with target_platform "LinkedIn",
    post_type "announcement", include_variations True.

    Outcome: {PERSONA_NAME} produces a copy-paste post ("Big
    news. After months of work, we are launching [feature]
    ..." with what it does, why it matters, and "Interested?
    Link in comments.") at 312/3000 chars with hashtags
    #[feature] #[industry] #innovation, plus a first-comment
    block carrying the early-access link. Engagement
    Likelihood: MEDIUM-HIGH.

# =========================================================
# PERSONA CONFIGURATION
# =========================================================

# Default Content Execution Persona - stored in
# PROJECT_VARIABLES for persistence across the Content
# Execution section, carried forward from the Content
# Calendar recipe. Users may attach a custom persona to
# override. This cookbook bundles the tier-less Quinn
# (PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-QUINN-CARD.txt).

CAMPAIGN_PERSONA = {
    "name": "Quinn",
    "title": "Multi-Channel Content Strategist",
    "greeting": "Let us turn calendar slots into posts that
        read native on every platform and still sound like
        your brand.",
    "methodology": "Hook to Body to CTA, optimized
        per platform",
    "formality": 5,
    "explanation_depth": "concise",
    "file_reference": "PERSONA-BRANDING-AND-IDENTITY-QUINN-CARD.txt"
}

PERSONA_NAME = CAMPAIGN_PERSONA["name"]
PERSONA_TITLE = CAMPAIGN_PERSONA["title"]
PERSONA_GREETING = CAMPAIGN_PERSONA["greeting"]
PERSONA_METHODOLOGY = CAMPAIGN_PERSONA["methodology"]


# =========================================================
# RECIPE DEFINITION
# =========================================================

SOCIAL_POST_CREATOR = Recipe(
    recipe_id="RCP-004-003-002-SOCIAL-POST-v3.00a",
    title="Social Post Creator",
    description="""
        Generates platform-optimized, copy-paste-ready
        social media content from calendar slots. Applies
        brand voice, platform conventions, and engagement
        best practices, with A/B variations and visual
        specs. Activates {PERSONA_NAME} (Multi-Channel
        Content Strategist) to guide the work.

# =========================================================
# NOTES SECTION
# =========================================================

Recipe Notes:

1. DEPENDENCY: This recipe requires calendar slots from the
   Content Calendar recipe (RCP-004-003-001) and brand voice
   guidelines. Optional inputs from the Messaging Matrix
   (RCP-004-002-002) and Channel Strategy (RCP-004-002-004)
   enhance output quality.

2. PLATFORM SPECIFICATIONS: Full specs are included for
   X/Twitter (280 chars, 2-3 hashtags), LinkedIn (3000
   chars, 3-5 hashtags), YouTube (titles/descriptions/
   thumbnails), TikTok (video scripts, 3-5 hashtags),
   Bluesky (300 chars, 1-2 hashtags), Mastodon (500 chars,
   2-4 hashtags, alt text), Dev.to (markdown articles, 4
   tags), and GitHub (README, release notes).

3. POST TYPES: Eight post structures are supported -
   announcement, educational, engagement, behind-scenes,
   promotional, thought-leadership, community, and
   blog-amplification.

4. HOOK STRATEGIES: Five pillar-specific hook banks -
   Educational, Behind-Scenes, Community, Promotional, and
   Thought Leadership.

5. VARIATIONS: When enabled, generates three versions -
   Variation A (primary baseline), Variation B (different
   hook), and Variation C (different CTA).

6. VISUAL SPECIFICATIONS: Platform-specific guidance -
   dimensions for images and video, thumbnail concepts for
   YouTube, and alt text suggestions for accessibility.

7. BATCH MODE: Process multiple calendar slots at once for
   efficient content creation sessions.

8. DOWNSTREAM: Posts can be published directly or tracked
   through the Performance Analyzer (RCP-004-003-004).


# =========================================================
# METADATA
# =========================================================

    - {PERSONA_NAME} - Active persona name (default Quinn)
    - {PERSONA_TITLE} - Active persona title
    - {PERSONA_GREETING} - Persona greeting text
    - {PERSONA_METHODOLOGY} - Persona methodology approach
    - {target_platform} - Platform being created for
    - {pillar} - Content pillar from the calendar slot
    - {slot_id} - Calendar slot identifier
    - {date} - Publication date of the slot

New Version Number: 3.00a

    "lessons_learned_applied" (LL-004..023: line width,
    indentation, plaintext-only, CAT-005 separation) are
    build-time conventions tracked in the cookbook build log,
    NOT shipped in the distributed recipe. Recipe-level
    CONTENT lessons now live in the Actual Recipe Code under
    ai_to_ai_communication.lessons_learned.

Version changes: see the Version History section above
    (promoted from the former metadata changelog block).

# Status: Ready for Validation

# RE-HOME NOTE (SP11 H025, Richard-approved Option 1): this
# recipe's content is content-execution blog planning, so it
# is placed in the Content Execution section (004-003) under
# Quinn, the bundled section SME. Source internal id
# RCP-005-002-003 (CAT-005 Campaign Planning) normalized to
